الفعل واجب، فلا اختيار للعبد فيه أصلاً، فهو اضطراري (فلا يكون حسناً ولا قبيحاً) أصلاً (عقلاً إجماعاً) لأن الاضطراري لا يوصف بهما، وهذا التبيان غير متوقف على إبطال الأولوية الغير البالغة حد الوجوب، بخلاف ما في «المختصر حيث قال : استدل أن فعل العبد غير مختار فلا يكون حسناً ولا قبيحاً لذاته إجماعاً، لأنه إن كان لازماً فواضح ، وإن كان جائزاً، فإن افتقر إلى مرجح عاد التقسيم وإلا فهو اتفاقي، فإنه متوقف على إبطالها، مع أن فيه شق الاتفاقي زائد لا حاجة إليه ولذلك قال وهذا حسن وأخصر مما في «المختصر) وقد يقال : إن استحالة ترجيح المرجوح ممنوع بل يجوز أن يكون الراجح أوّلي غير واجب والعدم مرجوحاً ممكناً فحينئذ ترجيح المرجوح غير أوّلي لا أنه مستحيل فحينئذ لا كفاية وهذا مكابرة فإن استحالته بين أوّلي غني عن البيان (والجواب ) أن غاية ما لزم من البيان وجوب الفعل من المرجح ويجوز أن يكون هو الاختيار و أن الوجوب بالاختيار لا يوجب الاضطرار) فإنه عدم تعلق الاختيار وههنا قد تعلق به الاختيار (ضرورة الفرق بين حركتي الاختيار والرعشة) كون كليهما واجبين عن مرجحيهما والأول اختياري لا الثاني على أنه مع منقوض بفعل الباري تعالى فإن فعله إن ترجح فقد وجب وإلا استحال صدوره. قيل تفصيل الدليل أنه لو صدر الفعل من العبد بالإرادة، فالإرداة لا تصدر بإرادة أخرى وهي بأخرى وإلاّ لزم التسلسل في المبدأ وأيضاً لا نجد من أنفسنا عند صدور الفعل إلا إرادة واحدة فإذن علة الإرداة غير إرادة المريد فإما أن يجب بخلق الله تعالى أو بفعل المريد لكن من غير إرادة وشعور وعلى التقديرين فالعبد في تحقق الإرادة مضطر والفعل واجب عند الإرادة فيكون اضطرارياً إذ الاختياري ما يصح فعله وتركه وبعبارة أخرى إن تحقق جميع ما يتوقف عليه الفعل فقد وجب ويلزم الاضطرار إذ لا يصح حينئذ تركه وإلا لزم الترجيح من غير مرجح وعند بلوغ التقرير إلى هذا لا يتمشى الجواب المذكور بل لا يمكن نعم يرد النقض بفعل الباري جل مجده إلا أن يقال بالإرادة المشوبة بالجبر ولا يجترى عليه مسلم ثم قال هذا القائل ويشكل حينئذ بثلاثة أمور الأول أن لا يكون الحسن والقبح في فعلي العبد والباري جل مجده عقليين الثاني أن لا يكون الباري جل مجده مختاراً صرفاً في فعله بل كان اختياره مشوباً بالجبر . الثالث يلزم كون العبد مضطراً في الفعل فيشكل أمر المعاد من الثواب والعقاب ثم قال يمكن دفع الأول والثالث بالتزام أن الاختيار المشوب بالاضطرار كاف في الحسن والقبح وكذا في إيصال الثواب والعقاب وأنت تعلم أن القول بتجويز اتصاف الاضطراري بالحسن والقبح خرق الإجماع والإشكال في الثواب والعقاب ليس لأن الفعل غير مختار أو مختار بل لأن العبد يتأتى له العذر بأن الفعل قد وجب فلا أستطيع أن أتحرز عنه فلم يكن الله الحجة البالغة هذا خلف وهو غير مندفع بقوله وقال وأجابوا عن الثاني بتجويز التخلف إذ غاية ما يلزم فيه الترجيح من غير مرجح وهو غير ممتنع، بل الرجحان من غير مرجح أو الوجود من غير موجد، ثم رده بإثبات استحالة التخلف وهكذا وقع القيل والقال، ولم تنكشف حقيقة الحال، وأجاب المصنف «الحاشية» أن هذا غير تام على رأي الأشعري، فإنه يكتفي بوجود قدرة متوهمة في توجه التكليف هذا، وأنت تعلم أنه يكفي في توجه التكليف الشرعي عنده لا الحسن العقلي، بل الإجماع وقع على أن الاضطراري لا يوصف بالحسن والقبح العقليين، وتحقيق المقام على ما استفاده هذا العبد من إشارات الكرام وتقرر عليه رأيه في تحقيق المرام، أن عند إرادة العبد
The second article on rulings in essence, as is apparent or by accidents, so it was assumed and the orientation to the house prevented good orientation, so it became bad accidentally, so ponder and be fair, that this explanation is not complete nor does it stand against the Jubba'iyya nor against us, even if it stands against the majority of the Mu'tazila, for it only follows the invalidity of both being required by the essence absolutely, and we do not say that, but we only say with absolute generality, so there is no need to undertake the answer. And they said: that it is not from secondly: (If each of them were essential, then two contradictories would combine in the example 'I will certainly lie tomorrow', for its truth necessitates lying) tomorrow which is the reported about (and vice versa), i.e., its falsehood necessitates the absence of lying tomorrow, so its truth entails the lie that is evil by essence, and its falsehood entails its absence which is good by essence, and the entailer has the ruling of the consequent) so its truth would be evil while being good, and its falsehood would be good while being evil. And it does not turn against them that it would follow upon them that its truth would be good legally and evil legally, and they are opposites, so where is escape? Because they can say that it is permissible that one of them be nullified, for it is by the Maker's making, contrary to the Mu'tazila, for they say that they are by the essence of the act, so reflect on that. (And perhaps that is prevented, i.e., that the ruling of the entailer is the same as the ruling of the entailment by essence. Do you not see that that which leads to evil is not evil by essence? How is it that the coming of the messenger causes the destruction of many people along with great good greater?) (Shaykh Abu Ali said in al-Isharat: Evil enters into decree accidentally) for the divine predetermination first and essentially attaches to good, but it was dependent on the existence of a little evil, the way of the wise is to leave much good for the sake of a little evil, so He ordained evil and brought it into existence. This, then, it is not hidden from one educated in legal etiquettes that the correct is to leave supporting with the words of Ibn Sina, for he is not among the men of this discussion. I say: this answer guides you to the commitment mentioned previously) that they are, as they are essentially, they are accidentally, for the goodness of the entailer, even if it does not necessitate the ruling of the consequent essentially, it necessitates it accidentally absolutely, and likewise its evil necessitates its evil accidentally (so understand) for there is no concealment in it. And it may be said in presenting the proof that the truth of 'I will certainly lie tomorrow' is the very realization of its referent which is the lie tomorrow, and it is evil by essence according to them, so the truth is evil while being good, so then this answer does not apply at all. And in it: we do not accept that truth is the very realization of the referent, but rather the correspondence to the actual referent, so the actuality of the referent is necessary for it, not that it is it. And if it is accepted, then 'I will certainly lie tomorrow' has two considerations: the consideration that it is the realization of the referent of the report, and the consideration that its referent is not realized. We say: we say that by the first consideration it is good by essence, and by the second consideration it is evil, so no harm. And this is apparent to us, but according to them there is room for reflection due to their not holding that obligation and prohibition can combine in one thing even by two considerations. (And) they said (thirdly: The act of the servant is compelled, for the act is possible, and the possible, as long as its existence is not preponderant over its non-existence, it does not exist) so at the time of existence, existence is preponderant and non-existence is deficient, and the preponderance of the deficient is impossible, so as long as it is not necessary it does not exist) so non-existence at the time of the preponderance of existence is impossible, so the existence of the act is necessary, so there is no choice for the servant in it at all, so it is compelled (so it is not good nor evil) at all (rationally by consensus) because the compelled is not described by them. And this explanation does not depend on invalidating the preference that does not reach the level of necessity, contrary to what is in al-Mukhtasar where he said: he argued that the act of the servant is not chosen, so it is not good nor evil by essence by consensus, because if it is necessary it is obvious, and if it is possible, then if it needs a preponderant, the division returns, otherwise it is accidental, for it depends on its invalidation, while in it there is the part of the accidental which is extra and not needed, and therefore he said: and this is good and shorter than what is in al-Mukhtasar). And it may be said: the impossibility of the preponderance of the deficient is denied; rather it is permissible that the preponderant is primary not necessary, and the non-existence is deficient possible, so then the preponderance of the deficient is not primary, not that it is impossible, so then there is no sufficiency. And this is obstinacy, for its impossibility is primary, in no need of explanation. (And the answer) is that the utmost that follows from the explanation is the necessity of the act from the preponderant, and it is permissible that it is choice, and that necessity by choice does not necessitate compulsion) for it is the absence of the attachment of choice, and here choice has attached to it (by necessity of the difference between the two movements of choice and tremor) as both are necessary from their preponderants, the first is voluntary not the second. Besides, it is refuted by the act of Allah Most High, for His act, if it preponderates, it becomes necessary, otherwise its occurrence is impossible. It was said: the detailed argument is that if the act issues from the servant by will, then will does not issue by another will, and it is by another, otherwise there would be regress in the beginning, and also we do not find from ourselves at the occurrence of the act except one will, so then the cause of the will is other than the will of the willing, so either it must be by the creation of Allah Most High or by the act of the willing but without will and consciousness, and in both cases, the servant in the realization of the will is compelled, and the act is necessary at the time of will, so it becomes compulsory, for the voluntary is that whose doing and leaving is possible. In other words, if everything that the act depends on has been realized, then it is necessary, and compulsion follows, for then its leaving is not correct, otherwise there would be preponderance without a preponderant. And when the exposition reaches this point, the aforementioned answer does not work; rather it is not possible. Yes, the refutation by the act of Allah Most High is raised, except that it is said by will mixed with compulsion, and no Muslim dares to do that. Then this speaker said: and it is problematic then with three matters: first, that good and evil would not be rational in the acts of the servant and Allah Most High; second, that Allah Most High would not be purely free in His act, but His choice would be mixed with compulsion; third, it leads to the servant being compelled in the act, so the matter of resurrection of reward and punishment becomes problematic. Then he said: the first and third can be repelled by accepting that choice mixed with compulsion is sufficient for good and evil, and likewise for delivering reward and punishment. And you know that saying that it is permissible to describe the compelled with good and evil breaks consensus. And the problem regarding reward and punishment is not because the act is not chosen or is chosen, but because the servant gets the excuse that the act was necessary so I cannot avoid it, so Allah would not have the conclusive argument. This is contrary to what is expected and is not repelled by his statement. And they answered the second by allowing delay, for the utmost that follows is preponderance without a preponderant, and it is not impossible; rather preponderance without a preponderant or existence without a cause is existing. Then he refuted it by proving the impossibility of delay, and thus went the talk and talk, and the reality of the matter was not disclosed. And the author of al-Hashiya answered that this is not complete according to the opinion of al-Ash'ari, for he is satisfied with the existence of an imagined ability in directing the obligation. And you know that that is sufficient in directing the legal obligation according to him, not rational good, rather consensus is that the compelled is not described by rational good and evil. And the verification of the station, according to what this servant has used from the indications of the noble ones and his opinion has settled in achieving the goal, that at the will of the servant
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning the nature of good and evil (husn wa qubh) and the issue of human free will versus determinism. It presents two key objections (ثانياً and ثالثاً) raised by opponents—likely Mu'tazila or philosophers—against the Hanafi/Ash'ari position that moral values are known by reason. The first objection argues that if good and evil were essential (ذاتي) to actions, contradictory qualities would combine in statements like 'I will certainly lie tomorrow': both truth and falsehood would be simultaneously good and evil. The author responds by distinguishing between essential and accidental (بالعرض) attributions, noting that the ruling of the entailer is not necessarily the same as the ruling of the entailment in essence, but can be accidental. He also references Abu Ali's view that evil enters into divine decree accidentally. The second objection claims that human actions are compelled (اضطراري) because every possible act requires a preponderant cause, making its existence necessary; hence no choice remains, and actions cannot be described as good or evil rationally by consensus. The response argues that the necessity comes from choice, which does not negate voluntariness, distinguishing between voluntary movement and involuntary tremor. It also invokes the act of Allah to refute the determinist chain. The passage then critiques a further elaboration, showing that if all prerequisites for an act are fulfilled, it is necessary, leading to compulsion—this is problematic for reward and punishment. The author notes that the Ash'ari position suffices for legal obligation without requiring rational good/evil, and that consensus remains that the compelled is not described rationally. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating ongoing analysis.

Key Terms
الذاتي (al-dhātī): Essential attribute that inheres in the essence of a thing.
بالعرض (bi-l-ʿaraḍ): Accidental attribute applied due to external factors.
الملزوم (al-malzūm): The entailer; the antecedent in a logical implication.
اللازم (al-lāzim): The entailment; the consequent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in the passage, why does the statement 'I will certainly lie tomorrow' not lead to a logical contradiction?
A) Because truth and falsehood are not subject to moral evaluation.
B) Because the act can be good in one respect and evil in another, essentially and accidentally.
C) Because the Mu'tazila argument relies on invalid premises.
D) Because the example is about legal rulings, not rational ones.

Key Takeaway
Good and evil can be accidental without being essential; this distinction resolves apparent logical contradictions in moral evaluation.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
15 min
Determinism vs Free Will: The Compulsion Argument in Human Actions
Hanafi response to the Mu'tazili determinism argument against rational good/evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Mu'tazili deterministic argument from necessity and state the Hanafi/Ash'ari response that necessity through choice does not negate moral responsibility.

Core Idea
Necessity from choice is not compulsion—the servant's act is voluntary despite causal necessity.

If every possible act requires a preponderant cause to exist, then once all conditions are met, the act is necessary and the agent has no real choice. The Mu'tazila used this to argue that human actions are compelled, and therefore cannot be rationally good or evil. In this lesson, we dissect their argument and the Hanafi response: the necessity comes from the agent's own choice (ikhtiyār), which is fundamentally different from involuntary compulsion (iḍṭirār). We also examine the refutation by analogy to divine acts and the complications that arise.

Guided Path
1
State the Mu'tazili determinist argument
The opponent argues: the act of the servant is possible (mumkin). A possible act cannot exist unless its existence becomes preponderant (rājiḥ) over non-existence. Once preponderant, existence is necessary, non-existence impossible. Hence the act is necessary, not free. Therefore it is compelled (iḍṭirārī) and cannot be described as good or evil rationally.
The argument relies on the principle of sufficient reason: no possible thing occurs without a preponderant cause.
2
Identify the Hanafi response: necessity through choice
The response concedes that the act is necessary from its preponderant cause, but allows that cause to be the servant's own choice (ikhtiyār). Necessity by choice does not equal compulsion; the agent acts voluntarily because the choice is his.
The example of voluntary movement vs. tremor (ikhtilāj) shows both are necessary from their causes, but only one is chosen.
3
Examine the refutation by divine acts
The same argument would apply to Allah's acts: if His act requires a preponderant, it becomes necessary, compromising His free will. Since Muslims affirm that Allah is free, the argument is overgeneralized.
The opponent may respond by claiming that Allah's will is mixed with compulsion (jabr), but that is unacceptable.
4
Analyze the detailed extension of the argument
A deeper version: the will (irāda) itself cannot be caused by another will (to avoid regress), so the cause of the will is either Allah's creation or an unconscious act. In both, the servant is compelled in willing. Then the act is necessary given the will, so overall compelled.
The text notes that at this level the earlier answer fails, and the only refutation is by analogy to Allah's act or by accepting choice mixed with compulsion.
5
Conclude with the consensus on compelled acts
Despite the difficulties, the passage emphasizes consensus (ijmāʿ) that the compelled (muḍṭarr) is not described by rational good/evil. The Ash'ari position suffices for legal obligation (taklīf sharʿī) even if rational evaluation is limited.
The problem of reward/punishment persists because the servant could claim inability to avoid the act. The text acknowledges this as an unresolved difficulty.

المقالة الثانية في الأحكام بالذات، كما هو الظاهر أو بالعوارض، فافترض وكان التوجه إلى البيت مانعاً التوجه الحسن فصار قبيحاً بالعرض فتدبر وأنصف على أنه لا يتم هذا البيان ولا ينتهض على الجبائية ولا علينا الجواب يرشدك إلى الالتزام المذكور سابقاً) من أنهما كما يكونان بالذات يكونان بالغير، فإن حسن الملزوم وإن لم يكن مستلزماً لحكم اللازم بالذات لكنه مستلزم له بالعرض البتة، وكذا قبحه يستلزم قبحه بالعرض (فافهم) فإنه لا سترة فيه، وقد يقال في تقرير الدليل أن صدق لأكذبن غداً هو نفس تحقق مصداقه الذي هو الكذب في الغد وهو قبيح بالذات عندهم فالصدق قبيح مع كونه حسناً، فحينئذ لا يتوجه هذا الجواب أصلاً، وفيه أنا لا نسلم أن الصدق نفس تحقق المصداق، بل المطابقة للمصداق الواقعي، فواقعية المصداق لازمة له لا أنه هي، ولو سلم فلأكذبن الغد اعتباران اعتبار أنه تحقق مصداق الخبر، واعتبار أن مصداقه غير متحقق قلنا إن نقول أنه بالاعتبار الأوّل حسن بالذات، وبالاعتبار الثاني قبيح، فلا ضير وهذا عندنا ظاهر، وأما عندهم فللتأمل فيه مجال لعدم قولهم باجتماع الوجوب والحرمة في شيء ما ولو باعتبارين (و) قالوا (ثالثاً : إن فعل العبد اضطراري، فإن الفعل ممكن والممكن ما لم يترجح وجوده على عدمه لا يوجد) فحين الوجود يكون الوجود راجحاً والعدم مرجوحاً وترجح المرجوح محال، فما لم يجب لم يوجد) فالعدم حال ترجيح الوجود محال، فوجود الفعل واجب، فلا اختيار للعبد فيه أصلاً، فهو اضطراري (فلا يكون حسناً ولا قبيحاً) أصلاً (عقلاً إجماعاً) لأن الاضطراري لا يوصف بهما، وهذا التبيان غير متوقف على إبطال الأولوية الغير البالغة حد الوجوب، بخلاف ما في «المختصر حيث قال : استدل أن فعل العبد غير مختار فلا يكون حسناً ولا قبيحاً لذاته إجماعاً، لأنه إن كان لازماً فواضح ، وإن كان جائزاً، فإن افتقر إلى مرجح عاد التقسيم وإلا فهو اتفاقي، فإنه متوقف على إبطالها، مع أن فيه شق الاتفاقي زائد لا حاجة إليه ولذلك قال وهذا حسن وأخصر مما في «المختصر) وقد يقال : إن استحالة ترجيح المرجوح ممنوع بل يجوز أن يكون الراجح أوّلي غير واجب والعدم مرجوحاً ممكناً فحينئذ ترجيح المرجوح غير أوّلي لا أنه مستحيل فحينئذ لا كفاية وهذا مكابرة فإن استحالته بين أوّلي غني عن البيان (والجواب ) أن غاية ما لزم من البيان وجوب الفعل من المرجح ويجوز أن يكون هو الاختيار و أن الوجوب بالاختيار لا يوجب الاضطرار) فإنه عدم تعلق الاختيار وههنا قد تعلق به الاختيار (ضرورة الفرق بين حركتي الاختيار والرعشة) كون كليهما واجبين عن مرجحيهما والأول اختياري لا الثاني على أنه مع منقوض بفعل الباري تعالى فإن فعله إن ترجح فقد وجب وإلا استحال صدوره. قيل تفصيل الدليل أنه لو صدر الفعل من العبد بالإرادة، فالإرداة لا تصدر بإرادة أخرى وهي بأخرى وإلاّ لزم التسلسل في المبدأ وأيضاً لا نجد من أنفسنا عند صدور الفعل إلا إرادة واحدة فإذن علة الإرداة غير إرادة المريد فإما أن يجب بخلق الله تعالى أو بفعل المريد لكن من غير إرادة وشعور وعلى التقديرين فالعبد في تحقق الإرادة مضطر والفعل واجب عند الإرادة فيكون اضطرارياً إذ الاختياري ما يصح فعله وتركه وبعبارة أخرى إن تحقق جميع ما يتوقف عليه الفعل فقد وجب ويلزم الاضطرار إذ لا يصح حينئذ تركه وإلا لزم الترجيح من غير مرجح وعند بلوغ التقرير إلى هذا لا يتمشى الجواب المذكور بل لا يمكن نعم يرد النقض بفعل الباري جل مجده إلا أن يقال بالإرادة المشوبة بالجبر ولا يجترى عليه مسلم ثم قال هذا القائل ويشكل حينئذ بثلاثة أمور الأول أن لا يكون الحسن والقبح في فعلي العبد والباري جل مجده عقليين الثاني أن لا يكون الباري جل مجده مختاراً صرفاً في فعله بل كان اختياره مشوباً بالجبر . الثالث يلزم كون العبد مضطراً في الفعل فيشكل أمر المعاد من الثواب والعقاب ثم قال يمكن دفع الأول والثالث بالتزام أن الاختيار المشوب بالاضطرار كاف في الحسن والقبح وكذا في إيصال الثواب والعقاب وأنت تعلم أن القول بتجويز اتصاف الاضطراري بالحسن والقبح خرق الإجماع والإشكال في الثواب والعقاب ليس لأن الفعل غير مختار أو مختار بل لأن العبد يتأتى له العذر بأن الفعل قد وجب فلا أستطيع أن أتحرز عنه فلم يكن الله الحجة البالغة هذا خلف وهو غير مندفع بقوله وقال وأجابوا عن الثاني بتجويز التخلف إذ غاية ما يلزم فيه الترجيح من غير مرجح وهو غير ممتنع، بل الرجحان من غير مرجح أو الوجود من غير موجد، ثم رده بإثبات استحالة التخلف وهكذا وقع القيل والقال، ولم تنكشف حقيقة الحال، وأجاب المصنف «الحاشية» أن هذا غير تام على رأي الأشعري، فإنه يكتفي بوجود قدرة متوهمة في توجه التكليف هذا، وأنت تعلم أنه يكفي في توجه التكليف الشرعي عنده لا الحسن العقلي، بل الإجماع وقع على أن الاضطراري لا يوصف بالحسن والقبح العقليين، وتحقيق المقام على ما استفاده هذا العبد من إشارات الكرام وتقرر عليه رأيه في تحقيق المرام، أن عند إرادة العبد
The second article on rulings in essence, as is apparent or by accidents, so it was assumed and the orientation to the house prevented good orientation, so it became bad accidentally, so ponder and be fair, that this explanation is not complete nor does it stand against the Jubba'iyya nor against us, even if it stands against the majority of the Mu'tazila, for it only follows the invalidity of both being required by the essence absolutely, and we do not say that, but we only say with absolute generality, so there is no need to undertake the answer. And they said: that it is not from secondly: (If each of them were essential, then two contradictories would combine in the example 'I will certainly lie tomorrow', for its truth necessitates lying) tomorrow which is the reported about (and vice versa), i.e., its falsehood necessitates the absence of lying tomorrow, so its truth entails the lie that is evil by essence, and its falsehood entails its absence which is good by essence, and the entailer has the ruling of the consequent) so its truth would be evil while being good, and its falsehood would be good while being evil. And it does not turn against them that it would follow upon them that its truth would be good legally and evil legally, and they are opposites, so where is escape? Because they can say that it is permissible that one of them be nullified, for it is by the Maker's making, contrary to the Mu'tazila, for they say that they are by the essence of the act, so reflect on that. (And perhaps that is prevented, i.e., that the ruling of the entailer is the same as the ruling of the entailment by essence. Do you not see that that which leads to evil is not evil by essence? How is it that the coming of the messenger causes the destruction of many people along with great good greater?) (Shaykh Abu Ali said in al-Isharat: Evil enters into decree accidentally) for the divine predetermination first and essentially attaches to good, but it was dependent on the existence of a little evil, the way of the wise is to leave much good for the sake of a little evil, so He ordained evil and brought it into existence. This, then, it is not hidden from one educated in legal etiquettes that the correct is to leave supporting with the words of Ibn Sina, for he is not among the men of this discussion. I say: this answer guides you to the commitment mentioned previously) that they are, as they are essentially, they are accidentally, for the goodness of the entailer, even if it does not necessitate the ruling of the consequent essentially, it necessitates it accidentally absolutely, and likewise its evil necessitates its evil accidentally (so understand) for there is no concealment in it. And it may be said in presenting the proof that the truth of 'I will certainly lie tomorrow' is the very realization of its referent which is the lie tomorrow, and it is evil by essence according to them, so the truth is evil while being good, so then this answer does not apply at all. And in it: we do not accept that truth is the very realization of the referent, but rather the correspondence to the actual referent, so the actuality of the referent is necessary for it, not that it is it. And if it is accepted, then 'I will certainly lie tomorrow' has two considerations: the consideration that it is the realization of the referent of the report, and the consideration that its referent is not realized. We say: we say that by the first consideration it is good by essence, and by the second consideration it is evil, so no harm. And this is apparent to us, but according to them there is room for reflection due to their not holding that obligation and prohibition can combine in one thing even by two considerations. (And) they said (thirdly: The act of the servant is compelled, for the act is possible, and the possible, as long as its existence is not preponderant over its non-existence, it does not exist) so at the time of existence, existence is preponderant and non-existence is deficient, and the preponderance of the deficient is impossible, so as long as it is not necessary it does not exist) so non-existence at the time of the preponderance of existence is impossible, so the existence of the act is necessary, so there is no choice for the servant in it at all, so it is compelled (so it is not good nor evil) at all (rationally by consensus) because the compelled is not described by them. And this explanation does not depend on invalidating the preference that does not reach the level of necessity, contrary to what is in al-Mukhtasar where he said: he argued that the act of the servant is not chosen, so it is not good nor evil by essence by consensus, because if it is necessary it is obvious, and if it is possible, then if it needs a preponderant, the division returns, otherwise it is accidental, for it depends on its invalidation, while in it there is the part of the accidental which is extra and not needed, and therefore he said: and this is good and shorter than what is in al-Mukhtasar). And it may be said: the impossibility of the preponderance of the deficient is denied; rather it is permissible that the preponderant is primary not necessary, and the non-existence is deficient possible, so then the preponderance of the deficient is not primary, not that it is impossible, so then there is no sufficiency. And this is obstinacy, for its impossibility is primary, in no need of explanation. (And the answer) is that the utmost that follows from the explanation is the necessity of the act from the preponderant, and it is permissible that it is choice, and that necessity by choice does not necessitate compulsion) for it is the absence of the attachment of choice, and here choice has attached to it (by necessity of the difference between the two movements of choice and tremor) as both are necessary from their preponderants, the first is voluntary not the second. Besides, it is refuted by the act of Allah Most High, for His act, if it preponderates, it becomes necessary, otherwise its occurrence is impossible. It was said: the detailed argument is that if the act issues from the servant by will, then will does not issue by another will, and it is by another, otherwise there would be regress in the beginning, and also we do not find from ourselves at the occurrence of the act except one will, so then the cause of the will is other than the will of the willing, so either it must be by the creation of Allah Most High or by the act of the willing but without will and consciousness, and in both cases, the servant in the realization of the will is compelled, and the act is necessary at the time of will, so it becomes compulsory, for the voluntary is that whose doing and leaving is possible. In other words, if everything that the act depends on has been realized, then it is necessary, and compulsion follows, for then its leaving is not correct, otherwise there would be preponderance without a preponderant. And when the exposition reaches this point, the aforementioned answer does not work; rather it is not possible. Yes, the refutation by the act of Allah Most High is raised, except that it is said by will mixed with compulsion, and no Muslim dares to do that. Then this speaker said: and it is problematic then with three matters: first, that good and evil would not be rational in the acts of the servant and Allah Most High; second, that Allah Most High would not be purely free in His act, but His choice would be mixed with compulsion; third, it leads to the servant being compelled in the act, so the matter of resurrection of reward and punishment becomes problematic. Then he said: the first and third can be repelled by accepting that choice mixed with compulsion is sufficient for good and evil, and likewise for delivering reward and punishment. And you know that saying that it is permissible to describe the compelled with good and evil breaks consensus. And the problem regarding reward and punishment is not because the act is not chosen or is chosen, but because the servant gets the excuse that the act was necessary so I cannot avoid it, so Allah would not have the conclusive argument. This is contrary to what is expected and is not repelled by his statement. And they answered the second by allowing delay, for the utmost that follows is preponderance without a preponderant, and it is not impossible; rather preponderance without a preponderant or existence without a cause is existing. Then he refuted it by proving the impossibility of delay, and thus went the talk and talk, and the reality of the matter was not disclosed. And the author of al-Hashiya answered that this is not complete according to the opinion of al-Ash'ari, for he is satisfied with the existence of an imagined ability in directing the obligation. And you know that that is sufficient in directing the legal obligation according to him, not rational good, rather consensus is that the compelled is not described by rational good and evil. And the verification of the station, according to what this servant has used from the indications of the noble ones and his opinion has settled in achieving the goal, that at the will of the servant
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning the nature of good and evil (husn wa qubh) and the issue of human free will versus determinism. It presents two key objections (ثانياً and ثالثاً) raised by opponents—likely Mu'tazila or philosophers—against the Hanafi/Ash'ari position that moral values are known by reason. The first objection argues that if good and evil were essential (ذاتي) to actions, contradictory qualities would combine in statements like 'I will certainly lie tomorrow': both truth and falsehood would be simultaneously good and evil. The author responds by distinguishing between essential and accidental (بالعرض) attributions, noting that the ruling of the entailer is not necessarily the same as the ruling of the entailment in essence, but can be accidental. He also references Abu Ali's view that evil enters into divine decree accidentally. The second objection claims that human actions are compelled (اضطراري) because every possible act requires a preponderant cause, making its existence necessary; hence no choice remains, and actions cannot be described as good or evil rationally by consensus. The response argues that the necessity comes from choice, which does not negate voluntariness, distinguishing between voluntary movement and involuntary tremor. It also invokes the act of Allah to refute the determinist chain. The passage then critiques a further elaboration, showing that if all prerequisites for an act are fulfilled, it is necessary, leading to compulsion—this is problematic for reward and punishment. The author notes that the Ash'ari position suffices for legal obligation without requiring rational good/evil, and that consensus remains that the compelled is not described rationally. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating ongoing analysis.

Key Terms
الاضطرار (al-iḍṭirār): Compulsion; the state of an action where the agent has no choice.
الاختيار (al-ikhtiyār): Choice; the voluntary decision to perform an act.
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Preponderance; making one possibility outweigh another.
الرعشة (al-raʿsha): Tremor; involuntary movement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why does the necessity of the act (after conditions are met) not make it compelled?
A) Because the act is still possible to avoid.
B) Because the necessity comes from the servant's own choice.
C) Because divine acts are also necessary, yet Allah is free.
D) Because rational good/evil do not depend on free will.

Key Takeaway
Necessity from voluntary choice does not constitute compulsion; human actions remain morally evaluable because they are chosen.

Module 11 · Lesson 9

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Human Choice and Moral Attribution of Actions
Dispute on whether human actions are compelled or chosen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Ash'ari/Hanafi position on human choice (ikhtiyār) and necessity (wujūb), evaluate the Mu'tazili objection that necessitated acts cannot be morally evaluated, and apply the definition of ikhtiyār to distinguish voluntary from involuntary acts.

Core Idea
Choice is directing power and will to an act; necessity through choice does not cancel moral responsibility.

This lesson tackles a foundational theological-legal dispute: if God creates all actions, how can humans be truly responsible and their acts be evaluated as good or bad? The Mu'tazila argue that a necessitated act is coerced and thus exempt from rational moral judgment. The Ash'ari school, adopted by the Hanafi tradition in usul, responds by defining choice (ikhtiyār) as the servant's direction of God-given power and will toward the act. The act becomes necessary only after this choice is made, preserving human accountability and the possibility of moral evaluation. We will trace the arguments and counter-arguments, and ultimately see how the Hanafi position upholds both divine omnipotence and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
State the core dispute
Identify the two opposing positions: the Mu'tazili claim that any act necessitated by a preponderant (murajjih) is coerced and cannot be described as good or bad, versus the Ash'ari claim that the act is chosen because choice is the attachment of will and power, and necessity arises from the choice itself.
The dispute hinges on the definition of 'choice' (ikhtiyār).
2
Analyze the key definition of ikhtiyār
The passage defines ikhtiyār as 'directing power and will to the act' (ṣarf al-qudrah wa al-irādah ilā al-fiʿl). Note that this definition does not require the act to be uncaused; it only requires the agent's volitional engagement.
This definition resolves the apparent conflict between necessity and choice.
3
Examine the distinction between voluntary and involuntary movements
The author contrasts a voluntary movement (e.g., raising one's hand) with an involuntary tremor. Both are necessitated by their causes, but only the former has choice attached to it, making it morally evaluable. This distinction is crucial for answering the objection.
The difference lies in the presence of choice, not in the absence of causation.
4
Follow the three objections and their counter-arguments
The Mu'tazili raises three problems: (1) loss of rational good/evil, (2) God's action would also be necessary and thus not purely free, (3) the servant would have an excuse, undermining reward and punishment. Track how the Ash'ari response handles each: (1) rational good/evil only applies to chosen acts, which this is; (2) God's action is according to wisdom and is voluntary in a different sense; (3) the servant's choice suffices for accountability.
The Ash'ari solution involves the concept of 'supposed power' (qudrah mutawahhamah) sufficient for legal obligation, even if the act is necessitated.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi/Ash'ari resolution via kasb
The author explains that when the servant directs his choice, he becomes prepared; by God's habit (jārī al-ʿādah), God creates the act in him. This is the doctrine of kasb (acquisition). The servant's act is attributed to him because he directed the choice, even though God creates the act. Thus, the act is both chosen and necessitated, without contradiction.
This resolves the problem of human responsibility while preserving divine omnipotence.

استدل أن فعل العبد غير مختار فلا يكون حسناً ولا قبيحاً لذاته إجماعاً، لأنه إن كان لازماً فواضح ، وإن كان جائزاً، فإن افتقر إلى مرجح عاد التقسيم وإلا فهو اتفاقي، فإنه متوقف على إبطالها، مع أن فيه شق الفعل هذا كله على رأي أهل الحق من أهل السنة الباذلين جهدهم في قمع البدعة كثرهم الله تعالى وأما عند المعتزلة فبعد تمام هذا الاستعداد والصلوح يخلق العبد الفعل فيجب بخلقه فيتصف به العبد اتصافاً واجباً متساوية إلى الإرادة واتفق أيهما وجود فهو باطل، لأنه لو كانت النسبة واحدة فتحقق الفعل دون الترك ترجيح من غير مرجح بل وجود من غير موجد، إذ لا موجد يجيء الترجيح منه، وإن أريد منه أن يصح الفعل والترك بالنظر إلى نفس القدرة، وإن أحدهما نظر إلى الحكمة فإن الحكيم لا يمكن أن تتعلق إرادته على خلاف ما علم من النظم الأتم فهذا صحيح وغير منافٍ لوجوب الفعل عند تعلق الإرادة، ووجوب الإرادة لأجل الحكمة، ووجوب للاضطرار، كيف والإيجاد منه تعالى لأجل الحكمة، ومطابقة الفعل للنظم الصالح من الكمالات، فيجب ثبوته له تعالى والإيجاد كيف ما اتفق من غير وجوب أمر مستحيل يجب تنزيهه تعالى منه، فلا يجترى مسلم على هذا والله He argued that the act of the servant is not chosen, so it is neither good nor bad in itself by consensus. Because if it is necessary it is obvious, and if it is permissible, then if it needs a preponderant the division returns, otherwise it is coincidental. So it depends on refuting that, while in it there is an extra coincidental branch not needed. Therefore he said: This is good and more concise than what is in al-Mukhtasar. It may be said: The impossibility of preferring the lesser is denied; rather it is permissible for the preponderant to be primary not obligatory, and the non-existent to be a possible lesser. Then preferring the lesser is not primary, not that it is impossible. Then there is no sufficiency, and this is obstinacy because its impossibility is primary, free from explanation. The answer: The utmost necessary from the explanation is the necessity of the act from the preponderant, and it is permissible that it be choice, and that necessity by choice does not necessitate compulsion, because it is absence of choice, and here choice is attached. Necessity of the difference between the two movements of choice and tremor: both are necessary from their preponderants, the first is chosen not the second, although it is rebutted by the act of Allah Most High, for if His act is preponderant it is necessary, otherwise its occurrence is impossible. It was said detailing the proof: If the act issues from the servant by will, the will does not issue from another will, and so on, otherwise infinite regress in the principle would occur. Also we do not find from ourselves at the occurrence of the act except one will, so the cause of the will is not the will of the willer. So either it must be by the creation of Allah or by the act of the willer but without will and consciousness. On both estimates, the servant in the realization of the will is compelled, and the act is necessary at the will, thus it becomes coerced, for the chosen is that whose doing and leaving are possible. In other words, if all that the act depends on is realized, then it is necessary and compulsion follows, for then leaving it is not possible, otherwise preference without preponderant would occur. When the report reaches this, the mentioned answer does not proceed; rather it is not possible. Yes, rebuttal occurs by the act of Allah, glory be to His majesty, unless it is said by will mixed with compulsion, and no Muslim dares to do that. Then this speaker said: Then there is difficulty with three matters: First, that goodness and badness in the acts of the servant and Allah, glory be to His majesty, are not rational. Second, that Allah, glory be to His majesty, is not purely free in His act, rather His choice is mixed with compulsion. Third, that the servant is compelled in the act, causing difficulty in the matter of resurrection of reward and punishment. Then he said: The first and third can be refuted by adhering that choice mixed with compulsion is sufficient for goodness and badness, and likewise for conveying reward and punishment. But you know that saying permitting description of the coerced with goodness and badness breaks consensus. And the difficulty in reward and punishment is not because the act is not chosen or chosen, but because the servant can have an excuse that the act is necessary, so I cannot avoid it; then Allah would not have the conclusive argument. This is an absurdity and is not repelled by his saying. And they answered the second by permitting delay, since the utmost entailed in it is preferment without preponderant, which is not impossible; rather preponderance without preponderant or existence without an existentiator. Then he refuted it by proving the impossibility of delay. And so back and forth occurred, and the reality of the situation was not revealed. And the author of al-Hashiyah answered that this is not complete according to the Ash'ari, for he is satisfied with the existence of a supposed power in directing this obligation. And you know that it suffices for directing the legal obligation in his view, not rational good. Rather consensus has occurred that the coerced is not described with rational goodness and badness. And the verification of the matter according to what this servant has used from the indications of the noble ones and his opinion has been established in achieving the goal: that at the will of the servant, the motives to the act become realized from the partial imagination and desire towards it, so the servant directs his choice given by the Exalted, and thereby becomes prepared to be described with that act. For it is not the divine way to leave the prepared matter, seeking by the tongue of preparedness, devoid of it by withholding the emanation from it because He is Generous. Rather, His habit proceeds by giving what makes the matter perfectly suitable. So Allah creates the act in the willer by customary course, and he becomes described by it, and it rarely fails at the prevention of a prophet or saint, and it is called violation of habit. This is according to the apparent view. And the precise view judges that this prevention and its likes are obstacles to the existence of the act, and when they are removed, the act is necessary. All this is according to the opinion of the people of truth from the Ahl al-Sunnah who expend their effort in suppressing innovation – may Allah multiply them. As for the Mu'tazila, after this preparedness and suitability, the servant creates the act, so it becomes necessary by his creation, and the servant becomes described with it as necessary by his creation. So choice in the servant is nothing but directing power and will to the act, whether it exists by this direction as with the Mu'tazila or not as with us, and this does not negate necessity. As for the act of Allah, its verification is that His eternal knowledge attached to the world as it was suitable for existence in the most perfect system. So His will attached in eternity that it exist in this pattern, since there was no pattern suitable for existence better than the pattern. So the world comes into existence by this attachment and becomes necessary upon its requirement. For example, His will attached that Adam come into being in a certain time, and Noah in a time between them a thousand years, so they came into being and became necessary in this pattern. This attachment is creation with choice. As for power in the sense that doing and leaving are possible – which is attributed to the theologians – if what is meant is that the ratio of doing and leaving is equal to the will and whichever occurs is agreed, then it is false, because if the ratio were one, then actualization of the act without leaving would be preferment without preponderant, rather existence without an existentiator, since there is no existentiator from whom preferment comes. And if what is meant is that doing and leaving are possible with respect to power itself, and one of them is considered with respect to wisdom – for a wise being cannot have His will attach contrary to what He knew of the most perfect system – then this is correct and not contradictory to the necessity of the act when the will attaches, and the necessity of the will because of wisdom, and the necessity of wisdom because it is a perfect attribute necessary of establishment for the Exalted by the requirement of His essence. So power in this sense, and in the sense of an attribute by which if He wills He does, and if He does not will He does not do, are concomitant. And will is the preferment of the attachment of power to the side of doing or leaving, but this preferment is in Allah according to the requirement of wisdom and knowledge of the system, and it is necessary because it is eternal like other attributes, and in us according to our motives and purposes. So the difference between the chosen and the coerced has been uncovered for you in the most complete ways, such that no shade of concealment remains. Then we say: The objection has been repelled regarding the act not being described with goodness and badness, because choice is as mentioned and necessity does not contradict it. Rather the chosen act becomes necessary after choice or by choice. And second, that there is no trace of compulsion, for how can it be when the causing to exist from Him is for the sake of wisdom, and the conformity of the act to the suitable system is among perfections, so its establishment for Him is necessary, and existence in any manner without necessity is an impossible matter from which the Exalted must be exonerated. So no Muslim dares to this. And Allah knows the reality of the situation. As for the third problem, its solution as it should be is sought from the commentary on Fusus al-Hikam, and we will refer to it in summary, Allah willing. And it has become clear to you from this verification that the principle of the chosen act must be there was necessary.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a dense theological-legal dispute about whether human actions are voluntary (ikhtiyari) and therefore morally evaluable (hasan/qabih). The context is the Ash'ari position against the objection that if an action is necessitated (wajib) by a preponderant (murajjih), then it is coerced (idtirari) and cannot be described as good or bad. The author engages with arguments from both the Mu'tazila and the philosophers.

The passage begins by stating the objection: if the servant's act is not chosen, consensus holds it cannot be good or bad. The objector argues that if the act requires a preponderant, it becomes necessary; if not, it is coincidental. The response is that the necessity arises from choice itself, and necessity through choice does not entail compulsion. A key distinction is made between voluntary movement (like reaching for something) and involuntary movement (like tremors): both are necessitated by their causes, but the former is chosen because choice is attached, while the latter is not. The author then addresses the rebuttal that God's acts would also be subject to this: since God's act is preponderant, it too would be necessary. The author suggests that this difficulty is met by the idea of will mixed with compulsion, but no Muslim dares to claim that.

The objector then raises three problems: (1) goodness and badness would not be rational; (2) God would not be purely free; (3) the servant would be compelled, making reward and punishment problematic. The author shows that the attempted answer to (1) and (3)—that choice mixed with compulsion suffices—breaches consensus. The real issue is that the servant would have an excuse ("I could not avoid it"), which would negate Allah's conclusive argument. The answer to (2) by allowing delay is refuted.

The author then presents the Ash'ari resolution (credited to the author of al-Hashiyah): what suffices for legal obligation is not rational goodness but a supposed power (qudrah mutawahhamah). For the Ash'ari, the coerced is not described with rational good/evil, but legal obligation can still apply because the servant has a capacity that is hypothetically effective. The author further elaborates his own synthesis: when the servant wills, motives arise, and he directs his God-given choice, becoming prepared for the act. By God's habit (jari al-'adah), God then creates the act in the servant, and the servant is described by it. This is the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb (acquisition). The Mu'tazila hold that the servant creates his own act, but for both, choice is essentially the direction of power and will to the act, and this does not negate necessity.

The author then analyzes divine action: God's eternal knowledge and will necessitate the world in the best pattern. This is creation with choice (al-khalq bi al-ikhtiyar). Power in the sense of equal possibility (as some theologians define) is false because it would lead to preferment without a preponderant. The correct sense is that power is an attribute by which one can do or not do, but in God it is always exercised according to wisdom, so it coexists with necessity. For humans, power and will operate according to motives.

Finally, the author concludes that the objections are repelled: the chosen act becomes necessary after choice, not before, so there is no compulsion. The third problem is deferred to Sharh Fusus al-Hikam. The passage is a thorough defense of the Ash'ari position on human agency and moral responsibility, essential for Hanafi usul because it underlies the basis of obligation (taklif).

Key Terms
الاختيار (al-ikhtiyār): صرف القدرة والإرادة إلى الفعل (directing power and will towards the action).
الاضطرار (al-iḍṭirār): عدم تعلق الاختيار (absence of choice); the state where no alternative is possible.
الحسن والقبح (al-ḥusn wa al-qubḥ): Goodness and badness, here referring to rational (ʿaqliyy) valuation of acts independent of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari/Hanafi position defended in this passage, what is the meaning of 'choice' (ikhtiyār) in human actions?
A) The ability to create one's own act independently of God
B) The direction of power and will to the act, while God creates the act
C) The absence of any cause for the act
D) The equality of probability between doing and leaving an act

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari/Hanafi definition of choice (ikhtiyār) as directing power and will to the act reconciles divine creation of all acts with human moral responsibility, because necessity arises from the choice itself, not before it.

Voluntary Action: Hanafi vs Mu'tazila on Creation of Acts
Explaining the process of voluntary action and refuting Mu'tazila objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the creation of voluntary acts, explain the rational argument against the Mu'tazila, and identify the key attributes involved (irada, qudra, wujub).

Core Idea
The servant directs choice, but Allah creates the act; necessity does not negate freedom.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut delves into the second article on rulings, addressing a foundational issue in Usul al-Fiqh: the nature of voluntary human action and its relationship to divine creation. The author presents the Ahl al-Sunnah (Hanafi) position against the Mu'tazila, using rational arguments to show that Allah creates the act habitually after the servant's choice, and that this does not imply compulsion. Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping how actions are attributed to the servant for taklif.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage and extract the Hanafi (Ahl al-Sunnah) position and the Mu'tazila position on who creates the voluntary act.
Hanafi: Allah creates the act habitually after the servant's choice. Mu'tazila: the servant creates the act after full preparedness.
2
Analyze the Hanafi rational proof
The author provides a rational argument: if power implied equal possibility of act and abandonment, then actualization would require a preponderator; since no such preponderator could come from the act itself, it must come from divine wisdom. Trace this reasoning.
Key phrase: 'فإن أريد به أن نسبة الفعل والترك متساوية... فهو باطل لأنه لو كانت النسبة واحدة فتحقق الفعل دون الترك ترجيح من غير مرجح'.
3
Understand the Hanafi response to Mu'tazila
The Hanafi response explains that the servant's choice is only direction, not creation. The necessity of the act after choice does not negate its voluntary nature because the necessity arises from divine custom, not compulsion.
The text says: 'فليس الاختيار في العبد إلا صرف القدرة والإرادة إلى الفعل... وهذا لا ينافي الوجوب'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this dispute for Islamic jurisprudence: attribution of actions to the servant for reward and punishment despite divine creation.
The text implies that taklif is based on the servant's choice, not his creation of the act.

هذا المقالة الثانية في الأحكام تتحقق الدواعي إلى الفعل من التخيل الجزئي والشوق إليه فيصرف العبد اختياره المعطى من سبحانه، فيستعد بذلك للاتصاف بذلك الفعل، إذ ليس الشأن الإلهي أن يترك المادة المستعدة الطالبة بلسان الاستعداد عارية عنه بإمساك الفيض عنه لكونه جواداً، بل أجرى عادته بإعطاء ما يصلح المادة صلوحاً كاملاً، فالله تعالى يخلق الفعل في المريد بجري العادة فيتصف به، وقلما يتخلف عند سد نبي أو ولي ويسمى خرق العادة هذا بحسب الجلي من النظر، والدقيق من النظر يحكم بأن هذا السد وأمثاله من موانع وجود الفعل، وعند ارتفاعه يجب الفعل هذا كله على رأي أهل الحق من أهل السنة الباذلين جهدهم في قمع البدعة كثرهم الله تعالى وأما عند المعتزلة فبعد تمام هذا الاستعداد والصلوح يخلق العبد الفعل فيجب بخلقه فيتصف به العبد اتصافاً واجباً بخلقه فليس الاختيار في العبد إلا صرف القدرة والإرادة إلى الفعل سواء وجد بهذا الصرف كما هو عند المعتزلة أو لا كما عندنا وهذا لا ينافي الوجوب، وأما فعل الله تعالى فتحقيقه أنه تعلق علمه الأزلي بالعالم على ما كان صالحاً للوجود على النظم الأتم، فتعلق إرادته في الأزل بأن يوجد على هذا النمط إذ لم يكن نظم صالح للوجود أولى من النظم، فيوجد العالم بهذا التعلق ويجب على اقتضائه مثلاً تعلق إرادته بأن يتكون آدم في الوقت الفلاني، ونوح في وقت بينهما ألف سنة فوجدا ووجبا بهذا النمط، وهذا التعلق هو الخلق بالاختيار، وأما القدرة بمعنى أن يصح الفعل والترك الذي نسب إلى أهل الكلام، فإن أريد به أن نسبة الفعل والترك متساوية إلى الإرادة واتفق أيهما وجود فهو باطل، لأنه لو كانت النسبة واحدة فتحقق الفعل دون الترك ترجيح من غير مرجح بل وجود من غير موجد، إذ لا موجد يجيء الترجيح منه، وإن أريد منه أن يصح الفعل والترك بالنظر إلى نفس القدرة، وإن أحدهما نظر إلى الحكمة فإن الحكيم لا يمكن أن تتعلق إرادته على خلاف ما علم من النظم الأتم فهذا صحيح وغير منافٍ لوجوب الفعل عند تعلق الإرادة، ووجوب الإرادة لأجل الحكمة، ووجوب الحكمة لكونها صفة كمالية واجبة الثبوت للباري باقتضاء ذاته، فالقدرة بهذا المعنى، وبمعنى صفة بها إن شاء فعل، وإن لم يشأ لم يفعل، متلازمتان، والإرادة ترجيح تعلق القدرة بجانب الفعل أو الترك، لكن هذا الترجيح يكون في الله سبحانه على حسب اقتضاء الحكمة والعلم بالنظم، ويجب لكونه أزلياً كسائر الصفات وفينا على حسب دواعينا وأغراضنا، فقد انكشف لك الفرق بين الاختياري والاضطراري على أتم الوجوه، بحيث لا يبقى فيه شائبة الخفاء، فحينئذ نقول : قد اندفع الإيراد بعدم اتصاف الفعل بالحسن والقبح، بأن الاختيار ما ذكر ولا ينافيه الوجوب، بل الفعل الاختياري يجب بعد الاختيار أو بالاختيار، والثاني بأنه لا شائبة للاضطرار، كيف والإيجاد منه تعالى لأجل الحكمة، ومطابقة الفعل للنظم الصالح من الكمالات، فيجب ثبوته له تعالى والإيجاد كيف ما اتفق من غير وجوب أمر مستحيل يجب تنزيهه تعالى منه، فلا يجترى مسلم على هذا والله تعالى أعلم بحقيقة الحال . وأما الإشكال الثالث فحله كما ينبغي يطلب من شرح فصوص الحكم، وسنشير إليه إن شاء الله تعالى إجمالاً
This is the second article concerning rulings. The motivations to the act are realized from partial imagination and desire towards it, so the servant directs his choice given from the Exalted, thereby preparing for being described by that act. For the divine affair is not to leave the prepared matter, which demands by the tongue of preparedness, devoid of it by withholding emanation, because He is Generous. Rather, His custom is to give what makes the matter perfectly sound. So Allah Almighty creates the act in the willing one by custom, and he becomes described by it. Rarely does it lag due to an obstacle from a prophet or saint, called a breaking of custom. This is according to the apparent view. The precise view judges that this obstacle and its likes are preventers of the act's existence, and when they are removed, the act becomes necessary. All this is according to the people of truth from the Ahl al-Sunnah who exert their effort in suppressing innovation. As for the Mu'tazila, after the completion of this preparedness and soundness, the servant creates the act, so it becomes necessary by his creation, and the servant is described with it necessarily by his creation. Thus choice in the servant is only directing power and will to the act, whether it occurs by this direction as with the Mu'tazila or not as with us, and this does not contradict necessity. As for the act of Allah, its reality is that His eternal knowledge was attached to the world as it was fit for existence in the most perfect order, so His will attached in eternity that it exists in this pattern, since no order fit for existence was more appropriate than another. So the world exists by this attachment and becomes necessary according to its requirement. For example, His will attached that Adam be formed at a specific time, and Noah at a time a thousand years between them, so they existed and became necessitated in this pattern. This attachment is creation by choice. As for power in the sense that the act and its abandonment are possible, which is attributed to the theologians: if it is meant that the ratio of act and abandonment is equal to the will and whichever occurs is by agreement, this is false because if the ratio were one, then the actualization of the act without abandonment would be a preponderance without a preponderator, indeed existence without an existentiator. If it is meant that the act and abandonment are possible with respect to power itself, and that one of them is considered in relation to wisdom, then the wise one cannot have His will attached contrary to what He knows of the most perfect order. This is correct and does not contradict the necessity of the act upon attachment of will. The necessity of will is for the sake of wisdom, and the necessity of wisdom because it is a perfection attribute necessarily established for the Creator by the requirement of His essence. Thus power in this sense and in the sense of an attribute by which if He wills He does, and if He does not will He does not, are concomitant. Will is the preponderance of the attachment of power to the side of act or abandonment, but this preponderance in Allah is according to the requirement of wisdom and knowledge of order, and it is necessary because it is eternal like other attributes. In us, it is according to our motivations and aims. So the difference between voluntary and involuntary has been uncovered for you in the most perfect manner, such that no trace of obscurity remains. Then we say: the objection has been repelled that an act is not described as good or evil, because choice is as mentioned and does not contradict necessity; rather the voluntary act is necessary after choice or by choice. The second objection: there is no trace of compulsion, how could it be, since existence from Him is for the sake of wisdom, and the act's conformity to the good order is among perfections, so its establishment for Him is necessary. Existence in any random manner without necessity is impossible, and He must be exalted from it. So no Muslim dares this. And Allah knows the reality of the situation. As for the third objection, its resolution, as it should be, is sought from Sharh Fusus al-Hikam, and we will allude to it briefly if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the second article on rulings, focusing on the nature of voluntary human action within the Hanafi-Ash'ari theological framework. The author first describes how motivations arise from imagination and desire, leading the servant to direct his God-given choice. This preparation makes the matter receptive for God to create the act habitually. The author distinguishes the apparent view (that miracles occur when prophets block action) from the precise view (that such blocks are preventers, and their removal necessitates the act). He then contrasts the Ahl al-Sunnah position with the Mu'tazila: the Mu'tazila hold that the servant creates his own act, while the Ahl al-Sunnah hold that Allah creates it in the willing servant. The author argues that choice is merely the direction of power and will, and this does not contradict necessity. Next, he discusses divine action: God's eternal knowledge and will necessitated the world in the most perfect order, and this attachment is creation by choice. He refutes the notion of power as equal possibility by showing that it would lead to preponderance without a preponderator. Instead, power in God is an attribute that, combined with wisdom, necessitates action. The author then resolves two objections: first, that voluntary acts can still be described as good or evil; second, that divine determination does not imply compulsion. He postpones the third objection to Sharh Fusus al-Hikam. This passage establishes the theological underpinnings for fiqh rulings on obligation and human responsibility.

Key Terms
اختياري (ikhtiyari): An act that occurs after the servant's choice and direction of power and will, though created by Allah
اضطراري (idtirari): An act that occurs without any choice, entirely determined by external causes
إرادة (irada): Divine attribute of will that necessitates the preponderance of power toward the act or its abandonment according to wisdom
قدرة (qudra): Divine attribute by which if He wills He does, and if He does not will He does not; it is concomitant with the sense of possibility of act and abandonment
وجوب (wujub): Necessity of existence or occurrence, either by divine custom or by logical requirement

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the role of the servant’s choice (ikhtiyar) in the occurrence of a voluntary act?
A) The servant creates the act through his choice.
B) The servant directs his power and will, and Allah then creates the act habitually.
C) The servant’s choice is irrelevant; Allah creates all acts without any role for the servant.
D) The servant’s choice only determines the moral quality, not the existence of the act.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position holds that Allah creates voluntary acts habitually after the servant's choice, but the servant is still responsible because choice (ikhtiyar) is the basis of taklif.

Defining Kasb: The Hanafi Middle Path on Human Action
Definition and school comparison of human acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of kasb, distinguish it from the Ash'ari definition, and explain why the Hanafi view safeguards moral obligation (taklif).

Core Idea
Hanafi kasb: real power directed to intention, not an illusion without effect.

The nature of human action is a foundational issue in usul al-fiqh, as it determines whether humans can be held morally accountable. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi concept of kasb (acquisition) by contrasting it with the views of the Jabriyya, Mu'tazila, and Ash'ariyya, showing how the Hanafi position avoids both compulsion and self-creation while affirming God's sole creative power.

Guided Path
1
Map the schools on human power
Identify the positions of Jabriyya (no power), Mu'tazila (creative power), Shi'a (dualistic), Ash'ariyya (imagined power), and Hanafiyya (acquisitive power). Note which are condemned and why.
The hadith 'Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation' targets those who deny predestination.
2
Extract the Hanafi definition of kasb
Find the precise wording: 'صرَفَ القدرة المخلوقة إلى القصد المصمم إلى الفعل فلها تأثير في القصد المذكور'. Break it into components: power (created), direction (sarf), intention (qasd), effect (ta'thir).
The power is real but not creative; it acts on the intention, not the external act.
3
Contrast with the Ash'ari definition
Ash'ari kasb is described as 'وجود قدرة متوهمة مع الفعل بلا مدخلية أصلاً'. Understand why this is considered equivalent to jabr.
The pen metaphor: no real influence, so the servant is like a pen in God's hand.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The Hanafi view gives the servant real (though non-creative) power, making taklif meaningful. The Ash'ari view does not, which the author argues undermines moral responsibility.
This difference affects how istita'a (capability) is defined for legal obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثانية في الأحكام فائدة في تحقيق صدور الأفعال الاختيارية للعبد . «القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة» عند الجهمية الذين هم الجبرية حقاً لا قدرة للعبد أصلاً لا على الكسب ولا على الإيجاد (بل هو كالجماد الذي لا يقدر على شيء وهذا سفسطة) فإن كل عاقل يعلم من وجدانه أن له نحواً من القدرة والذي شجعهم على هذه السفسطة رؤية نصوص خلق الأعمال ولم يتعمقوا فيها وعند المعتزلة له قدرة مخلوقة الله تعالى فيه مؤثرة في أفعاله كلها سيئاتها وحسناتها، فالعبد خالق لأفعاله ويرده نصوص قاطعة محكمة غير قابلة للتأويل والإجماع القاطع، بحيث لا يزعزعه شبهات أولي التلبيس الضالين والمضلين، الذين شمروا أذيالهم لتأويلها، فضلوا أنفسهم وأضلوا كثيراً (وهم مجوس هذه (الأمة للحديث الذي رواه الدارقطني : وهم يقولون : إن القائل بقدر الله تعالى فقط قدرية، فأنتم القدرية المرادة في هذا الحديث، وهذا أيضاً نشأ من جهلهم بالأحاديث الصحيحة، فإن فيها يجيء قوم يكذبون بالقدر، وفي أثر ابن عمر وقع صريحاً أنهم مكذبو القدر، ثم إن الشيعة الشنيعة يقولون : إن المعاصي بقدرة العبد دون الحسنات، توهماً أن خلق القبيح قبيح، وليس الأمر كما ظنوا وكيف وقد جهلوا أن الخلق إعطاء الوجود، وهو خير محض، وإنما الشر الاتصاف بها بالنسبة إلى ذات المتصف، فإنه يوجب الإثم وهذا الرأي أشبه برأي المجوس، فإنهم يقولون بالواجبين، أحدهما: خالق الخير، والآخر خالق الشر، لأجل هذا الزعم، والشيعة أيضاً قالوا بخالقين، خالق الخير وخالق الشر (وما فهموا أي المعتزلة بل هؤلاء الجهلة أيضاً أن الإمكان ليس من شأنه إفاضة الوجود فإن من هو في نفسه باطل الذات محتاج في الواقعية إلى الغير، وكل على مولاه، كيف يقدر على إيجاد الأفعال من غير اختلال بالنظام الأجود، وهذا ظاهر لمن له أقل حدس من أصحاب العناية الإلهية، لكن من لم يجعل الله له نوراً فما له من نور (وعند أهل الحق أصحاب العناية الذين هم أهل السنة الباذلون أنفسهم في سبيل الله بالجهاد الأكبر له قدره كاسبة فقط لا خالقة (لكن) عند الأشعرية من الشافعية (ليس معنى الكسب (إلا وجود قدرة (متوهمة يتخيلها الشخص قدرة (مع الفعل بلا مدخلية لها أصلاً) في شيء، فعندهم إذا أراد الله تعالى أن يخلق في العبد فعلاً يخلق أولاً صفة يتوهم أوّل الأمر أنها قدرة على شيء، ثم يوجهه الله تعالى إلى الفعل، ثم يوجد الفعل، فنسبة الفعل إليه كنسبة الكتابة إلى القلم (قالوا ذلك كاف في صحة التكليف والحق أنه كفؤ للجبر) وهو ظاهر، فإنه متى لم يكن في العبد قدرة حقيقية، فأي فرق بينه وبين الجماد وعند الحنفية: الكسب صرف القدرة المخلوقة) الله تعالى (إلى القصد المصمم إلى الفعل فلها تأثير في القصد المذكور) فإذا تم صلوحه لوجود هذا القصد فتفيد ويخلق الله تعالى الفعل المقصود عقيب ذلك بالعادة) وقد يتخلف عنه قليلاً، كما نقل في المعجزات والكرامات، وأما عند عدم مانع من الموانع أصلاً، فيجب صدور الفعل منه سبحانه، فإنك قد عرفت أن الوجود من غير واجب باطل، فإن قيل : ذلك)
The Second Article on Rulings: A Benefit on Verifying the Issuance of Voluntary Acts from the Servant. 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.' According to the Jahmiyya, who are truly the Jabriyya, the servant has absolutely no power, neither over acquisition nor over bringing into existence; rather he is like an inanimate object that has no power over anything, and this is sophistry. For every rational person knows from his own experience that he has some kind of power. What encouraged them to this sophistry is seeing texts about the creation of acts, but they did not delve deeply into them. According to the Mu'tazila, he has a power created by Allah in him that is effective in all his acts, both bad and good. So the servant is the creator of his acts. This is refuted by decisive, unambiguous texts not subject to interpretation and by conclusive consensus, which cannot be shaken by the doubts of those who mislead and are led astray, who rolled up their sleeves to interpret them, thereby misleading themselves and many others. They are the Magians of this nation, according to the hadith narrated by al-Daraqutni, but they say that only the one who says 'by Allah's decree alone' is Qadariyya, thus you are the intended Qadariyya in this hadith. This also arose from their ignorance of the authentic hadith, for in them it states that a people will come who deny predestination, and in the narration of Ibn Umar it is explicitly stated that they are deniers of predestination. Then the vile Shi'a say that sins are by the servant's power while good deeds are not, imagining that creating evil is evil. But it is not as they thought; indeed they were ignorant that creation is giving existence, which is pure good. Evil is only the description of the act relative to the essence described, which incurs sin. This view resembles the view of the Magians, who assert two necessary beings: one creator of good and another creator of evil. The Shi'a also said there are two creators, creator of good and creator of evil. They did not understand—rather these ignorant ones also—that possibility cannot flow existence, for what is in itself false and needy for a realizer, how can it produce acts without disturbing the best order? This is clear to those with the slightest intuition among the people of divine care, but whom Allah has not given light has no light. According to the people of truth, the people of care who are the Ahl al-Sunna who sacrifice themselves in the path of Allah with the greater jihad, he has power only for acquisition, not creation. However, according to the Ash'ariyya of the Shafi'is, the meaning of kasb is only the existence of an imagined power that the person imagines as power co-occurring with the act without any real involvement in anything. So according to them, when Allah wills to create an act in the servant, He first creates a quality that seems at first to be power over something, then Allah directs the servant to the act, then the act is created. The relation of the act to him is like the relation of writing to the pen. They say this is sufficient for the validity of moral obligation, but the truth is that it is equivalent to compulsion, which is obvious, for when there is no real power in the servant, what difference is there between him and an inanimate object? According to the Hanafis, kasb is directing the created power to a firm intention directed to the act. So it has an effect on the mentioned intention. When it becomes suitable for the existence of this intention, it benefits, and Allah creates the intended act subsequent to that by habit. It may occasionally be delayed, as reported in miracles and saintly wonders. But when there is no hindrance at all, the act necessarily proceeds from Him, for you already know that existence without a necessary being is false. If it is said: that...
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a definition and comparative analysis of the concept of 'kasb' (acquisition) in voluntary human actions, a key topic in usul al-fiqh because it relates to the capacity for moral obligation (taklif). The author begins by citing the hadith that Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation, then delineates the positions: Jabriyya (including Jahmiyya) deny any human power, reducing humans to inanimate objects. Mu'tazila affirm that humans create their own acts, which contradicts Quranic verses and consensus. The Shi'a hold a dualistic view that sins are from the servant and good deeds from God, resembling Magian dualism. The Ahl al-Sunna (people of truth) are then presented: they affirm a power of acquisition (kasb) that is not creative. Within Ahl al-Sunna, the Ash'ariyya define kasb as merely an imagined power that accompanies the act without any real influence, making the servant like a pen—which, the author argues, is equivalent to compulsion. The Hanafi definition, in contrast, is that kasb is directing the created power to a firm intention. This power has a real effect on the intention, and God creates the intended act habitually after that intention. Thus, the servant has meaningful responsibility. The Hanafi position is presented as the balanced middle path between pure compulsion and pure human creation.

Key Terms
الكسب (al-kasb): Hanafi: directing created power to a firm intention, with real influence on the intention, and God creates the act subsequently.
القدرية (al-qadariyya): Those who deny divine predestination and claim humans create their own actions.
الجبرية (al-jabriyya): Those who deny any human power, reducing humans to inanimate objects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis in this passage, what is the meaning of kasb?
A) The coexistence of an imagined power with the act without any real involvement.
B) The directing of created power to a firm intention, which has an effect on that intention.
C) The creation of acts by the servant using a power created by Allah.
D) The denial of any human power over actions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of kasb—real power influencing intention without creating the act—is the only position that both affirms God's sole creation and provides a genuine basis for human moral responsibility.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

15 min
Human Capacity and the Nature of Intention (Qasd Musammam)
Debating whether human intention is created by God or has some effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi-Maturidi position on human intention (qasd musammam) and evaluate how it balances divine omnipotence with human accountability by distinguishing between creation (khalq) and causing (ihdath).

Core Idea
Human intention is not created by God but is a state caused by the servant, preserving both divine sovereignty and moral obligation.

In usul al-fiqh, the possibility of obligation (taklif) rests on human capacity. The Mu'tazila argued that humans create their own acts; the Ash'aris that God creates everything, including intention. The Hanafi-Maturidi school charted a middle path: intention (qasd musammam) is a 'state' (hal) brought into existence by the human through 'causing' (ihdath), not 'creation' (khalq). This lesson unpacks that metaphysical framework and its implications for the Islamic theory of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core problem
Recognize the tension between divine omnipotence (God creates all acts) and human accountability (obligation requires capacity).
2
Trace the three positions
Outline the Mu'tazilite (full human efficacy), Ash'arite (no human efficacy), and Hanafi-Maturidi (intermediate) views on intention.
3
Understand ahwal and the khalq/ihdath distinction
Grasp the concept of 'states' (ahwal) as intermediary entities and the difference between creation (essential effusion of existence) and causing (bringing into being more easily).
4
Analyze the specification argument
Examine the claim that qasd musammam must be existent and specified from general creation texts, and the critique that this specification lacks a mukhassis.
5
Evaluate the author's synthesis
Understand al-Musannif's own view: universal and particular wills, with the human free at the particular level and compelled at the universal level.

Source Text

فائدة خلق القدرة إذ فائدته أن تؤثر في شيء، وأدناه أن تؤثر في هذا القصد وفعل الله تعالى الحكيم لا يخلو عن غاياتها المودعة فيها، فلا بد يكون للقدرة نحو من التأثير ( ر ) لأنه (أدنى ما يتجه به حسن التكليف) فإن التكليف لغير القادر، مما يحيله العقل، وهذا أدنى طريق كونه قادراً (وهذا الرأي (كأنه واسطة بين الجبر والتفويض والحق هو التوسط بينهما، كما حكي عن الإمام الهمام جعفر بن محمد الصادق الله تعالى عنه وعن آبائه الكرام. قال المصنف : (وفيه ما فيه) ووجه بأن فائدة خلق القدرة واتجاه حسن التكليف يقتضيان أن تخصص جميع أفعال العباد، وقد أبيتم فتخصيص القصد المصمم تخصيص من غير مخصص، وهذا غير واف فإن مقصودهم قدست أسرارهم أن فائدة خلق القدرة واتجاه التكليف يقتضيان أن يكون لها نوع من الأفعال التأثير في الاختيارية، إما في وسيلتها فقط، أو فيهما، والتأثير في الوسيلة أدناهما، فخصصنا بها، وأما الأفعال [الصافات: (٩٦] وأمثالهما، وأحاديث خلق الأعمال، ثم في «النصوص» أيضاً الله إشارة إلى أن هذا التخصيص من نسبة المشيئة والعمل إلينا كما لا يخفى على المنصف، فتأمل أحسن التأمل ولا تلتفت إلى شبه أولي التلبيس،
