Time for Performing an Expanded Obligatory Act: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Discusses whether the entire time or only the last part is the time for expanded wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the time for an expanded wajib and evaluate the Hanafi proof using consensus (ijma') and the command's expansion.

Core Idea
The entire time is equally valid for expanded wajib; specifying a part is a restriction without proof.

The Hanafi school teaches that an expanded obligatory act can be performed at any point within its time frame, based on the clear command and consensus. However, a major dispute arose with al-Baqillani and the Shafi'is, who argued that each moment carries a choice between the act and a resolve. This passage delves into the intricate arguments and establishes the Hanafi position through rigorous critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the legal time for performing an expanded wajib? Is it the entire designated period or only a specific part (beginning, end, or any segment)?
The answer determines whether delaying or advancing within the time is permissible.
2
State the Hanafi position and its key proofs
The Hanafi view: all parts of the time are equally valid. Proofs: (1) The command itself expanded the act (amr wassa'a al-fi'l), implying flexibility. (2) Definitive consensus (ijma' qat'i) that one who performs in any part is not disobedient.
These proofs are considered strong because they directly reflect the Lawgiver's intent.
3
Present the opposing view (Baqillani) and its dalil
Al-Baqillani and most Shafi'is: in every part of the time, the obligation is either the act itself or the resolve ('azm) as a substitute (badal). The act becomes specifically wajib at the end of the time. The resolve extends like intention and does not need renewal.
This view introduces the concept of badal (substitute) for the act.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes the Shafi'i view: (a) Specifying a part (e.g., the end) is a restriction (tadyiq) contrary to the expansion (tawse'ah) granted. (b) The choice between act and resolve is an addition without proof. (c) The performer in the middle of the time is compliant by being a pray-er (musalli), not by performing one of two things. (d) The concept of multiple substitutes is not textually established and leads to absurdities.
The Hanafi critique focuses on the lack of evidence for the Shafi'i added conditions.
5
Reflect on the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If one performs the wajib at the beginning of the time, does it count as wajib or nafl? Hanafi: it is wajib. Shafi'i (Baqillani): it is a substitute for the resolve; the actual wajib becomes due only at the end, but the early act suffices as a substitute.
This difference affects whether one is considered to have fulfilled the obligation immediately or merely provided a substitute.

Issue: The time for performing the expanded obligatory act. It is valid. (If the obligatory act is expanded, then all of the time is time for its performance, so the obligated person may choose to perform it at any time he wishes within its designated time, and he does not neglect it throughout the time. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani and most Shafi'is said: The obligation in every part of time is the act or the resolve as a substitute, and the act becomes specific at the end, and they do not require renewal of resolve in every part, so that if he neglects the resolve in the second part, he sins. Rather, their madhhab may be that the first resolve extends like the extension of intention until it becomes constrained. So what is in al-Minhaj that the substitute is multiple and the replaced is one, and that has not occurred in the Sharia, does not apply. The way to avoid applicability: We do not accept the multiplicity of the substitute, for it is not textually stated, so it may be one extending like the extension of intention. And if there are two resolves, each is not a substitute in essence, but the substitute is one of them existing within them, as in the characteristics of expiation. So the particularity of the first and second has no role in substitution. Moreover, the replaced is also multiple, for the occurrences of the act are by the number of parts, i.e., the number of parts of time. There is no doubt that those occurrences are obligatory as substitutes, for if he does not perform in the first part, the second occurrence becomes obligatory, and so on. So likewise their resolves are multiple, so the occurrences equal the resolves as substitutes. If it is said: The obligatory is only prayer, and there is no multiplicity in it; rather, there is multiplicity in partial occurrences, so the replaced is one and the substitute is many. I say: The absolute resolve is one resolve, a substitute for the absolute prayer, and its parts are like its parts. If you say: The Sharia only obligated one prayer, not multiple prayers, but expandedly, so in every part a single prayer is obligated as a substitute, and the substitute resolve, if it is the one existing in the first part extending to the other, then this is the first answer, and the requirement of multiplicity of substitutes is absolute. I say: Suppose the obligation from the Sharia is one prayer, but not with a specific unity, but any unity whatsoever. From page 61: The article: The time. The second discussion on rulings: For the obligatory prayer, it is in any part it occurs, and there is no doubt that the prayer occurring in the first part is a partial one, and in the second part another partial. So if he does not perform in the first part, he must perform in another part, rather its occurrence in another part, and likewise the resolves. So reflect, except that the obligatory is one existing in these partials in essence, and the resolves have become many in existence, so there is no answer except the first. (And it is transmitted from some Shafi'is, and it is said rather from some mutakallimun: Its time is the first, so if he delays it becomes qada). So according to this, he would sin by delaying in the first time. (And) it is narrated from some Iraqi Hanafis: Not all the time is time for the obligatory, but its last part is its time, so if he advances it becomes nafl that fulfills the fard, like wudu before the time. In al-Minhaj this view is attributed to the Hanafis, but this attribution is wrong. And some of its commentaries said that they said there is no obligation of performance in the first time, so it is nafl with no place, for the obligation itself does not necessitate the nafl nature of the performed act, but rather contradicts it. Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute (ikhtilaf) about the time for performing an expanded obligatory act (al-wajib al-muwassa'). The Hanafi position, supported by the author, is that all parts of the designated time are equally valid for performance; the obligated person may choose any part without sin. This is based on the command (amr) that expanded the act (wassa'a al-fi'l) and on consensus (ijma') that one is not considered disobedient regardless of which part he performs. The passage critiques other views: al-Baqillani and most Shafi'is hold that in every part the obligation is either the act or the resolve (al-'azm) as a substitute, with the act becoming specific at the end. Some say only the first part is the time; others (Iraqi Hanafis) say only the last part. Al-Karkhi presents a nuanced view: if the act performed earlier remains with the capacity for taklif until the end, it is wajib; otherwise nafl. The author refutes these by arguing that specifying a part of the time is a restriction (tadyiq) contrary to the expansion (tawse'ah) granted by the Lawgiver, and that imposing a choice between act and resolve is an addition without proof. The text also delves into a sophisticated discussion about whether the substitute (badal) is multiple or one, with analogies from kaffarah characteristics and wudu before time. The final Hanafi position is that compliance is achieved by performing the prayer itself, not by one of two things, and the opponent's view is invalidated. The passage ends with a subtle point about the relationship between act and resolve, distinguishing between original (asl) and deputy (khalaf).

Key Terms
واجب موسع (wajib muwassa'): An obligatory act whose performance time is expanded, allowing the obligated person to choose when to perform within that time without sin.
عزم ('azm): Resolve or firm intention to perform the act, considered a substitute (badal) for the actual performance in the view of some scholars.
بدل (badal): A substitute, something that stands in place of something else, e.g., resolve as a substitute for the act, or vice versa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position defended in this passage, what is the time for performing an expanded wajib?
A) Only the first part
B) Only the last part
C) All parts of the designated time
D) The middle part

Key Takeaway
For an expanded wajib, the entire time is equally valid; specification to a part is a restriction without evidence.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Applying Causality Transfer to Time Deficiency: The Case of 'Asr at Sunset
Ruling on performing 'Asr prayer in the deficient part at sunset

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of causality transfer (sababiyya al-intiqal) to derive the ruling on performing 'Asr prayer during the deficient part of time, and distinguish between the validity of current day's 'Asr and the invalidity of makeup of a previous day's 'Asr.

Core Idea
Causality transfer enables valid 'Asr at sunset, but the whole time's causality blocks makeup of yesterday's 'Asr.

This lesson explores a subsidiary issue (far') that applies the principle of causality transfer to a specific time: the sunset period (deficient part). The Hanafi school holds that performing the current day's 'Asr during this time is valid because causality has transferred to that part, making the prayer appropriately deficient. However, making up a missed 'Asr from the previous day in the same deficient part is generally ruled invalid because the cause for that prayer is the whole previous day, which is not deficient in every respect. We will trace the derivation of these rulings and examine an intra-Hanafi difference on the validity of the makeup.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases and their rulings
Extract the two rulings from the passage: (1) 'Asr of the current day performed at sunset is valid; (2) 'Asr of yesterday (makeup) performed at sunset is invalid (according to the preferred view). Determine the hukm level for each: valid (sahih) vs. invalid (la yasihh).
The invalidity applies only to the makeup, not the current day's prayer.
2
Identify the cause (sabab) for each ruling
For the current day's 'Asr, the cause (sabab) is the deficient part itself, because causality has transferred to it from the complete time. For the makeup, the cause is the whole time of the previous day (الجمله من الوقت), which is deficient in one aspect but not another.
The phrase 'أي الجملة من الوقت ناقص من وجه دون وجه' indicates the whole time is deficient in one aspect only.
3
Apply the principle of matching deficiency
The principle: the deficiency of the cause must match the deficiency of the obligated act. For the current day's 'Asr, both cause and performance are deficient in every aspect, so it is valid. For the makeup, the cause is deficient in only one aspect, so the obligated act is not deficient in every aspect, and thus cannot be performed in a time (the sunset) that is deficient in every aspect.
This is the core of the usul derivation: 'السببية انتقلت إلى الجزء الناقص فنقصانه أوجب ناقصا'.
4
Analyze the objections and responses
The passage raises an objection: if part of the makeup prayer occurs in the complete time and part in the deficient, it should be valid by the majority rule. The response refines that the causality of the whole is due to its containing a part-whatever (جزء ما), which is absolute and complete; deficiency is only in the particular actualization at sunset. Thus the whole time is not deficient in itself.
This leads to the conclusion that deficiency is accidental to the performance, not to time itself.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute and identify the mufta bihi
Imam Fakhr al-Islam held that the makeup is valid due to lack of contrary narration from the earlier authorities. Shams al-A'imma ruled it invalid, based on the causal reasoning above. The preferred view (al-mukhtar) is the latter: invalid. Understand the basis of each and why the second is chosen.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; the chosen view aligns with the stronger usul reasoning.

فرع (صح عصر يومه في الجزء (الناقص) وهو وقت احمرار الشمس، لأن السببية، قد انتقلت إليه، فنقصانه أوجب ناقصاً وأدى كما وجب (لا) عصر (أمسه) أي لا يصح قضاء العصر لليوم الآخر (الأن سببه أي عصر الأمس أي (الجملة من الوقت (ناقص من وجه) دون وجه، فالواجب به لا يكون ناقصاً من كل وجه فلا يتأدى بالناقص من كل وجه، واعترض بلزوم صحته إذا وقع بعضه في الناقص، وبعضه في الكامل بأن شرع في الكامل وأتم في الناقص (فعدل) منه إلى أن الكل كامل اعتباراً بالغلبة فإن أكثر الأجزاء كاملة، وللأكثر حكم الكل (فالواجب به كامل من كل وجه ويرد عليه أنه يلزم أن يصح إذا أدى أكثر الأجزاء في «الكامل»، وأقل في «الناقص»، فإن المؤدى كامل باعتبار الغلبة كالسبب، فالأولى أن يقال إن سببية الجملة ليست إلا لأنها مشتملة على جزء ما من تلك الأجزاء، ولا نقص في هذا المطلق وإنما هو في خصوص مادة تحققه في وقت الإحمرار فورد) من أسلم في الناقص فلم يصل فيه لا يصح عصر القضاء (في ناقص غيره مع تعذر الإضافة في حقه إلى الكل) فإنه لم يكن أهلاً فيه، فالسبب ليس في حقه إلا الناقص، فينبغي أن يصح في ناقص غيره، ولا يبعد أن يقال إن سببية الناقص ليست باعتبار خصوصه بل لما هو مصداق للمطلق وهو كامل لا نقص فيه، إنما النقص في «الخصوص فقط، وإنما صح عصر اليوم مع أن سببه أي لمطلق كامل لأن الإيجاب لم يكن منه إلا بالأداء فيه، فقد وجب ناقصاً، وفيه أن وجوب وجوب القضاء بعينه وجوب وجوبه كذلك كان وجوب القضاء أيضاً ناقصاً فيتأدى في الناقص، فتأمل (فأجيب بمنع عدم الصحة فإنه لا رواية عن المتقدمين فيلزم (الصحة) هذا مختار الإمام فخر الإسلام، وقال شمس الأئمة: لا يصح، وهو المختار، وأشار إليه بقوله : (والحق، أن لا نقص في الوقت لذاته فإن الوقت وقت كسائر الأوقات، ولذا تصح فيه عبادات أخرى (وإنما لزم) النقص (الأداء) للصلاة (بالعرض) لوقوع التشبه بعبادة الكفار فإن الشمس تطلع وتغرب مع قرن الشيطان فيعبد فيه ( فيحمل ) هذا النقص في الأداء الشرفه وكماله وإلا فات، هذا الكمال (دون غيره أي غير الأداء، فإن فيه اختيار النقصان مع إمكان الاجتناب عنه، فلا يصح هذا، والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال .
Subsidiary issue: (Performing) his day's Asr (is valid) in the (deficient) part, which is the time of sunset. Because causality has transferred to it. So its deficiency necessitates deficiency, and he performed as it was obligated. (Not) the Asr of (his yesterday) i.e., it is not valid to make up the Asr of the previous day (because its cause i.e., yesterday's Asr i.e., the whole of time is deficient in one aspect and not another. So the obligated by it is not deficient in every aspect, so it cannot be performed by the deficient in every aspect. And it was objected that it entails its validity if some of it occurs in the deficient and some in the complete, by starting in the complete and completing in the deficient. (So he altered) from it to the view that the whole is complete considering the majority, because most parts are complete, and the majority has the rule of the whole. (So the obligated by it is complete in every aspect. And it is replied that it would necessitate that it is valid if he performed most parts in the complete and a few in the deficient, for what is performed is complete by considering majority like the cause. So it is better to say that the causality of the whole is only because it includes a part-whatever of those parts, and there is no deficiency in this absolute; rather it is in the particular matter of its actualization in the time of sunset. So it should be valid in a deficient other than it. And it is not far to say that the causality of the deficient is not by consideration of its particularity but because it is a manifestation of the absolute, which is complete with no deficiency; deficiency is only in the particularity. And the validity of today's Asr is only because its cause is the absolute complete, because the obligation from it was not except by performance in it, so it was obligated as deficient. In it, that the obligation of the makeup itself is its obligation; similarly, the makeup obligation was also deficient, so it is performed in the deficient. So ponder. (So it was answered by denying invalidity, because there is no narration from the predecessors, so validity is necessary.) This is the choice of Imam Fakhr al-Islam. And Shams al-A'imma said: It is not valid, and it is the chosen view. And he indicated by his saying: (The truth is that there is no deficiency in the time in itself, for the time is a time like other times, and thus other acts of worship are valid in it. (Rather, the deficiency) occurs (to the performance) of prayer (accidentally) due to resemblance to the worship of the disbelievers, for the sun rises and sets with the horn of Satan, so worship is performed in it. (So this deficiency is carried in the performance of the noble and its perfection; otherwise it is lost. This perfection (is not other than the performance, for in it there is choice of deficiency with possibility of avoidance, so this is not valid. And Allah knows the reality of the situation.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a subsidiary issue (far') applying the earlier principle of causality transfer. It rules on the validity of performing 'Asr prayer during the deficient part of the day (the time of sunset, when the sun reddens). According to the principle, causality has transferred to this part, so performing 'Asr then is valid, but the prayer is considered deficient because its cause is deficient. However, making up the 'Asr of the previous day during a deficient part of the current day is invalid because the cause for that makeup is the whole time of the previous day, which is deficient in one aspect but not another, so the owed prayer is not deficient in every way and cannot be fulfilled by a prayer deficient in every way. The text then discusses objections about partial performance in deficient and complete parts, and concludes that the majority view (al-mukhtar) according to Shams al-A'imma is that it is not valid (i.e., the makeup), but Imam Fakhr al-Islam held that it is valid due to lack of contrary narration. The truth (al-haqq) is that the time itself is not deficient; rather the deficiency is accidental in the performance due to resembling the worship of disbelievers (since the sun rises and sets with the devil's horn). Therefore, deficiency in performance is not permissible, but the prayer itself can be valid if the deficiency is unavoidable. This complex discussion shows how the usul principle of causality is applied to fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
جزء ناقص (juz' naqis): The deficient part of time, specifically the time of sunset when the sun reddens.
سببية الجملة (sababiyyat al-jumla): The causality of the whole time, which is considered complete because it contains a part-whatever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (al-mukhtar) in the text, is it valid to make up a missed 'Asr from the previous day during the sunset time of the current day?
A) Yes, because causality has transferred to that part
B) No, because the cause for the makeup is the whole time of the previous day, which is not fully deficient
C) Yes, if most of the prayer is performed in the complete time
D) No, because all prayers at sunset are invalid

Key Takeaway
The validity of prayer in a deficient time depends on matching the deficiency of the cause (sabab) with the deficiency of the act; for a makeup prayer, the cause is the whole time of the missed day, which is not fully deficient, thus the act cannot be performed in a fully deficient part unless unavoidable.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Inseparability of Obligation and Obligation to Perform
Dispute on separability of wujub and wujub al-ada'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the inseparability of wujub and wujub al-ada' for bodily acts, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using zakat and wudu.

Core Idea
For bodily acts, the obligation itself demands immediate performance; financial obligations can be delayed.

This passage explores a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of obligation. While both agree that for bodily acts like prayer the obligation and demand to perform are inseparable, the Shafi'i school holds that for financial acts like zakat, the obligation exists before the demand. The discussion then examines wudu as a potential counterexample to test the principle, prompting a refinement of the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the claim being made: that for bodily obligations (wajib badani), wujub (obligation) and wujub al-ada' (obligation to perform) are inseparable. That is, once the cause of obligation is realized, both arise simultaneously.
The Hanafi school asserts this as a rule for bodily acts.
2
Identify the Shafi'i exception
Recognize that the Shafi'i school distinguishes between financial and bodily acts. For financial acts like zakat, they argue that the obligation (wujub) can precede the obligation to perform (wujub al-ada').
The exception is rooted in the nature of financial obligations.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Examine the evidence cited: for zakat, no sin in delaying before the year, and payment before the year fulfills the obligation. This shows that the zakat itself is obligatory before performance is demanded.
This is a form of istidlal bi al-athaar (reasoning from practical consequences).
4
Examine the wudu objection
Consider the challenge: wudu before the time is a bodily act, yet it shares features with zakat—no sin in delaying and performance before time counts. If the Shafi'i exception applies to financial acts, why not to wudu? This tests the Hanafi rule.
The objection forces a clarification of the Hanafi position.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the discussion assumes the cause (sabab) of obligation has been realized. In the case of wudu before time, the cause (e.g., time of prayer) has not yet occurred, so it is not a valid counterexample. Thus the inseparability holds once the cause is present.
This response highlights the importance of the cause in defining the scope of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان مسألة [ الوجوب ووجوب الأداء] الأداء ولما (لا ينفصل الوجوب عن وجوب الأداء في الواجب (البدني عند الشافعية بخلاف) الواجب المالي كالزكاة فإنها عنده قبل الحول كانت نفسها واجبة دون أدائها، فإنه يجب بعد الحول (بدليل عدم الإثم بالتأخير من وقت تملك النصاب إلى حولان الحول، فإن مات قبله لا يؤاخذ بها والسقوط بالتعجيل قبل حولان الحول بنية الفرض فعلم أن نفسها واجبة قبله وليست مطلوبة الأداء (أقول يرد الوضوء قبل الوقت فإنه لا يأثم بالتأخير إلى الوقت، ويسقط بالأداء، قبل الوقت فيجب أن يفترقا فيه أيضاً وهو بدني في الحاشية»: يمكن أن يقال: إن الكلام بعد تحقق السبب، وها هنا لم يتحقق سبب وجوب الوضوء ولم يرتض به، وقال فيه ما أن المقصود النقض على الدليل وهو لازم فإن ما استدل به جار ها هنا أيضاً عدم الافتراق عندكم، ويمكن أن يقرر الكلام بأن السقوط بالأداء فيه مع عدم الإثم في التأخير فيه، ووجهه
It was a question: [Obligation and Obligation to Perform] Performance and when (the obligation does not separate from the obligation to perform in bodily obligatory acts according to the Shafi'is, unlike) financial obligatory acts like zakat, for according to him before the year it itself was obligatory without its performance, for it becomes obligatory after the year (by evidence of no sin in delaying from the time of owning the nisab to the passing of the year. If he dies before it, he is not taken to account for it. And its falling by hastening before the passing of the year with the intention of the obligation, so it is known that it itself is obligatory before it and its performance is not demanded. (I say: wudu before the time is refuted, for he is not sinful by delaying it to the time, and it falls by performing it before the time, so they must separate in it as well, though it is bodily. In the margin: It can be said: The speech is after realization of the cause, and here the cause of wudu obligation has not been realized, and he did not approve it. And he said in it that the intent is to refute the evidence, and it is necessary, for what he used as evidence is also present here: non-separation according to you. And it can be established that the falling by performance in it with the absence of sin in delaying it, and its face.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of a usul principle: whether obligation (wujub) is inseparable from the obligation to perform (wujub al-ada'). According to the Shafi'i view, for bodily acts (like prayer) the obligation and the obligation to perform are inseparable; once the time enters, the act is obligatory and must be performed immediately. However, for financial acts like zakat, the Shafi'is say that zakat itself is obligatory (as a debt) before the year passes, but the obligation to perform (i.e., pay) arises only after the year. Evidence: delaying zakat before the year is not sinful, and if one dies before the year, no penalty; also, paying before the year counts as fulfillment. This indicates that the zakat obligation exists before performance is demanded. The text then raises an objection: wudu before the time is similar—no sin in delaying, and performing it before time counts, so it should also be separate even though it is bodily. The answer in the margin (hashiya) is that the discussion assumes the cause is realized; for wudu, the cause (time of prayer) has not yet been realized, so it is different. The objection forces a reconsideration of the evidence. The text ends with a suggestion to establish that falling (saqut) by performance with absence of sin in delaying indicates something about the nature of obligation, but the full resolution is not given.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): The legal obligation of an act in the liability (dhimma), irrespective of the demand to perform.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to actually perform the act, as opposed to the obligation of the act itself in the liability.
الواجب البدني (al-wajib al-badani): A bodily obligatory act, such as prayer and fasting, where performance requires physical action.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause that triggers an obligation, e.g., the entrance of time for prayer or the completion of a year for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shafi'i school, which of the following is correct regarding zakat?
A) Zakat is obligatory with the obligation to perform from the moment of owning nisab.
B) Zakat itself is obligatory before the year passes, but the obligation to perform arises after the year.
C) Zakat is not obligatory until the end of the year.
D) Zakat is recommended before the year.

Key Takeaway
The separability of wujub and wujub al-ada' hinges on the type of obligation (bodily vs. financial) and whether the cause has been realized, with the Hanafi school asserting inseparability for bodily acts once the cause is present.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
The Hanafi Distinction Between Nafs al-Wujub and Wujub al-Ada'
Core argument and counterargument on the separation of obligation levels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the separation of nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada' in both mali and badani obligations, and explain the Shafi'i counterargument and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, the obligation itself is established in the dhimma separate from the demand to perform it, even in physical acts like fasting.

This lesson tackles a foundational debate in Hanafi usul: whether the pure existence of an obligation (nafs al-wujub) is distinct from the obligation to perform it within a time (wujub al-ada'). The Shafi'i school argues that in physical acts like fasting, the two are identical because the act is itself the performance. The Hanafis respond by insisting that even physical obligations have a reality 'in the dhimma' that precedes the demand for actualization. Understanding this distinction unlocks several practical rulings, including the case of a woman who menstruates at the end of the prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core disagreement
Locate the question: do nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada' separate in both financial (mali) and physical (badani) obligations? The Hanafis say yes, the Shafi'is say no for badani.
The text begins with an analogy between wudu and zakat to illustrate the point.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof from zakat and wudu
Examine how zakat can be paid early and still count as fard, proving nafs al-wujub exists before the year ends. Contrast with wudu, where the obligation drops upon performance because the purpose is achieved.
The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection about intention is key.
3
Understand the Shafi'i argument from Shaykh Abu Ma'in
The Shafi'i claim: in fasting, the act (imsak) is the performance itself, so the obligation of the act equals the obligation of performance.
This is the strongest challenge to the Hanafi position.
4
Trace the Hanafi response: reality in the dhimma
The Hanafis assert that fasting and prayer have a 'state' (hala) established in the dhimma by the Lawgiver. The demand to actualize that state is wujub al-ada', separate from nafs al-wujub.
The distinction turns on the concept of 'thubut fi al-dhimma'.
5
Apply the distinction to the menstruating woman case
If a woman menstruates at the end of the prayer time, she has no wujub al-ada' (since she is not fit for performance), but nafs al-wujub may or may not be established. The Hanafi ruling: no qada'.
This is a preview of the practical thamarah al-khilaf.

المقالة الثانية في الأحكام. مات حال تحقق السبب آية الوجوب دون حال أخرى، فإنه لا مساغ فيها إلى قول بالوجوب فتدبر. وقد يجاب بأن الوضوء إنما يسقط الوجوب لحصول المقصود وهو ارتفاع الحدث، بخلاف الزكاة، فإن واجبة ولا يأثم بالتأخير إلى الحول، ومن قبل الحولان لا يأثم، وإن ظن الموت فعلم أنها غير واجبة الأداء، بخلاف الوضوء، فإنه لا يؤدي بنية الفرض، بل إنما يسقط الوجوب في الوقت لارتفاع علة الوجوب وهو الحدث، الواجب البدني ليس إلا فعل الصوم مثلاً، وهو نفس الأداء، كيف والصوم إما نفس الإمساك المخصوص أو غيره، والثاني مكابرة وبهت، وعلى الأول فهو إما نفسه فعل المكلف أو غيره، فإن كان غيره فإما أن يوجد بفعله وفعله ليس إلا الإمساك الذي هو الصوم، فقد وجد الشيء باقتضاء نفسه، وإما أن لا يوجد بفعله فلم يبق اختيارياً للعبد حتى يكلف به، وإن كان نفس الفعل والفعل هو الأداء، فوجوب نفس الصوم هو وجوب أدائه فلا يفترقان بخلاف الواجب المالي فإن المال شيء يجب في الذمة بإيجاب الله تعالى، والأداء فعل فيه، فلا بأس بالافتراق ولقد بين هذا مطنباً في العبارة وفيما ذكرنا كفاية، والجواب أنه لا شك أن للصوم والصلاة حقيقة وهي الحالة التي تحصل في العين والتصور، والأداء إخراج تلك الحالة إلى الفعل، فالأداء فعل فيه، كما أنه فعل في المال، وحينئذ فنقول : الصوم إن أريد به الحالة التي يتصف بها العبد فهو عين الفعل بمعنى المفعول وغيره بمعنى الإيقاع والأداء، وقد جعله الشارع جبراً على ذمة المكلف، كما يجعل المال على ذمته، وهذا نحو من الواقعية المعتبرة من الشارع ولا طلب عند هذا الجعل ثم بعد ذلك يطلب من العبد يوقع ذلك الثابت في الذمة في «العين»، فإثبات الحالة الصومية مثلاً في الذمة هو نفس الوجوب، وحكمه صحة الأداء، وطلب إيقاع هذا الثابت وجوب الأداء، فاتضح الفرق، ومعنى الثبوت في الذمة اعتبار الشارع كون ذمة المكلف مشتغلة بشيء سيطالب بإيقاعه هذا (وأما الحنفية فقالوا بالانفصال مطلقاً أي انفصال نفس الوجوب عن وجوب الأداء في المالي والبدني (فمن حاضت آخراً) أي في وقت آخر الأجزاء (لا قضاء عليها لعدم وجوب الأداء (بخلاف من طهرت آخراً) يجب عليها القضاء لوجوب الأداء عليها، واعلم أن هذا التفريع ذكره صاحب الكشف وليس في متنه ويفهم من هذا أن القضاء مبني على وجوب الأداء والاستدلال الآتي يدل على أن مبناه على نفس الوجوب، والظاهر هو هذا لأن الثابت في الذمة إذا لم يؤد في الوقت، ولا بد من التفريع، فيجب أداؤه في غير وقته، قال في الحاشية: ويمكن أن يقرر أصل الكلام بأنه بالحيض في الآخر انتقلت السببية عما قبلها من الأجزاء إلى أن انعدمت فانعدم نفس الوجوب، فلا يطالب بالقضاء وبالطهارة في الآخر تقررت السببية بعد أن لم تكن، فاشتغلت الذمة، وثبت نفس الوجوب (۱) وإن كان معه وجوب الأداء أيضاً، وقد أشار إلى أنه لا يصلح توجيهاً للتفريع، فالأحرى أن يجعل هذا من تفريعات انتقال السببية، وقد وقع في كلام الإمام فخر الإسلام تفريع عدم مؤاخذة من مات قبل الآخر على الانتقال، وهذا مثله، قال واقف الأسرار ولك أن تسقط مؤونة انتقال السببية وتقول : مبنى القضاء على أصل الوجوب، لكن بشرط بقائه، وها هنا لم يبق لارتفاع الأهلية عند توجه المطالبة بخلاف الطاهرة آخراً لتقرر الوجوب مع عدم الأداء، وهذا لا يفهمه هذا العبد فإن ارتفاع الوجوب بعد تقرره وبراءة الذمة بعد اشتغالها لا بدل له من وجه وكيف يرتفع الوجوب وقد تقرر سببه، فلا بد من الاستعانة بانتقال السببية، فإن سببية السبب قد ارتفعت وارتفعت الأهلية عند وجوب سبب آخر فتأمل (واستدلوا بوجوب القضاء على نائم كل الوقت بالإجماع (وهو فرع الوجوب) لأن ما لم تكن الذمة مشغولة به لا يتدارك، وهو إما نفس الوجوب أو وجوب الأداء والاتفاق على الأداء عليه أي على نائم كل الوقت لعدم الخطاب) ولا بد من الخطاب وإنما الخطاب (حذراً عن (اللغو) فإن خطاب من لا يقدر على فهمه لغو، فإن قلت : إذا لم يكن النائم مخاطباً ولم يجب عليه الأداء لا يجب عليه القضاء، لأن القضاء عندهم لا يجب إلا بما يجب به الأداء، قلت : لفظ الأداء يطلق على معنيين : أحدهما نفس الفعل الواجب، ووجوبه إما مع طلب الأداء وهو وجوب الأداء، أو بدون الطلب بل بنفس ثبوته في الذمة وهو نفس الوجوب ومقابله القضاء، وهذا هو المراد في تلك المسألة . والثاني : إيقاع الفعل المطلوب، وهو يعم القضاء والأداء، وهو المراد ها هنا فتدبر . ثم من العجائب ما وقع في بعض شروح أصول الإمام فخر الإسلام من أن النائم أيضاً مطالب بالصلاة، لكن لأن يظهر أثره في القضاء فإن الطلب كما أنه قد يكون لأن يوقع المطلوب، كذلك قد يطلب لأن يوقع مثله، كما في من صار أهلاً آخر الوقت بحيث لا يسع
The second article on rulings. He died at the moment of occurrence of the cause, which is a sign of obligation, not in another state, for there is no room for a statement of obligation in it, so reflect. And it may be answered that ablution only nullifies obligation due to attainment of the intended purpose, which is removal of hadath, unlike zakat, for its intended purpose is performance which is an act of drawing near, so if it were not obligatory beforehand it would not be valid. If you say: This is not valid according to al-Shafi'i because intention is a condition with him, so the intended purpose there is also drawing near, I say: The intended purpose is removal of hadath, but its removal with him is not achieved without intention. And this answer was refuted by [saying] that zakat may have as its intended purpose the arrival of wealth to the recipient from a specific source, which is the nisab, and when it has arrived, the obligation falls. Perhaps this is disputation, for zakat is a pillar of religion and a foundation of worship, so the intended purpose of obligating it is to burden the obligated person by performing it in the [specific] property, so if it were not obligatory before the year's end, it would not be valid. The best in rebuttal is to say: Zakat is dropped by advancing it with the intention of performing the obligatory duty; if he intends supererogatory, it does not drop, so it is known that it is obligatory and he does not sin by delaying until the year, and before the year's end he does not sin even if he fears death, so it is known that it is not obligatory in terms of performance, unlike ablution, for it is not performed with the intention of obligatory duty, but rather the obligation in the time drops due to removal of the cause of obligation, which is hadath. Its analogue is the dropping of jihad by the death of disbelievers, or by other disbelievers killing them. Then know that the proof of the Shafi'is only indicates separation in financial [obligations], which is agreed upon, and from it does not follow non-separation in physical [obligations]. Shaykh Abu Ma'in strengthened their pillars by [saying] that physical obligatory duty is nothing but the act of fasting, for example, which is the performance itself. How so? For fasting is either the specific abstinence or something else; the second is obstinacy and slander. On the first, it is either the act of the obligated person itself or something else. If it is something else, then either it exists by his action, and his action is nothing but the abstinence which is fasting, then the thing exists by its own requirement; or it does not exist by his action, then it is not subject to the servant's choice so as to be obligated with it. And if it is the act itself, and the act is performance, then the obligation of the fasting itself is the obligation of its performance, so they do not separate, unlike financial obligatory duty, for wealth is something that becomes obligatory in the dhimma by Allah's command, and performance is an act in it, so there is no harm in separation. He explained this at length in the expression, and in what we have mentioned is sufficient. The answer: There is no doubt that fasting and prayer have a reality, which is the state that occurs in the entity and conception, and performance is bringing out that state into action, so performance is an act in it, just as it is an act in wealth. Then we say: If by fasting is meant the state that the servant is described with, it is the act itself in the sense of the object, and other [meaning] in the sense of causing and performing. And the Lawgiver has made it a burden on the dhimma of the obligated person, just as He makes wealth on his dhimma. This is a kind of reality considered by the Lawgiver, and there is no demand with this establishment. Then after that, the servant is demanded to actualize that which is established in the dhimma in the [external] entity. So establishing the state of fasting, for example, in the dhimma is the obligation itself (nafs al-wujub), and its ruling is the validity of performance, and the demand to actualize this established [thing] is the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'). So the difference is clear. And the meaning of 'thubut in the dhimma' is the Lawgiver's consideration that the dhimma of the obligated person is occupied with something for which he will be asked to actualize it. (As for the Hanafis, they said with complete separation, i.e., separation of the obligation itself from the obligation of performance in both financial and physical [obligations]. So if a woman menstruates at the end [of the time], i.e., in the time of the last part, there is no qada' upon her due to lack of obligation of performance. (Unlike one who becomes pure at the end, qada' is obligatory upon her due to the obligation of performance being upon her). And know that this subdivision was mentioned by the author of al-Kashf and is not in its matn. From this it is understood that qada' is based on the obligation of performance, and the following proof indicates that it is based on the obligation itself. The apparent is this because if what is established in the dhimma is not performed in time, it must be made up, so its performance becomes obligatory outside its time. He said in al-Hashiya: It can be established that by menstruation at the end, the causality transfers from what preceded it of the parts to being non-existent, so the obligation itself ceases, and he is not asked for qada'. By purity at the end, causality is established after it was not, so the dhimma becomes occupied, and the obligation itself is established, although with it is also the obligation of performance. And he indicated that this is not suitable as a directing for the subdivision, so it is more appropriate to make this from the subdivisions of transfer of causality. And it occurred in the words of Imam Fakhr al-Islam a subdivision of non-accountability of one who dies before the end based on transfer, and this is similar. The bearer of secrets said: You can drop the burden of transfer of causality and say: qada' is based on the original obligation, but with the condition of its remaining, and here it did not remain due to removal of capacity at the time of demand, unlike the one who becomes pure at the end because the obligation is established with non-performance. This this servant does not understand it, for the removal of obligation after its establishment and the clearing of the dhimma after its occupation has no substitute from any aspect, and how can the obligation be removed when its cause has been established? So there is no escape from seeking help from transfer of causality, for the causality of the cause has been removed and the capacity has been removed when another cause becomes obligatory, so reflect. (And they argued by the obligation of qada' on one who sleeps the entire time by consensus, and it is a branch of obligation). Because what the dhimma is not occupied with cannot be made up, and it is either the obligation itself or the obligation of performance, and they agreed on [the absence of] performance upon him, i.e., upon one who sleeps the entire time, due to lack of address. And the address must be, because addressing one who cannot understand it is vain. If you say: If the sleeper is not addressed and performance is not obligatory upon him, then qada' is not obligatory upon him, because with them qada' is only obligatory by what performance is obligatory with. I say: The term 'ada'' is used in two senses: one is the obligatory act itself, and its obligation is either with the demand for performance, which is the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'), or without demand but by its very establishment in the dhimma, which is the obligation itself (nafs al-wujub), and its counterpart is qada'. This is what is meant in that issue. The second is the actualization of the demanded act, which includes qada' and ada', and this is what is meant here. So reflect. Then among the wonders is what occurred in some commentaries on the Usul of Imam Fakhr al-Islam that the sleeper is also asked for prayer, but so that its effect appears in qada', for the demand, just as it may be to actualize the demanded, likewise it may be to actualize its like, as in one who becomes eligible at the end of the time such that it does not have room.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the relationship between nafs al-wujub (the obligation itself) and wujub al-ada' (the obligation of performance). The discussion begins with an analogy between wudu and zakat. It is argued that wudu drops the obligation once performed because the purpose (raf' al-hadath) is achieved, whereas zakat requires niat for it to be valid according to the Shafi'is, but the Hanafi response emphasizes that zakat is obligatory before the year ends, and advancing it with niat of fard fulfills the obligation. The Shafi'i position is that in physical obligations like fasting, the obligation itself is identical to the obligation of performance because the act is the performance itself. The Hanafi position is that there is a clear distinction: nafs al-wujub is the establishment of a state in the dhimma (e.g., the state of being obligated to fast), while wujub al-ada' is the demand to actualize that state in the external world. The Hanafis hold this separation in both financial and physical obligations. The text then applies this to the case of a menstruating woman at the end of the prayer time: according to the Hanafis, since she has no obligation of performance, no qada' is required; but if she becomes pure at the end, she must perform qada'. This leads to a discussion on whether qada' is based on wujub al-ada' or nafs al-wujub, with references to scholars like the author of al-Kashf, al-Hashiya, and Fakhr al-Islam. The concept of 'transfer of causality' is invoked to explain why qada' becomes obligatory. Finally, the case of a person who sleeps the entire time is examined: despite lacking direct address (khitab) during sleep, the obligation of qada' is established by consensus, and the term 'ada'' is clarified to have two meanings: the obligatory act itself (which can be qada' or ada') and the actualization of the demanded act. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that physical obligations cannot have a separate nafs al-wujub from wujub al-ada'. The Hanafi position is that even in physical obligations, the dhimma can be occupied with a state that must be actualized, allowing for qada' even when performance was not possible.

Key Terms
نفس الوجوب (nafs al-wujub): The obligation itself; the establishment of a duty (e.g., state of fasting) in the dhimma of the obligated person by the command of the Lawgiver.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation of performance; the demand to actualize the duty established in the dhimma within the specified time.
الأداء (al-ada'): Two meanings: (1) the obligatory act itself (which may be performed as ada' or qada'), (2) the actualization of the demanded act (includes both first-time performance and make-up).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the basis for qada' being obligatory on a woman who becomes pure at the end of the prayer time?
A) The obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') was present.
B) The obligation itself (nafs al-wujub) was established and remained.
C) She had the capacity to perform before purity.
D) The cause of obligation transferred to the next time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi separation of nafs al-wujub from wujub al-ada' is a fundamental usul principle that explains how qada' can be owed even when performance during the time was impossible.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
7 min
Practical Consequences: Menstruation, Sleep, and the Basis of Qada'
Application of the separation principle to specific cases and proof by consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada' to determine whether qada' is required for a menstruating woman at the end of time and for a person who sleeps the entire time, and explain the role of consensus in establishing the principle.

Core Idea
Qada' is based on nafs al-wujub, not wujub al-ada'; thus a menstruating woman at the end has no qada' because nafs al-wujub was never established.

Having established the theoretical distinction between nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada', this lesson examines its application to two paradigmatic cases: the menstruating woman who becomes impure at the last moment of the prayer time, and the person who sleeps through an entire prayer time. These cases are litmus tests for understanding how obligation functions in Hanafi usul. The sleeper case is particularly important because it is supported by consensus, providing a strong proof for the separation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on the menstruating woman
If a woman menstruates at the end of the prayer time (e.g., at the last moment of Asr), she has no qada' according to the Hanafis. Understand why: because wujub al-ada' requires capacity (ahliyyat) during a significant part of the time, which she lacks.
The text says: 'فمن حاضت آخراً لا قضاء عليها لعدم وجوب الأداء'.
2
Contrast with the woman who becomes pure at the end
If she becomes pure at the end, she must perform qada'. This shows that nafs al-wujub was established when she became pure (since she had capacity), and it remains, necessitating qada'.
The text says: 'بخلاف من طهرت آخراً يجب عليها القضاء لوجوب الأداء'.
3
Analyze the consensus on the sleeper
The Hanafis argue: by consensus, one who sleeps the entire time must make up the prayer, even though during sleep she was not addressed (no khitab). This proves that qada' is based on nafs al-wujub, not wujub al-ada'.
The text says: 'واستدلوا بوجوب القضاء على نائم كل الوقت بالإجماع'.
4
Clarify the term 'ada' '
The author disambiguates 'ada'': it can mean the obligatory act itself (which includes qada' as its counterpart) or the actualization of the demanded act (which includes both ada' and qada'). The sleeper case uses the first meaning.
This resolves the objection that sleeper has no ada' obligation.
5
Explore the transfer of causality theory
The text discusses a subtle point: for the menstruating woman, some scholars explain the absence of qada' by 'transfer of causality' (intiqal al-sababiyya). The cause of obligation shifts to another time, so nafs al-wujub does not remain.
This is an intra-Hanafi refinement, not the main proof.

المقالة الثانية في الأحكام. مات حال تحقق السبب آية الوجوب دون حال أخرى، فإنه لا مساغ فيها إلى قول بالوجوب فتدبر. وقد يجاب بأن الوضوء إنما يسقط الوجوب لحصول المقصود وهو ارتفاع الحدث، بخلاف الزكاة، فإن المقصود فيها الأداء الذي هو قربة، فلو لم تكن واجبة من قبل لم تكن مجزئة، فإن قلت: هذا لا يصح على رأي الشافعي لأن النية شرط عنده، فالمقصود هناك القربة أيضاً، قلت : المقصود رفع الحدث، لكن ارتفاعه عنده لا يتحقق بدون النية، ورد هذا الجواب بأن الزكاة يجوز أن يكون المقصود فيها وصول المال إلى المصرف عن محل مخصوص، وهو النصاب وإذا قد وصل سقط الوجوب، ولعل هذا مجادلة فإن الزكاة من أركان الدين وأساس العبادات فالمقصود من إيجابها إتعاب المكلف بإيقاعها في «العين»، فلو لم تكن واجبة قبل الحولان لم تكن مجزئة هذا، والأحسن في الدفع أن يقال : الزكاة تسقط بالتعجيل بنية أداء الفرض، وإن نوى النفل لم تسقط فعلم أنها واجبة ولا يأثم بالتأخير إلى الحول، ومن قبل الحولان لا يأثم، وإن ظن الموت فعلم أنها غير واجبة الأداء، بخلاف الوضوء، فإنه لا يؤدي بنية الفرض، بل إنما يسقط الوجوب في الوقت لارتفاع علة الوجوب وهو الحدث، ونظيره سقوط الجهاد بموت الكفار، أو بقتل كفار آخرين إياهم، ثم اعلم أن دليل الشافعية لا يدل إلا على الافتراق في المالي وهو متفق عليه ولا يلزم منه عدم الافتراق في البدني وشيد الشيخ أبو معين أركانهم بأن الواجب البدني ليس إلا فعل الصوم مثلاً، وهو نفس الأداء، كيف والصوم إما نفس الإمساك المخصوص أو غيره، والثاني مكابرة وبهت، وعلى الأول فهو إما نفسه فعل المكلف أو غيره، فإن كان غيره فإما أن يوجد بفعله وفعله ليس إلا الإمساك الذي هو الصوم، فقد وجد الشيء باقتضاء نفسه، وإما أن لا يوجد بفعله فلم يبق اختيارياً للعبد حتى يكلف به، وإن كان نفس الفعل والفعل هو الأداء، فوجوب نفس الصوم هو وجوب أدائه فلا يفترقان بخلاف الواجب المالي فإن المال شيء يجب في الذمة بإيجاب الله تعالى، والأداء فعل فيه، فلا بأس بالافتراق ولقد بين هذا مطنباً في العبارة وفيما ذكرنا كفاية، والجواب أنه لا شك أن للصوم والصلاة حقيقة وهي الحالة التي تحصل في العين والتصور، والأداء إخراج تلك الحالة إلى الفعل، فالأداء فعل فيه، كما أنه فعل في المال، وحينئذ فنقول : الصوم إن أريد به الحالة التي يتصف بها العبد فهو عين الفعل بمعنى المفعول وغيره بمعنى الإيقاع والأداء، وقد جعله الشارع جبراً على ذمة المكلف، كما يجعل المال على ذمته، وهذا نحو من الواقعية المعتبرة من الشارع ولا طلب عند هذا الجعل ثم بعد ذلك يطلب من العبد يوقع ذلك الثابت في الذمة في «العين»، فإثبات الحالة الصومية مثلاً في الذمة هو نفس الوجوب، وحكمه صحة الأداء، وطلب إيقاع هذا الثابت وجوب الأداء، فاتضح الفرق، ومعنى الثبوت في الذمة اعتبار الشارع كون ذمة المكلف مشتغلة بشيء سيطالب بإيقاعه هذا (وأما الحنفية فقالوا بالانفصال مطلقاً أي انفصال نفس الوجوب عن وجوب الأداء في المالي والبدني (فمن حاضت آخراً) أي في وقت آخر الأجزاء (لا قضاء عليها لعدم وجوب الأداء (بخلاف من طهرت آخراً) يجب عليها القضاء لوجوب الأداء عليها، واعلم أن هذا التفريع ذكره صاحب الكشف وليس في متنه ويفهم من هذا أن القضاء مبني على وجوب الأداء والاستدلال الآتي يدل على أن مبناه على نفس الوجوب، والظاهر هو هذا لأن الثابت في الذمة إذا لم يؤد في الوقت، ولا بد من التفريع، فيجب أداؤه في غير وقته، قال في الحاشية: ويمكن أن يقرر أصل الكلام بأنه بالحيض في الآخر انتقلت السببية عما قبلها من الأجزاء إلى أن انعدمت فانعدم نفس الوجوب، فلا يطالب بالقضاء وبالطهارة في الآخر تقررت السببية بعد أن لم تكن، فاشتغلت الذمة، وثبت نفس الوجوب (۱) وإن كان معه وجوب الأداء أيضاً، وقد أشار إلى أنه لا يصلح توجيهاً للتفريع، فالأحرى أن يجعل هذا من تفريعات انتقال السببية، وقد وقع في كلام الإمام فخر الإسلام تفريع عدم مؤاخذة من مات قبل الآخر على الانتقال، وهذا مثله، قال واقف الأسرار ولك أن تسقط مؤونة انتقال السببية وتقول : مبنى القضاء على أصل الوجوب، لكن بشرط بقائه، وها هنا لم يبق لارتفاع الأهلية عند توجه المطالبة بخلاف الطاهرة آخراً لتقرر الوجوب مع عدم الأداء، وهذا لا يفهمه هذا العبد فإن ارتفاع الوجوب بعد تقرره وبراءة الذمة بعد اشتغالها لا بدل له من وجه وكيف يرتفع الوجوب وقد تقرر سببه، فلا بد من الاستعانة بانتقال السببية، فإن سببية السبب قد ارتفعت وارتفعت الأهلية عند وجوب سبب آخر فتأمل (واستدلوا بوجوب القضاء على نائم كل الوقت بالإجماع (وهو فرع الوجوب) لأن ما لم تكن الذمة مشغولة به لا يتدارك، وهو إما نفس الوجوب أو وجوب الأداء والاتفاق على الأداء عليه أي على نائم كل الوقت لعدم الخطاب) ولا بد من الخطاب وإنما الخطاب (حذراً عن (اللغو) فإن خطاب من لا يقدر على فهمه لغو، فإن قلت : إذا لم يكن النائم مخاطباً ولم يجب عليه الأداء لا يجب عليه القضاء، لأن القضاء عندهم لا يجب إلا بما يجب به الأداء، قلت : لفظ الأداء يطلق على معنيين : أحدهما نفس الفعل الواجب، ووجوبه إما مع طلب الأداء وهو وجوب الأداء، أو بدون الطلب بل بنفس ثبوته في الذمة وهو نفس الوجوب ومقابله القضاء، وهذا هو المراد في تلك المسألة . والثاني : إيقاع الفعل المطلوب، وهو يعم القضاء والأداء، وهو المراد ها هنا فتدبر . ثم من العجائب ما وقع في بعض شروح أصول الإمام فخر الإسلام من أن النائم أيضاً مطالب بالصلاة، لكن لأن يظهر أثره في القضاء فإن الطلب كما أنه قد يكون لأن يوقع المطلوب، كذلك قد يطلب لأن يوقع مثله، كما في من صار أهلاً آخر الوقت بحيث لا يسع
The second article on rulings. He died at the moment of occurrence of the cause, which is a sign of obligation, not in another state, for there is no room for a statement of obligation in it, so reflect. And it may be answered that ablution only nullifies obligation due to attainment of the intended purpose, which is removal of hadath, unlike zakat, for its intended purpose is performance which is an act of drawing near, so if it were not obligatory beforehand it would not be valid. If you say: This is not valid according to al-Shafi'i because intention is a condition with him, so the intended purpose there is also drawing near, I say: The intended purpose is removal of hadath, but its removal with him is not achieved without intention. And this answer was refuted by [saying] that zakat may have as its intended purpose the arrival of wealth to the recipient from a specific source, which is the nisab, and when it has arrived, the obligation falls. Perhaps this is disputation, for zakat is a pillar of religion and a foundation of worship, so the intended purpose of obligating it is to burden the obligated person by performing it in the [specific] property, so if it were not obligatory before the year's end, it would not be valid. The best in rebuttal is to say: Zakat is dropped by advancing it with the intention of performing the obligatory duty; if he intends supererogatory, it does not drop, so it is known that it is obligatory and he does not sin by delaying until the year, and before the year's end he does not sin even if he fears death, so it is known that it is not obligatory in terms of performance, unlike ablution, for it is not performed with the intention of obligatory duty, but rather the obligation in the time drops due to removal of the cause of obligation, which is hadath. Its analogue is the dropping of jihad by the death of disbelievers, or by other disbelievers killing them. Then know that the proof of the Shafi'is only indicates separation in financial [obligations], which is agreed upon, and from it does not follow non-separation in physical [obligations]. Shaykh Abu Ma'in strengthened their pillars by [saying] that physical obligatory duty is nothing but the act of fasting, for example, which is the performance itself. How so? For fasting is either the specific abstinence or something else; the second is obstinacy and slander. On the first, it is either the act of the obligated person itself or something else. If it is something else, then either it exists by his action, and his action is nothing but the abstinence which is fasting, then the thing exists by its own requirement; or it does not exist by his action, then it is not subject to the servant's choice so as to be obligated with it. And if it is the act itself, and the act is performance, then the obligation of the fasting itself is the obligation of its performance, so they do not separate, unlike financial obligatory duty, for wealth is something that becomes obligatory in the dhimma by Allah's command, and performance is an act in it, so there is no harm in separation. He explained this at length in the expression, and in what we have mentioned is sufficient. The answer: There is no doubt that fasting and prayer have a reality, which is the state that occurs in the entity and conception, and performance is bringing out that state into action, so performance is an act in it, just as it is an act in wealth. Then we say: If by fasting is meant the state that the servant is described with, it is the act itself in the sense of the object, and other [meaning] in the sense of causing and performing. And the Lawgiver has made it a burden on the dhimma of the obligated person, just as He makes wealth on his dhimma. This is a kind of reality considered by the Lawgiver, and there is no demand with this establishment. Then after that, the servant is demanded to actualize that which is established in the dhimma in the [external] entity. So establishing the state of fasting, for example, in the dhimma is the obligation itself (nafs al-wujub), and its ruling is the validity of performance, and the demand to actualize this established [thing] is the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'). So the difference is clear. And the meaning of 'thubut in the dhimma' is the Lawgiver's consideration that the dhimma of the obligated person is occupied with something for which he will be asked to actualize it. (As for the Hanafis, they said with complete separation, i.e., separation of the obligation itself from the obligation of performance in both financial and physical [obligations]. So if a woman menstruates at the end [of the time], i.e., in the time of the last part, there is no qada' upon her due to lack of obligation of performance. (Unlike one who becomes pure at the end, qada' is obligatory upon her due to the obligation of performance being upon her). And know that this subdivision was mentioned by the author of al-Kashf and is not in its matn. From this it is understood that qada' is based on the obligation of performance, and the following proof indicates that it is based on the obligation itself. The apparent is this because if what is established in the dhimma is not performed in time, it must be made up, so its performance becomes obligatory outside its time. He said in al-Hashiya: It can be established that by menstruation at the end, the causality transfers from what preceded it of the parts to being non-existent, so the obligation itself ceases, and he is not asked for qada'. By purity at the end, causality is established after it was not, so the dhimma becomes occupied, and the obligation itself is established, although with it is also the obligation of performance. And he indicated that this is not suitable as a directing for the subdivision, so it is more appropriate to make this from the subdivisions of transfer of causality. And it occurred in the words of Imam Fakhr al-Islam a subdivision of non-accountability of one who dies before the end based on transfer, and this is similar. The bearer of secrets said: You can drop the burden of transfer of causality and say: qada' is based on the original obligation, but with the condition of its remaining, and here it did not remain due to removal of capacity at the time of demand, unlike the one who becomes pure at the end because the obligation is established with non-performance. This this servant does not understand it, for the removal of obligation after its establishment and the clearing of the dhimma after its occupation has no substitute from any aspect, and how can the obligation be removed when its cause has been established? So there is no escape from seeking help from transfer of causality, for the causality of the cause has been removed and the capacity has been removed when another cause becomes obligatory, so reflect. (And they argued by the obligation of qada' on one who sleeps the entire time by consensus, and it is a branch of obligation). Because what the dhimma is not occupied with cannot be made up, and it is either the obligation itself or the obligation of performance, and they agreed on [the absence of] performance upon him, i.e., upon one who sleeps the entire time, due to lack of address. And the address must be, because addressing one who cannot understand it is vain. If you say: If the sleeper is not addressed and performance is not obligatory upon him, then qada' is not obligatory upon him, because with them qada' is only obligatory by what performance is obligatory with. I say: The term 'ada'' is used in two senses: one is the obligatory act itself, and its obligation is either with the demand for performance, which is the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'), or without demand but by its very establishment in the dhimma, which is the obligation itself (nafs al-wujub), and its counterpart is qada'. This is what is meant in that issue. The second is the actualization of the demanded act, which includes qada' and ada', and this is what is meant here. So reflect. Then among the wonders is what occurred in some commentaries on the Usul of Imam Fakhr al-Islam that the sleeper is also asked for prayer, but so that its effect appears in qada', for the demand, just as it may be to actualize the demanded, likewise it may be to actualize its like, as in one who becomes eligible at the end of the time such that it does not have room.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the relationship between nafs al-wujub (the obligation itself) and wujub al-ada' (the obligation of performance). The discussion begins with an analogy between wudu and zakat. It is argued that wudu drops the obligation once performed because the purpose (raf' al-hadath) is achieved, whereas zakat requires niat for it to be valid according to the Shafi'is, but the Hanafi response emphasizes that zakat is obligatory before the year ends, and advancing it with niat of fard fulfills the obligation. The Shafi'i position is that in physical obligations like fasting, the obligation itself is identical to the obligation of performance because the act is the performance itself. The Hanafi position is that there is a clear distinction: nafs al-wujub is the establishment of a state in the dhimma (e.g., the state of being obligated to fast), while wujub al-ada' is the demand to actualize that state in the external world. The Hanafis hold this separation in both financial and physical obligations. The text then applies this to the case of a menstruating woman at the end of the prayer time: according to the Hanafis, since she has no obligation of performance, no qada' is required; but if she becomes pure at the end, she must perform qada'. This leads to a discussion on whether qada' is based on wujub al-ada' or nafs al-wujub, with references to scholars like the author of al-Kashf, al-Hashiya, and Fakhr al-Islam. The concept of 'transfer of causality' is invoked to explain why qada' becomes obligatory. Finally, the case of a person who sleeps the entire time is examined: despite lacking direct address (khitab) during sleep, the obligation of qada' is established by consensus, and the term 'ada'' is clarified to have two meanings: the obligatory act itself (which can be qada' or ada') and the actualization of the demanded act. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that physical obligations cannot have a separate nafs al-wujub from wujub al-ada'. The Hanafi position is that even in physical obligations, the dhimma can be occupied with a state that must be actualized, allowing for qada' even when performance was not possible.

Key Terms
انتقال السببية (intiqal al-sababiyya): Transfer of causality: the idea that when the cause of obligation (e.g., time) passes without performance, the obligation transfers to another time or is nullified.
نفس الوجوب (nafs al-wujub): The obligation itself; establishment of a duty in the dhimma by the Lawgiver.
الأداء (al-ada'): Two meanings: (1) the obligatory act itself, (2) the actualization of the demanded act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the consensus mentioned in this passage, why does a person who sleeps through the entire prayer time owe qada'?
A) Because he was able to perform but chose not to.
B) Because nafs al-wujub was established at the entry of time and remains.
C) Because he is addressed in his sleep.
D) Because the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') applies to him.

Key Takeaway
The consensus on the sleeper provides the strongest proof that qada' is based on nafs al-wujub, and this principle consistently explains the rulings for both the menstruating woman and the woman who becomes pure at the end of time.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
15 min
The Obligation of Means to an Obligation: Hanafi Position
Debate on whether means to wajib are wajib with branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi position on the obligation of means and EVALUATE the opposing argument using the concept of wujub bil-‘arad, and APPLY this principle to the branch of exiting prayer.

Core Idea
The means to a wajib are not independently obligatory; only one sin is incurred for abandoning the original obligation.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut presents a classical usul al-fiqh debate on whether the prerequisites (muqaddimat) for an obligatory act are themselves obligatory. The Hanafi school maintains that means are commanded accidentally (bil-‘arad) and do not create a separate obligation. The text then applies this principle to branches involving confusion between wives and the obligation of exiting prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Determine what the two positions are: whether the means (muqaddima) to an obligatory act are themselves wajib. Note the Hanafi view and the opposing view.
The opposing view is attributed to some theologians like the Mu'tazila.
2
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses the concept of wujub bil-‘arad: the means are commanded accidentally by virtue of the original command. Only one sin is incurred if the means and the act are omitted.
The text argues the dispute is verbal if opponents acknowledge accidental obligation.
3
Analyze the branch of confusion between wives
In the scenario where two women are in a house and the husband does not know which is his wife, the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings differ. Understand how the muqaddima principle applies: refraining from both is not a wajib means because the duty is to avoid the haram, but the haram is not determined.
Hanafi: the husband may have intercourse with one as a substitute, not as a means to avoid haram.
4
Evaluate the branch of exiting prayer
Some argue that exiting prayer by one's action is wajib because it is a means to enter the next prayer. The Hanafi response cites the hadith of the Bedouin and the view of Imam al-Karkhi to reject this, showing that exit is not a devotional act.
Imam Abu Hanifa did not explicitly state its obligation; it is derived from branches, but the relied-upon view is that it is not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بوجوب الواجب ومأمورة بأمره (وهو معنى قولهم : إيجاب المشروط إيجاب الشرط، ولهذا لا يلزم إلا معصية واحدة إذا ترك الواجب مع المقدمات بالنظر إلى الواجب الأصل) بالذات (لا المعاصي بالنظر إلى الأسباب والشروط بل معصية الواجب الأصل منسوبة إليها بالعرض، والظاهر أن المنكرين لا ينكرون هذا، بل إنما أنكروا الوجوب صريحاً، فالنزاع لفظي، وإن أنكروا هذا المعنى فقد ظهر فساده القائلون بعدم الوجوب مطلقاً (قالوا: لو وجب) ما يتوقف عليه الواجب من المقدمة لزم تعقل الموجب له لأن الإيجاب بدون التعقل غير معقول، والتالي باطل، لأنا كثيراً ما نأمر بشيء ونغفل عن المقدمات (قلنا) اللزوم (ممنوع وإنما يلزم) التعقل ولو كان الأمر (صريحاً) وبالذات وليست المقدمة مأمورة إلا بمأمورية الأول بالعرض (ومن ها هنا لم يلزم تعلق الخطاب بنفسه ولا وجوب النية وإنما يلزم فيما إذا كان الوجوب صريحاً، بل لا لزوم هناك أيضاً، إذ لا تجب النية في الوضوء والغسل عندنا، وفي غسل الثياب وستر العورة بالاتفاق ومن ها هنا ظهر لك اندفاع ما استدلوا به من لزوم المعصية بترك المقدمة، وبلزوم وجوب النية في المقدمات وقالوا: لو وجبت لما التقليد بعدم الوجوب، ونحن نقطع بصحة أوجبت غسل الوجه دون الرأس، قلنا بطلان اللازم ممنوع، ولا قطع بصحة مثالك بحسب العادة، وقالوا: لو صح لزم قول الكعبي من انتفاء المباح وسيجيء فرع صح. (إذا اشتبهت المنكوحة (بالأجنبية إذا دخل امرأتان في بيت وقد زوج أحدهما الوكيل ولا يعرف الزوج الزوجة بعينها وقد مات الوكيل (حرمت) المنكوحة (لأن الكف عن الحرام) وهو وطء الأجنبية (واجب) وهو بالكف عنهما جميعاً للاشتباه ومنها هنا اشتهر أن الحلال والحرام لا يجتمعان إلا وقد غلب الحرام ولو قال مخاطباً لزوجتيه (إحداكما طالق حرمتا، لأن الاجتناب عن المطلقة يقينا فيه أي في الاجتناب عنهما كذا في كتب الشافعية، وأما عندنا ففي تلك الصورة لا يقع الطلاق على المعين منهما ، بل في «المبهم»، وإنما يقع في المعين بالبيان فله قبل البيان أن يطأ أيتهما شاء بدلاً، لكن وطء إحداهما يكون بياناً لتعيين الطلاق في الأخرى، فليس هناك الكف عن إحداهما واجباً حتى يكون الكف عنهما مقدمة الواجب، نعم، لو طلق معيناً طلاقاً بائناً ثم نسي المطلقة ينبغي أن تحرما، لأن هذا من صور اشتباه المنكوحة بالأجنبية (أقول) وإذا ثبت وجوب المقدمة فالغاية داخلة في المغيا) وإن كانت مقدمة ليعلم وجود المغيا) فعلم وجود المغيا موقوف على دخولها، وعموم التوقف في «الغايات كلها محل تأمل بل إنما يصح في البعض الذي هو مقدمات للمغيا. (فرع آخر قالوا: خروج المصلي بصنعه ،فرض، لأن من ضروريات الدخول في صلاة أخرى خروجه عن الأولى، والدخول في الأخرى فرض، فكذا الخروج عن الأولى، ولا يفقهه هذا العبد، فإن كونه من اللوازم لا يوجب أن يكون الخروج بصنع المصلي عنها فرضاً، كيف ويجوز أن يخرج من صلاة بعد تمام الأركان من غير اختيار بل هو الظاهر من حديث الأعرابي ، فإذا فعلت ذلك فقد تمت صلاتك إن شئت قم رواه الإمام محمد على أنه لو سلم فالخروج إذاً من متممات الصلاة الأخرى إلا من فرائض هذه ولم ينص الإمام أبو حنيفة على فرضيته، إنما استخرجوها عن بعض الفروع كفساد الفجر فيما إذا طلعت الشمس في القعدة الأخيرة بعد التشهد قبل السلام والجمعة فيما إذا خرج وقت الظهر في تلك الحال، أو تعلم الأمي سورة فيها وغيرها، وفيه كلام قد استوفى في فتح القدير»، وقال الإمام أبو الحسن الكرخي : إن القول بفرضية الخروج بصنعه لا اعتداد به فإن الفرض ما يكون قربة، وهذا الخروج ليس قربة، بل قد يكون قهقهة فكيف يكون فرضاً فالأشبه ما قال إنه ليس بفرض والله أعلم بالصواب.
With the obligation of the obligatory and it is commanded by His command (that is the meaning of their statement: making the conditioned obligatory makes the condition obligatory, and hence only one sin is incurred if he leaves the obligatory along with the means, with respect to the original obligation) essentially (not sins with respect to causes and conditions; rather the sin of the original obligation is attributed to them accidentally. It appears that the deniers do not deny this, but they denied the obligation explicitly, so the dispute is verbal. If they denied this meaning, then the corruption of those who say it is not obligatory at all has become apparent. They said: If what the obligatory depends on from the means were obligatory, then conceiving the obligator would be necessary, because obligation without conception is inconceivable. The consequent is false, because we often command something and are heedless of the means. We said: The necessity is denied; rather, conception is necessary even if the command is explicit and essential, and the means is not commanded except by the being commanded of the first accidentally. From here it does not follow that the address is attached to itself nor the obligation of intention; it only follows when the obligation is explicit; rather there is no necessity there either, since intention is not obligatory in ablution and bathing according to us, and in washing garments and covering the private parts by agreement. From here it became clear to you the refutation of what they argued from the incurrence of sin by leaving the means, and the necessity of intention in the means. And they said: If it were obligatory, then [?] by lack of obligation, and we are certain of the validity of 'you must wash the face not the head'. We said: The falsity of the necessary is denied, and there is no certainty of the validity of your example habitually. And they said: If it were valid, it would lead to the saying of al-Ka'bi of the negation of permissible things, and a branch will come. (If the married woman is confused with a foreign woman) when two women enter a house and the agent married one of them, and the husband does not know the specific wife and the agent died (then the married woman is forbidden) because refraining from the forbidden - which is intercourse with the foreign woman - is obligatory, and that is by refraining from both due to the confusion. Hence it is well-known that the halal and haram cannot meet except that the haram prevails. And if he said addressing his two wives 'One of you is divorced', both become forbidden because avoidance of the divorced woman definitively requires avoidance of both; thus in Shafi'i books. However according to us, in that case the divorce does not fall on a specific one, but rather on the ambiguous, and it only falls on the specific by clarification; so before clarification he may have intercourse with whichever he wishes as a substitute, but intercourse with one of them becomes a clarification for the divorce of the other. So there is no obligation to refrain from one of them such that refraining from both would be a means to the obligation. Indeed, if he divorced a specific woman with an irrevocable divorce then forgot the divorced woman, both should be forbidden because this is a case of confusion between the married and the foreign woman. (I say) If the obligation of the means is established, then the goal is included in the thing to which the goal is attached, even if it is a means to know the existence of the goal. But knowing the existence of the goal depends on its inclusion; and the general dependency in all goals is questionable; rather it is correct only in some which are means to the goal. (Another branch) They said: The exit of the praying person by his action is obligatory, because one of the necessities of entering another prayer is his exit from the first, and entering another is obligatory, so likewise exit from the first. And this servant does not understand it, for being a necessary consequence does not necessitate that the exit by the action of the praying person from it be obligatory. How, and it is permissible that he exit from a prayer after completing the pillars without choice; rather that is apparent from the hadith of the Bedouin, 'When you have done that, your prayer is complete; if you wish, stand,' narrated by Imam Muhammad. Even if it were conceded, then the exit is from the completions of the other prayer, not from the obligations of this one. Imam Abu Hanifa did not explicitly state its being obligatory; they only extracted it from some branches like the invalidity of Fajr when the sun rises in the last sitting after tashahhud before salam, and Jumu'ah when the time of Zuhr exits in that situation, or when the unlettered person learns a surah and others. There is discussion which has been covered in Fath al-Qadir. And Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi said: The statement that the exit by his action is obligatory is not to be considered, for the obligatory is that which is a devotional act, and this exit is not devotional; rather it may be laughter, so how can it be obligatory? So the most appropriate is what he said that it is not obligatory, and Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a detailed debate on whether the means (muqaddima) to an obligatory act are themselves obligatory. The author first clarifies that when we say 'obligation of the conditioned entails obligation of the condition', it means only one sin is incurred if one abandons both the obligation and its means – the sin relates to the original obligation, not to the means as independent acts. He argues that opponents who deny the obligation of means really deny explicit obligation, so the dispute is verbal. The opponents' proof: if means were obligatory, one must conceive them, but we often command things without thinking of means. The Hanafi response: conception is only needed for the explicit command, not for the accidental obligation of the means. He gives examples: intention (niyya) is not obligatory in wudu and ghusl according to Hanafis, and washing garments or covering private parts is obligatory by consensus without intention obligation. Then he addresses the subsidiary case of confusion between a married woman and a foreign woman when two women are in a house and the husband does not know which is his wife. He distinguishes between Shafi'i ruling (both forbidden) and Hanafi ruling (husband may have intercourse with either, because the divorce of one is not determined until clarification). He also comments on the goal being included in the thing goal is attached to, but denies that all goals require that. Finally, a branch on the obligation of exiting prayer (khuruj) by one's own action: some argue it is obligatory because entering another prayer depends on exiting the first. The author refutes this, citing Imam Abu Hanifa's silence, Imam al-Karkhi's view that it is not a devotional act, and the hadith of the Bedouin. He concludes that the relied-upon view is that exiting is not obligatory.

Key Terms
المقدمة (al-muqaddima): The means or prerequisite that is necessary for performing an obligatory act.
الوجوب بالعرض (al-wujub bil-‘arad): Accidental obligation - the means are not inherently obligatory but become so due to the obligation of the end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how many sins are incurred if one leaves both the obligatory act and its means?
A) One sin for the means, one for the act.
B) Only one sin, for the original obligation.
C) No sin because the means are not obligatory.
D) One sin for the means only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that means to an obligatory act are not independently obligatory; they are commanded accidentally, and only one sin is incurred for abandoning the original obligation.
