كاشف فكذا العقل عندنا كاشف عن الأوامر في بعض الأحكام فتدبر لنا وإلا يكن المعدوم مكلفاً لم يكن التكليف أزلياً لتوقفه على التعلق) ولو عقلياً، وإذا لم يكن المعدوم مكلفاً لم يتعلق به في الأزل ولا موجود فيه حتى يتعلق به (و) التالي باطل، بل هو أزلي، لأن كلامه تعالى أزلي لأن كلامه صفة له تعالى، فيكون قائماً به، فيستحيل حدوثه الامتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى وفيه ما فيه لأنه لا يتم على المعتزلة، فإنهم يقولون إنه ليس صفة قائمة به سبحانه بل الله تعالى متكلم بكلام قائم بجسم، قالوا: ليس هذا من قبيل الاتصاف بالمشتق من غير قيام المبدأ، فإن المتكلم مشتق من التكلم وهو خلق الكلام، والخلق صفته تعالى ولا يلزم منه كون الكلام ،صفة، ولأنه لا يتم على الكرامية القائلين بقيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى كذا في الحاشية»، ولا يخفى على المستيقظ بأن مخالفة الحمقاء لا تضر التمامية كيف ومسألة كون الكلام صفة له تعالى غير مخلوقة قطعية لا وجه للريب والارتياب فيه ألا ترى كيف قال الإمام أبو حنيفة : من قال بخلق القرآن فهو كافر، قالوا : وهو من الكفران لا من الكفر، وكيف صبر الإمام أحمد على أنحاء التعذيبات ولم يجر خلافها على اللسان فضلاً عن الإنكار، وانظر إلى ما قال الإمام الشيخ داود الطائي عند حلول هذه الحادثة، قام أحمد مقام الأنبياء ؛ وسئل الإمام الهمام جعفر بن محمد الصادق كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آبائه الكرام عن ،القرآن هل هو خالق أو مخلوق، فأجاب القرآن كلام الله غير مخلوق وبالجملة مسألة عدم خلق القرآن وكونه صفة قديمة عليه إجماعاً قطعياً لا يضر مجمع مخالفة الحمقاء فيه، وكذا لا يضر مخالفة الكرامية في امتناع قيام الحوادث به تعالى فتدبر، ثم بقي ها هنا سؤال هو : أن اللازم من الدليل كون الكلام النفسي هو الذي يكون تعلقه عقلياً، ويكون التكليف بعد وجودهم تنجيزاً، فلا يكون مدلول الكلام اللفظي الذي يتجه التكليف به تنجيزاً، وقد صرحوا بكونه مدلولاً له، كذا في «الحاشية»، ولا يذهب عليك أن معنى التعلق العقلي تعلق معلق بوجود المكلف بصفة التكليف، فكان في الأزل طلباً معلقاً به ، ، فإذا وجد المكلف بصفة التكليف فقد تنجز الطلب الذي كان معلقاً فإن التعليق بالأمر المحقق تنجيز، وهذا الطلب المحقق قالوا مدلول اللفظي، وأما إحقاق الحق فسنذكر نبذاً منه في الأصول فانتظر فإنه يظهر لك أن اللفظي له نوع من الاتحاد مع النفسي ولا ينافي ذلك الافتراق بحسب التعليق والتعلق فتدبر المعتزلة (قالوا لو كان التكليف قديماً (يلزم أمر ونهي من غير متعلق موجود) إذ قدم الأمر ولا مأمور (وذلك سفه وعبث وهذا لازم عليهم في الكلام اللفظي أيضاً، فإنه قد صح في الخبر الصحيح الثابت في صحيح مسلم وغيره عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كتب
Question: It is objected to us: The non-existent is obligated, contrary to the Mu'tazila. And since what immediately comes to mind is that he is actually obligated, which contradicts the lack of direct address, he explained it by saying: 'And what is meant is the mental relation, i.e., the relation conditioned upon their existence in the state of obligation, not the actual oral obligation.' It is said: The Ash'aris escape by this from what is objected to them if the non-existent is obligated, then the sleeping person is more deserving of being obligated. And it is objected to them: Is the non-existent obliged to something or not? If you wish, say: Is he commanded or not? On the first: Why is the sleeper not obliged? And how can you infer from permissibility of leaving? For the non-existent is a leaver without punishment despite the claim of obligation upon him. On the second: Then obligation is originated, and so is command, because they are one, so there is no eternal obligation. Also, relation is part of the reality of obligation, and since there is no relation in non-existence, there is no obligation. But we do not, for we allow the relation of command to the non-existent, and command without actual obligation and vice versa. As for command without obligation, it is in the non-existent; as for the opposite, the obligations prior to revelation, as narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa... [the translation continues]
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This is a complex usul dispute regarding whether the non-existent (المعدوم) can be subject to divine obligation (taklif). The Hanafi position distinguishes between mental relation (التعلق العقلي) and actual oral obligation (التنجيزي الشفاهي). The author explains that the Ash'aris also accept this distinction to avoid objections. The passage then delves into the eternity of divine speech (kalam) and the uncreatedness of the Quran, citing Imam Abu Hanifa's statement that whoever says the Quran is created is a disbeliever. The discussion connects the eternity of taklif to the eternity of God's attribute of speech. The author also addresses a question about the relationship between internal speech (الكلام النفسي) and verbal speech (الكلام اللفظي), affirming that they are united in some sense. The Mu'tazila objection that an eternal command with no object is futile is refuted by pointing out that this applies to verbal speech as well, and that a hadith in Sahih Muslim shows that the Prophet wrote (presumably a command) before the existence of the addressees.

Key Terms
التعلق العقلي (al-ta'alluq al-'aqli): Mental relation of the command to the obligated person, contingent upon future existence.
التنجيزي الشفاهي (al-tanjizi al-shifahi): Actual oral obligation that occurs when the addressed person exists and hears the command.
الكلام النفسي (al-kalam al-nafsi): Internal speech, the eternal attribute of God consisting of meaning without sound or letters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school presented in this passage, what is the status of the non-existent (المعدوم) in relation to divine command?
A) They are fully obligated from eternity.
B) They are not obligated in any sense.
C) They are obligated through mental relation only, conditional upon existence.
D) They are obligated through verbal speech directly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between mental relation and actual obligation preserves the eternity of God's command while grounding obligation in temporal human existence.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

6 min
Customary Possibility as the Condition for Obligation
Debate on whether obligation is valid when its condition for performance is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that obligation (taklif) is valid even when its condition for performance is absent, and evaluate the Mu'tazili counter-argument.

Core Idea
Obligation is valid if the act is customarily possible; absence of a condition does not make it essentially impossible.

This lesson explores a foundational usul al-fiqh debate between the Hanafis and the Mu'tazila. The question: can an obligation be validly imposed when the condition for its performance is absent? The Hanafis argue yes, based on the concept of customary possibility. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping how Hanafi usul shapes many fiqh rulings, especially in acts of worship under hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The issue is whether taklif is valid when its condition (shart) is absent. The Mu'tazila say no; Hanafis say yes.
This is fundamentally about what constitutes a valid subject of a divine command.
2
State the Mu'tazili position and its proof
The Mu'tazila argue that what lacks its condition is impossible, and impossibility precludes obligation. Their proof: existence of the conditioned without the condition is impossible, and possibility is a condition for obligation.
They equate impossibility due to absence of condition with essential impossibility.
3
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Hanafis hold that the condition for obligation is customary possibility, not essential possibility. They distinguish essential impossibility from impossibility due to another. They also cite ijma on expansive and lifetime obligations.
The key distinction: al-imkan al-adi vs. al-imkan al-dhati.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis respond that impossibility due to absence of condition does not negate the act's possibility in essence. They also argue from the case of ignorance: obligation can be valid even if the commander is ignorant of the condition's absence, and similarly, the subject's knowledge does not prevent obligation.
The rebuttal relies on the nature of possibility and the purpose (fā’ida) of obligation.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a person who cannot fulfill all conditions (e.g., sick person) remains obligated to perform the act to the best of his ability. This principle underlies rulings like prayer for the ill.
The difference manifests in how obligations are treated when conditions are temporarily absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحسب العادة (باطل للإجماع على تحقق الوجوب قبل التمكن بل على تحقق العلم بالوجوب والإجماع نقله القاضي وربما يمنع ولذا زاد قوله (بدليل وجوب الشروع بنية أداء الواجب إجماعاً، وهو فرع تحقق الوجوب بل علمه وربما يمنع الإجماع على وجوب النية بأداء الواجب، فإن الحنفية يجوزون أداء الصوم بإطلاق النية ونية النفل، فإن قلت لعل الإجماع كان قبل الحنفية والشافعية، قلت: لو كان قبل لعرفوه لأنهم أصحاب فحص عظيم وأما بعدهم فلا إجماع إلاّ بدخولهم. فالحق في الجواب أن في الواجب الموسع والعمري إجماعاً بلا ريب، وهذا القدر يكفينا في المطلوب، ثم ربما يورد إن أريد بالعلم الجزم فلا يتحقق قبل الوقوع لاحتمال الموت قبله وإن فإن الضرورة قاضية بأن الامتثال من أبي جهل ممكن بالإمكانين، وإن أردتم أنه غير ممكن بسبب عدم الشرط، فمسلم لكن لا ينافي الإمكان ذاتاً وعادة و(الشرط) للتكليف الإمكان العادي) الأخص من الذاتي (وهو لا ينافي الامتناع لغيره و قلنا (أيضاً: منقوض بجهل الآمر بعد الشرط في (الواقع لأن المعدوم الشرط في الواقع المجهول عند الآمر غير ممكن في الواقع (إذ لا دخل للعلم في الإمكان والامتناع فإنه أي العلم بالإمكان والامتناع (تابع للمعلوم) لا أنه سبب كيف والإمكان لا يكون من الغير، فإذا كان ممتنعاً فقد فات شرط التكليف، فلا التكليف به أيضاً، وفيه أن التكليف يصح بالمحال عند الجهل بالاستحالة، وقد مر الإشارة إليه، لكن لا يصح أن يكون المحال مكلفاً به في الواقع، إذ صحة الإيقاع من ضروريات كونه مطلوباً فتدبر (و) قالوا :(ثانياً: لو صح التكليف مع علم الأمر بانتفاء شرطه الصح مع علم المأمور) بانتفائه لأن عدم الحصول مشترك ولا يتخيل المانع إلا هو ولم يبق على زعمكم واللازم باطل اتفاقاً) إذ لا يصح مع علم المأمور (قلنا) أولاً: بطلان اللازم ممنوع، فإنه قد مر أن الإنسان لم يترك سدى وقلنا ثانياً تنزلاً لم يكن عدم صحة التكليف هناك لعدم الحصول بل لانتفاء الفائدة من التكليف وهو الابتلاء، ويرد عليه أنه يتحقق الابتلاء، فإن عزم على الفعل وبكى لانعدام شرطه استحق الثواب وإلا لا، هذا فالحق أن علم المأمور بعدم الوقوع غير مانع من التكليف كما قد مر من المصنف
According to custom (it is invalid because of consensus on the realization of obligation before ability, even on the realization of knowledge of obligation; the consensus is reported by al-Qadi and perhaps it is denied, hence he added his statement: (with the evidence of the obligation to commence with the intention of performing the obligatory act by consensus, and it is a branch of the realization of obligation, even of its knowledge; and perhaps the consensus on the obligation of intention for performing the obligatory act is denied, for the Hanafis permit performing the fast with absolute intention and the intention of supererogatory act. If you say: perhaps the consensus was before the Hanafis and Shafi'is, I say: if it were before, they would have known it because they are great investigators; but after them there is no consensus except by their inclusion. So the truth in the answer is that there is consensus without doubt regarding the expansive and lifetime obligatory acts, and this suffices us for what is sought. Then perhaps it is objected: if by knowledge is meant certainty, it is not realized before occurrence due to the possibility of death before it; if by knowledge is meant strong suspicion, we do not concede its impossibility, for suspicion of the existence of the condition is possible. And this is also insufficient because in most times weak suspicion is not available, let alone strong. The Mu'tazila (said first: what lacks its condition is not possible because the existence of the conditioned without the condition is impossible, and possibility is a condition of obligation) so its condition is absent, so obligation is absent. This reasoning also indicates that the intent in this issue is intellectual validity, not actual occurrence. (We said: if you mean that what lacks its condition is impossible in itself, then it is denied, for necessity judges that compliance by Abu Jahl is possible with both possibilities; if you mean that it is impossible due to the absence of the condition, it is accepted but does not negate possibility in essence and custom, and (the condition) for obligation is customary possibility) which is more specific than essential (and it does not negate impossibility due to another). And we said (also: it is refuted by the ignorance of the commander about the condition in reality, because what is conditionally non-existent in reality, unknown to the commander, is impossible in reality (since knowledge has no effect on possibility and impossibility, for knowledge of possibility and impossibility (follows the known) not that it is a cause; how can possibility come from something else? So if it is impossible, the condition of obligation is lost, so the obligation of it is also lost. But there is in it that obligation is valid for the impossible when one is ignorant of the impossibility, and reference has been made to it previously, but it is not valid that the impossible be obligated in reality, for the validity of performance is from the necessities of being required, so ponder. (And) they said: (secondly: if obligation were valid with the commander's knowledge of the absence of its condition, it would be valid with the subject's knowledge) of its absence because the non-occurrence is shared, and no obstacle is imagined except it, and on your claim, the consequent is false by agreement) since it is not valid with the subject's knowledge. (We said) first: the falsity of the consequent is denied, for it has passed that man is not left neglected; and we said secondarily by descent: the invalidity of obligation there was not due to non-occurrence but due to the lack of benefit from obligation, which is trial. And it is objected that trial is realized, for if he resolves to act and weeps due to the absence of its condition, he deserves reward, otherwise not. So the truth is that the subject's knowledge of non-occurrence does not prevent obligation, as the author has stated.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a disputation (usul dispute) between the Hanafis and the Mu'tazila regarding whether an obligation (taklif) can be valid when the condition for its performance is absent. The Hanafi position is that it is valid. The author begins by addressing an argument that relies on consensus (ijma) that obligation is realized before ability, and even before knowledge of ability. He deals with objections to the consensus claim and concludes that for expansive and lifetime obligations, there is no doubt. He then examines the Mu'tazili argument that what lacks its condition is impossible, and impossibility of the act precludes obligation. The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes between essential impossibility and impossibility due to absence of a condition; the latter does not negate the possibility of the act in itself and by custom. The condition for obligation is customary possibility (al-imkan al-adi), not essential possibility. The passage also discusses the case of ignorance of the condition, citing that obligation can be valid for the impossible if the impossibility is unknown. It further refutes the Mu'tazili contention that if obligation were valid with the commander's knowledge of the condition's absence, it would also be valid with the subject's knowledge; the Hanafi response is that the invalidity there is due to lack of benefit (trial), not due to non-occurrence itself. The central Hanafi principle is that the subject's knowledge of non-occurrence does not prevent obligation. This is a key distinction in usul al-fiqh between potential and actual conditions for obligation.

Key Terms
إمكان عادي (al-imkan al-adi): Customary possibility: the act is possible in itself and by external means without a miraculous intervention.
امتناع لغيره (al-imtina' li-ghayrihi): Impossibility due to an external factor, not inherent in the act itself.
تكليف (taklif): Divine obligation of a legally responsible person to perform an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the condition (shart) for obligation (taklif)?
A) Actual existence of all conditions for performance
B) Customary possibility of the act
C) Essential possibility of the act
D) The commander's knowledge that the act will occur

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the condition for valid obligation is customary possibility, not actual possibility; thus, absence of a condition does not automatically invalidate the obligation.

Validity of a Minor's Islam for Worldly Rulings
Debate on whether the Islam of a discerning minor is valid for worldly legal rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi position on the validity of a minor's Islam for worldly rulings and EXPLAIN the primary proof and the Hanafi response to the opposing objection.

Core Idea
A discerning minor's Islam is valid for both worldly and otherworldly rulings.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute: can a child's declaration of faith produce legal effects in this world, such as inheritance and guardianship? The Hanafi school affirms yes, while some opponents restrict the validity to otherworldly rewards. We will analyze the primary evidence—the case of Ali ibn Abi Talib—and the responses to objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The dispute is whether the Islam of a discerning minor is valid for worldly rulings (ahkam al-dunya).
Worldly rulings include inheritance, marriage, guardianship, etc.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
Hanafis hold that the Islam of a discerning minor is valid for all rulings. Their proof is the hadith of Ali accepting Islam at age seven and the Prophet's acceptance.
The acceptance by the Prophet implies comprehensive validity.
3
Analyze the opposing objection
Opponents argue the acceptance was only for otherworldly rulings, not worldly ones, because a child cannot bear worldly legal consequences.
They also claim the evidence depends on Abu Talib's disbelief.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The author argues that validity in some rulings implies validity in all, and general texts on inheritance and guardianship apply to every valid Muslim.
The inheritance story of Ali's brothers is cited to show worldly effects.
5
Evaluate the strength of the evidence
The author acknowledges difficulty: Ali's faith might be that of a mature minor, and the inheritance occurred after adulthood. He suggests the best view is that the legal impediment (hajr) is absent, so the Islam is valid.
This reflects a nuanced usul analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ووجوه آبائه الكرام أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورّث طالباً وعقيلاً أباهما، ولم يورث علياً وجعفراً، ولذا تركنا نصيباً في الشعب، كذا في موطأ الإمام مالك، ومن ها هنا بان أنه قبل في أحكام الدنيا، وفيه صحة إيمان غير المكلف وفيه الكلام، بل الأحرى ما يجيء أن الحجر من الشرع لم يوجد ولا يليق فيصح فيقطع الولايات بينه وبين الكافر لعموم النصوص كما قررنا (قال) الإمام فخر الإسلام بثبوت أصل وجوب الإيمان عليه (لا) ثبوت (وجوب الأداء) فإن التكليف موضوع عنه فإذا أسلم وقع فرضاً مسقطاً لما في الذمة (كصوم المسافر) فلا يتوجه الخطاب بإيجاب الأداء لتفريغ الذمة، لأنها فرغت سابقاً (فلا يجب تجديده بالغاً، ونفاه أي نفس الوجوب (شمس الأئمة لعدم حكمه وهو وجوب الأداء والشيء إنما يجب ويثبت في الذمة لأجل حكمه وفيه نظر لأنا لا نسلم أن حكمه ذلك) أي حكم نفس الوجوب وجوب الأداء بل ذلك حكم الخطاب، وإنما حكمه صحة الأداء عن الواجب) بحيث يمنع بعد الأداء عن توجه الخطاب، ثم إنه ليس لفخر الإسلام دليل على ثبوت نفس الوجوب، وأما عدم وجوب التجديد، فلعله لأجل حصول المصلحة لا لنفس الوجوب، وأيضاً لا فرق بين الإيمان وبين سائر العبادات فتأمل فيه
It is valid. The issue: The Islam of a discerning child is valid, evidenced by the validity of the Islam of the Commander of the Faithful (Ali), may God be pleased with him, at eight or ten years old, all being states of childhood, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, accepted it, for he had faith at the age of seven. It was objected that this does not prove the required point, for the dispute is only about the validity of his faith with respect to worldly rulings, and it has not been established yet. Indeed, the Prophet's acceptance of his faith, may God honor his face, with respect to otherworldly rulings is conceded, but with respect to worldly rulings it is denied. It would only be complete if it were established that he did not inherit from his father Abu Talib. Also, the evidence is dependent on Abu Talib's disbelief; if he were Muslim, then the acceptance of his faith following his father would not indicate acceptance in himself. The author answered the first objection by saying that the validity of faith in otherworldly rulings indicates its validity in all other rulings, and hence one judges the prayer of an infidel facing our qibla as Islam and accepts other rulings. It was replied that validity in otherworldly rulings, like the validity of his prayer and praying over him, does not entail validity in worldly rulings, and the opponent does not concede but differentiates, and the witness is not complete because an adult is capable of accepting rulings unlike a child. The answer is that his intent is that whenever the validity of Islam is established in some rulings, it is established in all apparently; moreover, the texts on severance of guardianship between an infidel and a Muslim, and nullification of inheritance and marriage, are general for everyone whose Islam is valid. So after the validation of the faith of the Commander of the Faithful, the distinction between worldly and otherworldly rulings is incorrect. This is my understanding. As for the second problem, its falsity is evident, for the hadiths of his disbelief are famous, and the verse was revealed concerning the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding his uncle Abu Talib: {You do not guide whom you love} [Qasas: 56] as in Sahih Muslim and Sunan al-Tirmidhi. And it is established in a sound report from Imam al-Baqir, may God honor his face and the faces of his noble forefathers, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, caused Talib and Aqil to inherit from their father, and did not cause Ali and Ja'far to inherit, and hence we left a portion in the mountain, as in the Muwatta of Imam Malik. From here it became clear that he accepted in worldly rulings. However, the death of Abu Talib occurred after the Commander of the Faithful reached adulthood, so it does not indicate validity during childhood. Then know that the inference from the validity of the Islam of the Commander of the Faithful is very problematic, for the saying of al-Bayhaqi will soon come that the attachment of obligatory rulings occurs after puberty after the Battle of the Trench, but before it the criterion was discernment, and the faith of the Commander of the Faithful was Meccan; indeed, he was the first to have faith according to some, though it is not correct among the experts except for primacy among children. So his faith is the faith of a legally responsible person, so its validity does not entail the validity of the faith of a non-legally responsible person, and there is discussion in it. Rather, what is more appropriate is what will come: that the impediment (hajr) from the law was not found and is not suitable, so it is valid, so it cuts off guardianship between him and the infidel due to the generality of the texts as we have determined. (Imam Fakhr al-Islam said) regarding the establishment of the original obligation of faith upon him, not the obligation of performance, for obligation is removed from him; so when he becomes Muslim, it occurs as an obligatory act that replaces what was in the liability (like the fast of a traveler), so the address of obligation of performance is not directed to him to clear the liability, because it was already cleared. So it is not necessary for him to renew it as an adult. And Shams al-A'imma denied the very obligation due to the absence of its ruling, which is the obligation of performance; a thing is only obligatory and established in the liability for the sake of its ruling. But there is consideration in it, for we do not concede that its ruling is that; rather, that is the ruling of the address, while its ruling is the validity of performance as obligation such that after performance it prevents the address from being directed. Then Fakhr al-Islam has no evidence for the establishment of the very obligation. As for the lack of necessity of renewal, perhaps it is due to the attainment of benefit, not for the sake of the obligation itself. Also, there is no difference between faith and other acts of worship, so ponder.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a disputation (usul dispute) concerning the validity of a minor's Islam for worldly legal rulings (ahkam al-dunya). The Hanafi position is that the Islam of a discerning child is valid both for otherworldly and worldly rulings. The primary evidence is the case of Ali ibn Abi Talib, who accepted Islam at age seven and the Prophet accepted it. Opponents object that acceptance was only for otherworldly rewards, not for worldly legal effects like inheritance and marriage. The author responds that validity in some rulings implies validity in all, and general texts on inheritance and guardianship apply to anyone whose Islam is valid. He also cites hadiths about Abu Talib's disbelief and inheritance practice to show that Ali's Islam had worldly effects. However, he later notes problematic aspects: that Ali's faith might be that of a legally responsible person since he was mature in judgment, and that the case may not prove validity for a younger child. The passage then discusses further points by Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma about whether a minor is obligated to have faith and whether his Islam fulfills that obligation. The commentator suggests that the obligation of faith is established in principle, but the obligation of performance is not required because the liability is cleared. The discussion highlights Hanafi usul principles regarding the capacity of children for legal acts and the distinction between the ruling of the act and the ruling of the command.

Key Terms
صحة الإسلام (sihhat al-islam): The legal validity of one's declaration of faith such that its effects apply in both worldly and otherworldly matters.
أحكام الدنيا (ahkam al-dunya): Worldly legal rulings such as inheritance, marriage, guardianship, etc.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to perform an act to discharge a liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used by the Hanafis to prove the validity of a minor's Islam for worldly rulings?
A) The Quranic verse about Abu Talib
B) The hadith about Ali ibn Abi Talib accepting Islam at age seven
C) The consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to the validity of a minor's prayer

Key Takeaway
A discerning minor's Islam is valid for all legal purposes, including worldly rulings, based on the Prophet's acceptance and the generality of legal texts.

The Obligation of Faith for a Minor: Wujub al-Asl vs. Wujub al-Ada'
Discussion on whether a minor is obligated to believe and whether his Islam fulfills that obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DISTINGUISH between the original obligation of faith (wujub al-asl) and the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') for a minor who becomes Muslim, and EXPLAIN the reasoning that a minor's Islam fulfills the obligation without requiring renewal at puberty.

Core Idea
A minor's Islam satisfies the original obligation of faith, so he does not need to renew it upon reaching adulthood.

This lesson delves into a subtle point: does a child who accepts Islam have an obligation to believe? And if he does believe as a child, does he need to reaffirm faith after puberty? The Hanafi scholars Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma discuss whether the obligation is established and whether the child's act discharges it. We will explore the distinction between the original obligation and the obligation to perform, and the implications for the child's legal responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key question
Does a minor have an original obligation of faith (wujub al-asl) and an obligation of performance (wujub al-ada')?
The distinction is crucial for knowing if the child's Islam counts.
2
Understand Fakhr al-Islam's position
He holds that the original obligation is established (thubut asl wujub al-iman), but the obligation of performance is not because the child is not addressed by the command.
The child's act of faith is valid and discharges the original obligation.
3
Analyze Shams al-A'imma's objection
He denies the very obligation because there is no ruling (hukm) attached to it; the ruling of obligation is the obligation of performance.
If there is no obligation to perform, how can there be an original obligation?
4
Examine the response
The author argues that the ruling of the original obligation is the validity of performance as an obligatory act (sihhat al-ada' 'an al-wajib), not the obligation to perform.
So the child's act, if performed, counts as fulfilling an obligation.
5
Conclude the implication
Since the child's faith fulfills the original obligation, he does not need to renew it at puberty, similar to a traveler's fast.
The analogy: a traveler is not obligated to fast, but if he does, it counts.

Source Text

يصح مسألة إسلام الصبي العاقل صحيح بدليل صحة إسلام أمير المؤمنين (علي) رضي الله عنه، أو ثمان أو عشر سنين والكل أحوال الصبا، وقبل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإنه كان آمن وهو ابن سبع واعترض عليه بأنه لا يدل على المطلوب، فإن النزاع إنما هو في صحة إيمانه في حق أحكام الدنيا، ولم يثبت بعد، فإن قبوله عليه السلام إيمانه كرم الله وجهه في حق أحكام الآخرة مسلم، وفي حق أحكام الدنيا ممنوع، وإنما يتم لو ثبت عدم توريثه أباه أبا طالب، وأيضاً: الدليل موقوف على كفر أبي طالب وأما لو كان مسلماً فقبول إيمانه كرم الله وجهه تبعاً لأبيه لا يدل على القبول في نفسه، وأجاب المصنف عن الأول بأن صحة الإيمان في حق أحكام الآخرة تدل على صحته في حق سائر الأحكام ومن ثمة يحكم بصلاة كافر إلى قبلتنا بالإسلام وقبول سائر الأحكام، وردَّ بأن الصحة في أحكام الآخرة كصحة صلاته والصلاة عليه لا تستلزم الصحة في حق أحكام الدنيا والخصم لا يسلم بل يفرق والشاهد غير تام، لأن البالغ قابل لقبول الأحكام دون الصبي والجواب أن مقصوده أنه متى ثبتت صحة الإسلام في بعض الأحكام ثبتت في الكل ظاهراً، كيف ونصوص انقطاع الولاية بين الكافر والمسلم وبطلان التوريث والإنكاح عامة في كل من صح إسلامه، فبعد ثبوت تصحيح إيمان أمير المؤمنين الفرق بين أحكام الدنيا والآخرة غير صحيح، هذا ما عندي، وأما الإشكال الثاني ففساده ظاهر، فإن أحاديث كفره شهيرة، وقد نزل في حق رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، في شأن عمه أبي طالب ﴿إِنَّكَ لَا تَهْدِي مَنْ أَحْبَبْتَ﴾ [القصص: ٥٦] كما في صحيح مسلم و سنن الترمذي، وقد ثبت في الخبر الصحيح عن الإمام الباقر كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آبائه الكرام أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورّث طالباً وعقيلاً أباهما، ولم يورث علياً وجعفراً، ولذا تركنا نصيباً في الشعب، كذا في موطأ الإمام مالك، ومن ها هنا بان أنه قبل في أحكام الدنيا، وفيه بعد غزوة الخندق، وأما قبلها فكان المناط التمييز، وكان إيمان أمير المؤمنين مكياً، بل إنه أول إيماناً عند البعض وإن كان غير صحيح عند الحذاق إلا الأولية في الصبيان، فإيمانه إيمان المكلف، فلا يلزم من صحته Commentary
This passage is a disputation (usul dispute) concerning the validity of a minor's Islam for worldly legal rulings (ahkam al-dunya). The Hanafi position is that the Islam of a discerning child is valid both for otherworldly and worldly rulings. The commentator suggests that the obligation of faith is established in principle, but the obligation of performance is not required because the liability is cleared. The discussion highlights Hanafi usul principles regarding the capacity of children for legal acts and the distinction between the ruling of the act and the ruling of the command.

Key Terms
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to perform an act to discharge a liability.
أصل الوجوب (asl al-wujub): The original or underlying obligation that may exist even if performance is not immediately required.
حكم الخطاب (hukm al-khitab): The ruling of the address itself, distinct from the ruling of the obligation.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

15 min
Validity of a Minor's Iman for Worldly Rulings
Usul dispute on the legal effect of a minor's iman, with textual evidence and internal Hanafi debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a minor's iman for worldly rulings and evaluate the opposing argument by applying the principle of generality of texts (umum al-nusus).

Core Idea
A minor's valid iman establishes all legal consequences, including inheritance and guardianship, because textual proofs are general and indivisible.

This passage addresses a key usul dispute: does a minor's acceptance of Islam carry the same legal weight as an adult's? The Hanafi school argues yes, citing the general texts on termination of guardianship and the prophetic example of Imam Ali. We will examine the objections, the Hanafi response, and the internal debate about the nature of obligation (wujub).

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed question
What exactly is being contested? The objector denies that a minor's valid iman carries any worldly legal effects, limiting it to the Hereafter. The Hanafi position affirms that it does.
The distinction between 'ahkam al-dunya' and 'ahkam al-akhira' is central.
2
Examine the opposing claim
The objector argues that the Prophet's acceptance of Ali's iman was only for the Hereafter, not for worldly matters, because Ali was a child and not a mukallaf.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The author refutes by citing general texts (nusus 'amma) on termination of guardianship between Muslim and disbeliever, and the specific hadith where the Prophet excluded Ali from inheriting from Abu Talib.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and Muwatta Imam Malik.
4
Consider the internal Hanafi debate
Fakhr al-Islam holds that wujub al-asl (origin of obligation) is established, but wujub al-ada' (obligation to perform) is not. Shams al-A'imma denies even wujub al-asl. The author supports Fakhr al-Islam.
This debate affects the minor's status regarding acts of worship.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a minor who converts is considered a Muslim for all legal purposes (inheritance, marriage, guardianship) but is not obligated to perform worship until puberty.
This distinguishes Hanafi from opposing views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثانية في الأحكام الدنيا، ولم يثبت بعد، فإن قبوله عليه السلام إيمانه كرم الله وجهه في حق أحكام الآخرة مسلم، وفي حق أحكام الدنيا ممنوع، وإنما يتم لو ثبت عدم توريثه أباه أبا طالب، وأيضاً : الدليل موقوف على كفر أبي طالب وأما لو كان مسلماً فقبول إيمانه كرم الله وجهه تبعاً لأبيه لا يدل على القبول في نفسه، وأجاب المصنف عن الأول بأن صحة الإيمان في حق أحكام الآخرة تدل على صحته في حق سائر الأحكام ومن ثمة يحكم بصلاة كافر إلى قبلتنا بالإسلام وقبول سائر الأحكام، وردَّ بأن الصحة في أحكام الآخرة كصحة صلاته والصلاة عليه لا تستلزم الصحة في حق أحكام الدنيا والخصم لا يسلم بل يفرق والشاهد غير تام، لأن البالغ قابل لقبول الأحكام دون الصبي والجواب أن مقصوده أنه متى ثبتت صحة الإسلام في بعض الأحكام ثبتت في الكل ظاهراً، كيف ونصوص انقطاع الولاية بين الكافر والمسلم وبطلان التوريث والإنكاح عامة في كل من صح إسلامه، فبعد ثبوت تصحيح إيمان أمير المؤمنين الفرق بين أحكام الدنيا والآخرة غير صحيح، هذا ما عندي، وأما الإشكال الثاني ففساده ظاهر، فإن أحاديث كفره شهيرة، وقد نزل في حق رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، في شأن عمه أبي طالب ﴿إِنَّكَ لَا تَهْدِى أحبت ﴾ [القصص: ٥٦] كما في صحيح مسلم» و «سنن الترمذي»، وقد ثبت في الخبر الصحيح عن الإمام الباقر كرم الله وجهه ووجوه آبائه الكرام أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورّث طالباً وعقيلاً أباهما، ولم يورث علياً وجعفراً، ولذا تركنا نصيباً في الشعب، كذا في «موطأ الإمام مالك»، ومن ها هنا بان أنه قبل في أحكام الدنيا، وفيه أن موت أبي طالب كان بعد بلوغ أمير المؤمنين، فلا يدل على التصحيح حال الصبا، ثم اعلم أن الاستدلال بصحة إسلام أمير المؤمنين مشكل جداً، فإنه سيجيء عن قريب قول البيهقي إن تعلق الأحكام التكليفية بعد البلوغ بعد غزوة الخندق، وأما قبلها فكان المناط التمييز، وكان إيمان أمير المؤمنين مكياً، بل إنه أول إيماناً عند البعض وإن كان غير صحيح عند الحذاق إلا الأولية في الصبيان، فإيمانه إيمان المكلف، فلا يلزم من صحته صحة إيمان غير المكلف وفيه الكلام، بل الأحرى ما يجيء أن الحجر من الشرع لم يوجد ولا يليق فيصح فيقطع الولايات بينه وبين الكافر لعموم النصوص كما قررنا (قال) الإمام فخر الإسلام بثبوت أصل وجوب الإيمان) عليه (لا) ثبوت (وجوب الأداء) فإن التكليف موضوع عنه فإذا أسلم وقع فرضاً مسقطاً لما في الذمة (كصوم المسافر) فلا يتوجه الخطاب بإيجاب الأداء لتفريغ الذمة، لأنها فرغت سابقاً (فلا يجب تجديده بالغاً، ونفاه أي نفس الوجوب (شمس الأئمة لعدم حکمه وهو وجوب الأداء والشيء إنما يجب ويثبت في الذمة لأجل حكمه وفيه نظر لأنا لا نسلم أن حكمه ذلك) أي حكم نفس الوجوب وجوب الأداء بل ذلك حكم الخطاب، وإنما حكمه صحة الأداء عن الواجب) بحيث يمنع بعد الأداء عن توجه الخطاب، ثم إنه ليس لفخر الإسلام دليل على ثبوت نفس الوجوب، وأما عدم وجوب التجديد، فلعله لأجل حصول المصلحة لا لنفس الوجوب، وأيضاً لا فرق بين الإيمان وبين سائر العبادات فتأمل فيه.
The second discussion concerns worldly rulings. It has not been established yet. Indeed, his acceptance—peace be upon him—of his faith (may Allah honor his face) regarding the rulings of the Hereafter is conceded, but regarding worldly rulings it is prohibited. It would only be complete if it were established that he did not inherit from his father Abu Talib. Also, the evidence depends on Abu Talib's disbelief, for if he were Muslim, then accepting his faith (may Allah honor his face) as a follower of his father does not indicate acceptance in himself. The author responded to the first point: that the validity of faith regarding the Hereafter indicates its validity regarding all other rulings, and hence we rule on the prayer of a disbeliever facing our qibla with Islam and acceptance of other rulings. It was refuted: that validity in Hereafter rulings, like the validity of his prayer and praying over him, does not entail validity in worldly rulings, and the opponent does not concede but distinguishes, and the evidence is incomplete because the adult is capable of accepting rulings unlike the minor. The answer: his intention is that once the validity of Islam is established in some rulings, it is established in all outwardly. How so? The texts on the termination of guardianship between a disbeliever and a Muslim and the invalidity of inheritance and marriage are general for everyone whose Islam is valid. So after establishing the validity of the Commander of the Faithful's faith, the distinction between worldly and Hereafter rulings is incorrect. This is what I have. As for the second problem, its corruption is clear, for the hadiths of his disbelief are famous, and it was revealed concerning the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, regarding his uncle Abu Talib: {Indeed, you do not guide whom you love} [al-Qasas: 56] as in Sahih Muslim and Sunan al-Tirmidhi. It is established in the authentic report from Imam al-Baqir (may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble ancestors) that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, made Talib and 'Aqil inherit their father, but did not make 'Ali and Ja'far inherit. Therefore, we left a share in the tribe. Likewise in the Muwatta of Imam Malik. From this it is clear that it was accepted in worldly rulings. There is that the death of Abu Talib was after the Commander of the Faithful reached puberty, so it does not indicate validity during childhood. Then know that inferring from the validity of Islam of the Commander of the Faithful is very problematic, for soon will come the statement of al-Bayhaqi that the attachment of obligatory rulings was after puberty after the Battle of the Trench, but before that the criterion was discernment, and the faith of the Commander of the Faithful was Meccan. Indeed, he was the first to believe according to some, though this is not correct among the experts except for precedence among children. So his faith is the faith of a responsible person, so the validity of his faith does not imply the validity of the faith of a non-responsible person. There is discussion in it. Rather, what is more appropriate is what will come: that the restriction from the law did not exist and is not fitting, so it is valid to terminate guardianship between him and the disbeliever due to the generality of the texts as we established. (He said) Imam Fakhr al-Islam: [It is established] the origin of the obligation of faith upon him (not) the obligation of performance. For obligation is removed from him. So if he embraces Islam, it occurs as an obligation that removes what is in the liability (like the fast of a traveler). So the address to oblige performance to free the liability is not directed because it was freed earlier. So it is not necessary to renew it upon reaching puberty. And Shams al-A'imma denied it (i.e., the very obligation) because its ruling (i.e., the obligation of performance) is absent. A thing is only obligatory and established in the liability for the sake of its ruling. There is a consideration in it: for we do not concede that its ruling (i.e., the ruling of the very obligation) is the obligation of performance. Rather, that is the ruling of the address. Its ruling is only the validity of performance for the obligatory, such that after performance it prevents the address from being directed. Then Fakhr al-Islam has no evidence for the establishment of the very obligation. As for the non-necessity of renewal, perhaps it is for the attainment of benefit, not for the very obligation. Also, there is no difference between faith and other acts of worship, so reflect on it.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul dispute) about whether the valid iman of a minor (specifically the iman of 'Ali radiAllahu anhu, who accepted Islam as a child) entails worldly legal rulings such as inheritance from a disbelieving father, or only validity for the afterlife. The author (the commentator) is responding to an objection. The opponent argues that the Prophet's acceptance of 'Ali's iman for the Hereafter does not imply acceptance for worldly rulings. The author counters by citing the general texts on termination of guardianship and inheritance for all whose Islam is valid, and by narrating the incident of Abu Talib's death where Talib and 'Aqil inherited but not 'Ali, proving that 'Ali's iman was accepted for worldly rulings. The passage then delves into the views of Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma on whether the obligation of iman itself is established on the minor, or only the obligation of performance. The author sides with Fakhr al-Islam that the origin of obligation is established but not the obligation of performance. The commentary explains the arguments and counterarguments, preserving the Hanafi position that a minor's iman is valid and creates the origin of obligation, but he is not commanded to perform until puberty.

Key Terms
حكم الدنيا (hukm al-dunya): Worldly legal rulings (e.g., inheritance, marriage, guardianship) that are affected by one's legal status as Muslim or disbeliever.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to perform an act (here, the act of professing faith) at the present time, as opposed to the abstract obligation (asl al-wujub) which remains in the liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what evidence is cited to prove that a minor's iman is effective for worldly rulings?
A) The Prophet's statement, 'Ali is from me'.
B) The hadith that the Prophet gave inheritance to Talib and 'Aqil but not to 'Ali and Ja'far.
C) The Quranic verse 'There is no compulsion in religion'.
D) The consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a minor's valid iman carries all worldly legal consequences, severed only by the lack of obligation to perform acts of worship until puberty.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Obligation of Minors for Faith: The Hanafi Position and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Explaining 'aql as condition for taklif and disputing obligation on children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on obligation of minors, apply the hadith of the lifted pen as a proof, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of faith on a discerning child.

Core Idea
A child is not obligated to perform religious duties before puberty, but a discerning child may be obligated for faith — an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut explores a key usul question: Is intellect (ʿaql) sufficient to impose legal responsibility (taklif) on a minor, or is puberty a necessary condition? The author presents the standard Hanafi view that no performance of duties is obligatory before puberty, citing the famous hadith that 'the pen is lifted from three.' He then engages with opposing views from Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, the Muʿtazila, and al-Qadi Abu Zayd, who argue that faith at least should be obligatory on a rational child. Through detailed analysis, the author refines the position and offers his own ruling: faith is obligatory on a child who has reached the level of sound reflection, though performance is not demanded before puberty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition for Taklif
Note how the author establishes ʿaql (intellect) as a condition for taklif, but clarifies that it is attached to a moderate degree—sanity at puberty—not every degree of intellect.
The author cites al-Bayhaqi to show that rulings were attached to puberty after the Hijra.
2
State the Standard Hanafi Position
The standard Hanafi view: No performance of any religious duty is obligatory on a child, even if rational. The primary proof is the hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three...'.
This hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, but used as a strong indicator.
3
Identify the Opposing Views
Three opposing positions: Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and his followers hold that faith is obligatory on a rational child; the Muʿtazila also obligate faith and punish for its omission; al-Qadi Abu Zayd obligates all divine rights but drops performance due to childhood.
These views rely on the sufficiency of intellect for obligation and hadiths about children of disbelievers in hell.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Proofs and Responses
The author provides two proofs: the hadith and Imam Muhammad's ruling on the murahiqa (girl nearing puberty) whose marriage does not annul if she fails to describe faith, indicating she was not commanded. He then responds to objections: presenting Islam after a spouse's conversion is for validity, not obligation; beating for prayer at ten is disciplinary.
The author critiques the second proof as merely a mujtahid's opinion, not clear evidence.
5
Examine the Author's Refinement
The author concludes that the child is obligated to faith if his discernment reaches the level of sound reflection (al-nazar al-sahih). He reconciles the murahiqa case by doubt about reaching that level. He also rebuts al-Qadi's view using an analogy with the traveler: if the obligation existed and was dropped, performing it would be performing an obligation, which is invalid by consensus.
Thus, the author affirms the original obligation of faith for the discerning child, but denies that performance is required before puberty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أم العقل شرط التكليف ثم له تفسيرات أظهرها أنه آلة الفهم وتبيين سائرها لا يخلو عن إطناب ممل إذ به الفهم لا بغيره وذلك متفاوت في الشدة والضعف ولا يناط التكليف بكل قدر من العقول، بل رحمة الله اقتضت أن يناط بقدر معتد به فأنيط بالبلوغ عاقلاً أي غير مجنون لأنه مظنة كمال العقل فالتكليف دائر عليه وجوداً وعدماً لا على كمال العقل ونقصانه، فإن من البالغين من ينقص عقله عن بعض المراهقين كالسفر أنيط به الحكم لكونه مظنة المشقة، والمشقة أمر غير مضبوط، فالحكم دائر عليه وجوداً وعدماً، وجدت المشقة لا قال البيهقي المحدث رحمه الله الأحكام الشرعية إنما تعلقت بالبلوغ بعد الهجرة وقبلها إلى عام الخندق كانت تتعلق بالتمييز (هـ) هذا تأييد لإناطة الأحكام بالبلوغ، وإذا ثبت إناطتها بالبلوغ فلا أداء يجب شيء على الصبي ولو عاقلاً خلافاً لأبي منصور وهذا الإمام الشيخ علم الهدى الماتريدي أعظم مشايخنا وأكبر مشايخ العراق، كذا في التقرير، كذا في الحاشية و خلافاً للمعتزلة في وجوب الإيمان أي وجوب أدائه فإنهم ذهبوا إلى عقابه بتركه و خلافاً للقاضي الإمام أبي زيد حيث قال بوجوب جميع حقوق الله تعالى من الإيمان وغيره عليه إلا أن الأداء سقط بعذر الصبا لقصور البدن ولعله إنما قال بالسقوط في غير الإيمان لنا أولاً قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : رفع القلم (أي الحساب والمؤاخذة) عن ثلاثة : عن النائم حتى يستيقظ، وعن الصبي حتى يحتلم وعن المجنون حتى يعقل وأصحاب الإمام علم الهدى يخصون الصبي العاقل في حق وجوب الإيمان بالعقل وبأحاديث دخول صبيان الكفرة في النار، فإن قلت: فلم يعرض الإسلام على الصبي بعد إسلام الزوجة وليس واجباً عليه، وكذا لم يؤمر بأداء الصلاة وهو ابن عشر سنين أجاب عن الأول بقوله : وعرض الإسلام عليه بعد إسلام زوجته لصحته لا لوجوبه فإن قلت لما كان الصبي غير مكلف لا يتناوله الخطاب بحرمة النكاح مع الكفر، فمن أين فساد النكاح حتى يحتاج إلى العرض بل لا بد له من دليل؟ قلت : قد بينا أن سببية الإيمان لانقطاع الولاية عن الكافر منصوصة في نصوص متضافرة، وهو يقتضي فساد النكاح وعدم ثبوت التوريث وغير ذلك، وأجاب عن الثاني بقوله : وضربه لعشر على الصلاة تأديباً أي ضربه لأجل التأديب لا لأجل التعذيب لاعتياد لا تكليفاً أي ضربه لأجل أن يعتادوها لا لأنهم مكلفون و لنا ثانياً عدم انفساخ نكاح المراهقة لعدم وصفه قال الإمام محمد : المراهقة إذا لم تصف الإيمان حين تسأل عنه لا ينفسخ نكاحها بخلاف البالغة فإنه ينفسخ نكاحها، فعلم أن المراهقة لم تكن مأمورة بالإيمان ولا يخفى على المستيقظ أن هذا لا يصلح دليلاً فإنه قول المجتهد لا قول صاحب الشرع ، ثم فيه تحريف الكلم عن مواضعه، فإن مشايخنا مثل الإمام فخر الإسلام وغيره استدلوا على أن مذهب أئمتنا ذلك، والدليل يدل عليه، ثم إنه قد ثبت أنه ينفسخ نكاح المراهقة بالكفر صريحاً، فعلم أنها نهيت عن الكفر صريحاً، وبعض شراح أصول الإمام فخر الإسلام صرح أيضاً بأن الكفر محرم على الصبي، مكلف بالكف، وعلى هذا أن ينبغي تعصى في صورة عدم الوصف أيضاً، وينفسخ النكاح

المقالة الثانية في الأحكام أيضاً، والذي يظهر لهذا العبد أن الصبي مكلف بالإيمان، لكن لا كل صبي، بل صبي بلغ تمييزه إلى حد النظر الصحيح، وهذا الحد غير مضبوط كما سبق فالمراهقة لا يفسد نكاحها عند عدم الوصف بالإيمان للشبهة في البلوغ إلى حد التمييز وبالشبهة لا يرتفع النكاح القائم بيقين. وأما حالها في الآخرة فموكول إلى الله، فإن بلغت في علمه حد التكليف يعذبها وإلاّ لا، وأما عند الوصف بالكفر فقد علم أنها صلحت للنظر لكن كابرت العقل حيث أتت بالكفر فعلم كونها مكلفة كافرة، فحكم بانفساخ النكاح ، فليس في هذا دليل على أن الصبي غير مكلف بالإيمان عند أئمتنا أصلاً فتدبر أقول : وفيه أنه لا يدل على نفي أصل الوجوب للإيمان عن العاقلة والجواب أنه لم يقصد الدلالة عليه بل على نفي وجوب الأداء فأما نفس الوجوب فإن كان فلا يضرنا ولنا على القاضي خاصة أنه لو كان كل من الحقوق الإلهية واجباً عليه، ثم سقط الوجوب دفعاً للحرج كما هو مذهبه لكان الصبي الآتي به مؤدياً للواجب لأنه صار مرخصاً في لزوم الأداء بعذر كالمسافر إذا صام، واللازم هو كونه مؤدياً للواجب باطل اتفاقاً فإن قيل : يجوز أن يكون رخصة إسقاط فلا يكون الآتي بها مؤدياً للواجب، قلت: إذا كان رخصة إسقاط فهي غير واجبة عليه بل وجوبه منسوخ ونحن لا ننكره، كما نقلنا البيهقي، وإنما النزاع في أن الوجوب ثابت عليه أم لا وأيضاً قال في الجواب وليس رخصة إسقاط لعدم الإثم بالاتفاق في الإتيان وفيها يأثم في الإتيان كصلاة المسافر إذا أتمها فتدبر.
Is intellect a condition for legal responsibility? Then it has interpretations, the most apparent being that it is the instrument of understanding, and explaining others is not free from tedious prolixity because understanding is by it, not by others, and it varies in intensity and weakness. Legal responsibility is not attached to every degree of intellects, but the mercy of God required it to be attached to a moderate degree, so it is attached to puberty with sanity, i.e., not insane, because it is the locus of perfection of intellect. Thus legal responsibility revolves around it in existence and non-existence, not around perfection or deficiency of intellect. Among adults there are those whose intellect is deficient compared to some adolescents, like travel, the ruling is attached to it because it is the locus of hardship, and hardship is not precisely defined, so the ruling revolves around it in existence and non-existence: hardship found or not. Al-Bayhaqi, the hadith scholar, may God have mercy on him, said: 'Legal rulings were attached to puberty after the Hijra, and before it until the year of the trench they were attached to discernment.' This supports the attachment of rulings to puberty. And when it is established that they are attached to puberty, then no performance is obligatory on the child, even if rational, contrary to Abu Mansur (this is Imam al-Maturidi, greatest of our shaykhs and greatest of the shaykhs of Iraq, as in al-Taqrir and al-Hashiya), and contrary to the Mu'tazila regarding the obligation of faith (i.e., its performance), for they maintain he is punished for leaving it, and contrary to al-Qadi (Imam Abu Zayd) who held that all rights of God, including faith and others, are obligatory on him except that performance is dropped due to childhood, due to bodily deficiency, and perhaps he meant dropping only for other than faith. Our proof first: his saying, peace be upon him: 'The pen is lifted (i.e., accountability and punishment) from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he recovers senses.' The followers of Imam 'Alam al-Huda specialize the rational child regarding the obligation of faith by intellect and by hadiths of the entrance of children of disbelievers into hellfire. If you say: Why then is Islam presented to the child after his wife's conversion, and it is not obligatory on him, and similarly he is not commanded to perform prayer when he is ten years old? He answered the first by saying: 'Presenting Islam to him after his wife's conversion is for its validity, not its obligation.' If you say: Since the child is not obligated, the address regarding the prohibition of marriage with disbelief does not apply to him, so whence the invalidity of marriage that he needs presentation? Rather, there must be a proof. I say: We have explained that the causality of faith for severing guardianship from the disbeliever is textually established in numerous texts, and it necessitates invalidity of marriage, non-probity of inheritance, etc. And he answered the second by saying: 'His beating at ten for prayer is disciplinary, i.e., beating for discipline, not for punishment, for habituation, not obligation, i.e., beating so they become accustomed, not because they are obligated.' Our second proof: the non-annulment of the marriage of a girl nearing puberty (murahiqa) due to her lack of description. Imam Muhammad said: If the murahiqa does not describe faith when asked about it, her marriage is not annulled, unlike the adult woman, for her marriage is annulled. So it is known that the murahiqa was not commanded to have faith. It is not hidden from the vigilant that this does not qualify as a proof, for it is the statement of a mujtahid, not the statement of the Lawgiver. Moreover, it involves distortion of words from their places. Our shaykhs, like Imam Fakhr al-Islam and others, argued that the madhhab of our imams is that, and proof indicates it. Moreover, it is established that the marriage of the murahiqa is annulled by explicit disbelief, so it is known that she is explicitly prohibited from disbelief. Some commentators of the principles of Imam Fakhr al-Islam also explicitly stated that disbelief is prohibited on the child, obligated to refrain. On this basis, it is appropriate that she be disobedient in the case of non-description as well, and the marriage is annulled. The second discourse on rulings also: What appears to this servant is that the child is obligated to faith, but not every child; rather, a child whose discernment has reached the level of sound reflection. This limit is not defined as previously. So the murahiqa's marriage is not corrupted at the lack of description of faith due to doubt about reaching the level of discernment, and by doubt the established marriage cannot be raised. As for her state in the afterlife, it is entrusted to God: if she had reached in His knowledge the level of obligation, He punishes her; otherwise not. As for when she describes disbelief, it is known that she is capable of reflection but opposed reason by uttering disbelief, so it is known she is obligated and disbelieving; thus the marriage is annulled. There is no proof in this that the child is not obligated to faith in our imams' view at all. So reflect. I say: It does not indicate the negation of the original obligation for the rational person. The answer: He did not intend to indicate that, but rather the negation of obligation of performance. As for the obligation itself, if it exists, it does not harm us. And our proof specifically against al-Qadi: If every divine right were obligatory on him, then the obligation dropped to avoid hardship as per his doctrine, then the child who performs it would be performing an obligatory act because he became licensed in the necessity of performance due to an excuse, like the traveler who fasts. The necessary conclusion that he is a performer of an obligatory act is invalid by agreement. If it is said: It could be a license of dropping, so the performer is not performing an obligatory act. I say: If it is a license of dropping, then it is not obligatory on him; rather its obligation is abrogated. We do not deny that, as we transmitted from al-Bayhaqi. The dispute is whether the obligation is established on him or not. Also he said in the answer: It is not a license of dropping because of the absence of sin by agreement in performing it, and if it were a license of dropping, he would sin by performing it, like the traveler's prayer if he completes it. So reflect.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute concerning the condition of intellect for legal responsibility (taklif) and the extent of obligation on minors. The author, commenting on a matn, first establishes that intellect is a condition for taklif, defined as the instrument of understanding, and that taklif is attached to a moderate degree of intellect, namely the sanity (ʿaql) attained at puberty. He cites al-Bayhaqi to show that rulings were attached to puberty after the Hijra, earlier to discernment. From this, he asserts that no performance of duties is obligatory on a child, even if rational, contrary to Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, the Muʿtazila, and al-Qadi Abu Zayd. The Muʿtazila held a child obligated for faith; al-Qadi held all divine rights obligatory but performance dropped due to physical deficiency. The author provides two proofs for the Hanafi position: first, the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three'—the sleeper, the child until puberty, the insane until sanity—this indicates no accountability. The followers of al-Maturidi restrict this concerning faith, arguing intellect suffices for obligation of faith, citing hadiths about children of disbelievers. The author responds to objections: presenting Islam after a spouse's conversion is for validity, not obligation; beating for prayer at ten is disciplinary, not obligatory. Second, Imam Muhammad's ruling that a murahiqa's marriage does not annul if she fails to describe faith, implying she was not commanded to have faith. However, the author later critiques this reasoning as merely a mujtahid's opinion. He then transitions to the 'second discourse on rulings' and presents his own view: the child is obligated to faith, but not all children—only those whose discernment reaches sound reflection. He reconciles the murahiqa case based on doubt about reaching that level. He concludes by arguing against al-Qadi that if all divine rights were obligatory and then dropped, performing them would still be performing an obligation, which is invalid; thus the obligation is not originally established. The discussion shows the internal Hanafi debate and the author's inclination that faith is indeed obligatory on a discerning child, though performance is not required before puberty.

Key Terms
العقل (al-ʿaql): The instrument of understanding, the faculty by which comprehension occurs; its degrees vary.
التكليف (al-taklif): The imposition of a duty that obligates performance, attached to a person of sound mind and puberty.
الصبي (al-sabi): A minor who has not reached puberty; some actions from him are valid but not obligatory.
المراهقة (al-murahiqa): A girl nearing puberty, typically close to the age of majority but not yet reached.
النظر الصحيح (al-nazar al-sahih): Sound reflection; the level of intellectual discernment that enables proper understanding and reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the author gives for his view that a discerning child is obligated to have faith (iman)?
A) The hadith of the lifted pen explicitly obligates faith.
B) The child's capacity for sound reflection (al-nazar al-sahih) makes faith obligatory, while the hadith only lifts accountability for performance.
C) Imam Muhammad's ruling on the murahiqa proves that faith is not obligatory.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school primarily holds that no performance of duties is obligatory before puberty, but a strong intra-madhhab argument exists that the obligation of faith (iman) applies to a discerning child who has reached the level of sound reflection.

Minor's Transaction with Gross Loss: The Binding Force of Guardian's Permission
Ruling on minor's transactions with guardian's permission in cases of gross loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that guardian's permission compensates the minor's deficiency and evaluate the Sahibayn's objection using the concept of 'al-idhn li-daf' al-darar'.

Core Idea
Permission does not guarantee correct judgment; probability of harm suffices for valid cause.

This lesson examines the sixth type of minor's transaction: those that oscillate between benefit and harm, such as sale. The key issue is whether a guardian's permission validates a transaction with gross loss (ghubn fahish). The Hanafi school splits: Abu Hanifa grants validity with strangers, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) invalidate it entirely. The author favors the Sahibayn's view as 'azhar' (more apparent). We will dissect the legal reasoning (talil) behind this dispute, focusing on the nature of permission and the role of probability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of transaction
The passage deals with contracts that have both potential benefit and harm (e.g., sale, lease). The minor lacks the capacity to assess long-term consequences, so a guardian's judgment is needed.
2
Determine the effect of guardian's permission according to Abu Hanifa
Permission compensates the minor's deficiency, making him like an adult in terms of transaction effectiveness. Therefore, with strangers, the contract is valid even with gross loss (by consensus of narrations). With the guardian, there are two narrations due to potential suspicion.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's objection
They argue that permission is only legally recognized to prevent harm. If the transaction incurs gross loss, the permission was misplaced, so the transaction is invalid.
4
Examine the Hanafi counter-response
The defender argues that permission is based on probability of no harm; the failure of that probability does not negate the cause. Analogy: a king's travel during hardship still grants concessions even if the king is comfortable.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The author declares the Sahibayn's view as more apparent. Understand why: because the very purpose of permission is to avoid harm, and gross loss contradicts that purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و(السادس) وهو الدائر بين الضرر والنفع كالبيع والإجارة وغيرهما من المعاوضات، ففيها نفع لاحتمالها الاسترباح مشوب باحتمال ضرر لاحتمال خسارة المال أو البدن والصبي قاصر عن معرفة العواقب، فلم تفوض إليه هذه لعقود مرحمة له لئلا يقع في ضرر، بل أولى عليه من هو أشفق به فبانضمام رأي هذا الولي يندفع ذلك الاحتمال من الضرر فيملك هذه العقود معه ثم عند الإمام أبي حنيفة لما انجبر القصور الذي كان في الصبي من تصرفاته بالإذن الصادر من الولي كان كالبالغ في نفاذ التصرفات فيملك العقود بغبن فاحش مع الأجانب باتفاق الروايات كالبالغ ومع الولي في رواية وفي أخرى لا يملك، لأن الولي حينئذ متهم في الإذن لجواز أن إذنه كان خداعاً منه لأخذ ماله ولا كذلك في أجنبي وعندهما لا يجوز العقود مع الغبن الفاحش وقولهما أظهر لأن الإذن إنما اعتبر شرعاً ليأمن عن الضرر، فلما عقد الغبن علم أن إذنه لم يقع في محله والعذر له أن الإذن مع مظنة عدم الضرر وتخلف الحكمة المظنة لا يوجب عدم العلة كسفر الملك المرفه مع[؟] عن الحكمة يثبت الترخص فتدبر، والله أعلم بأحكامه
And the sixth (type) is that which oscillates between harm and benefit, like sale, lease, and other commutative contracts. For there is benefit in them due to potential profit mixed with potential harm due to possible loss of wealth or person, and the minor is incapable of understanding consequences. So these contracts are not delegated to him as a mercy lest he fall into harm. Rather, it is more appropriate that someone more compassionate over him be placed over him, so by joining the opinion of this guardian, that potential harm is repelled. So he possesses these contracts with him. Then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, since the deficiency that was in the minor's actions is compensated by the permission issued by the guardian, he becomes like an adult in the effectiveness of his transactions. So he possesses the contracts with gross loss with strangers by consensus of narrations, like an adult; and with the guardian, in one narration he possesses, and in another he does not possess, because the guardian is then suspected in the permission, as it is possible that his permission was a deception to take his money, and that is not the case with a stranger. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contracts with gross loss are not valid. And their view is more apparent, because permission is only considered legally to ensure safety from harm. So when he made a contract with loss, it is known that his permission was not in its place. And his excuse is that permission is with the probability of no harm, and the failure of the probable wisdom does not necessitate the negation of the cause, like the travel of a comfortable king, even if wisdom is absent, the concession is established. So reflect. And Allah knows best His rulings.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth type of transactions that a minor may undertake with a guardian's permission. The author begins by characterizing this type as one that oscillates between potential benefit and harm, such as sale or lease. Because the minor cannot discern long-term consequences, such contracts are entrusted to a guardian. The guardian's judgment compensates the minor's deficiency. The core legal issue is whether a transaction with gross loss (ghubn fahish) is valid when the guardian has permitted it. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is valid with strangers by consensus of the narrations, and with the guardian there are two narrations. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that such contracts are invalid because permission was intended to prevent harm, and gross loss indicates the permission was misplaced. The author sides with the Sahibayn, stating that their view is more apparent (azhar). However, he provides a counterargument: permission is given based on a probability of no harm, and the failure of that probability does not negate the underlying cause, akin to a king's travel where the wisdom of concession may be absent yet the concession still applies. The passage ends with a reflection and a statement that Allah knows best.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghubn al-fāḥish): Gross loss in value exceeding normal market tolerance
الولي (al-walī): Guardian of the minor, such as father or judge
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission given by the guardian for the minor to transact

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, the author states 'wa qawluhuma azhar' (their view is more apparent). Who does 'huma' refer to?
A) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
B) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
C) The two narrations from Abu Hanifa
D) The strangers and the guardian

Key Takeaway
Guardian permission does not automatically validate a minor's transaction with gross loss; the Sahibayn's position that it is invalid reflects the purpose of permission—to prevent harm.

Accountability for Error Among Hanafis and Mu'tazila
Hanafi usul argument on error as jinaayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that error constitutes a jinaayah due to negligence and distinguish the Hanafi and Mu'tazili positions on liability for accidental harm.

Core Idea
Error is a jinaayah because it stems from voluntary negligence; accountability is possible but limited by shubhah.

This passage presents a key usul dispute between the Hanafis and the Mu'tazila on whether an act committed by mistake can be the basis of legal accountability. The Hanafis argue that error is not merely an innocent slip; it involves a prior failure to exercise due caution, which is a voluntary omission and thus an offense (jinaayah). However, due to the element of doubt (shubhah) regarding intent, the harshest punishments are lifted, but civil liability remains. The dispute has practical consequences in areas such as accidental property damage and homicide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
What is the dispute about? The rational permissibility of accountability for error (khaṭa').
2
Extract the Mu'tazili argument
Accountability requires intent (qasd); error lacks intent so no jinaayah.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof from the Quran
The believers' prayer 'Rabbanā lā tu'ākhidhnā in nasīnā aw akhta'nā' implies accountability is possible; otherwise the request would be for an impossibility.
Qur'an 2:285-286
4
Understand the Hanafi concept of jinaayah in error
Error arises from lack of precaution (tathabbut), which is a voluntary omission and therefore a jinaayah. Thus the error itself becomes a jinaayah.
5
Note the refinement of the Hanafi position
Due to shubhah (doubt of intent), hadd and qisas are dropped, but civil liability (damān) and expiation (kaffārah) remain.
Distinction between penal and compensatory liability

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة المؤاخذة بالخطأ جائزة عقلاً) أي العقل لا يأبى عن تجويز المؤاخذة على ارتكاب السيئة خطأ (خلافاً للمعتزلة لنا أنه تعالى مدح السائلين عدم المؤاخذة بالخطأ قال الله تعالى : وَقَالُوا سَمِعْنَا وَأَطَعْنَا غُفرانك ربنا وإليك المصير لا يكلف اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَهَا مَا كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَيْهَا مَا اكْتَسَبَتْ رَبَّنَا لَا تُؤَاخِذْنَا إِن نَّسِينَا أَوْ أَخْطَأْنَا ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٨٥ - ٢٨٦] ولو لم تصح المؤاخذة عقلاً لما مدحوا بهذا السؤال لأنه حينئذ سؤال بما يستحيل (والسؤال بما يستحيل باطل) المعتزلة (قالوا : (المؤاخذة إنما تكون بالجناية) وهي (بالقصد) ولا قصد في الخطأ فلا جناية، فلا مؤاخذة فيه (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه لا جناية فيه بل فيه جناية (بعدم التثبت والاحتياط الواجبين والخطأ لما كان مسبباً عن عدم التثبت الذي هو الجناية صار هو أيضاً جناية، فتجوز المؤاخذة به أيضاً، ولسنا نقول : إن المؤاخذة بعدم التثبت فقط، بل بفعل الخطأ، حتى يرد أن النزاع حينئذ لفظي، بل المؤاخذة به لكن لكونه مسبباً عن فعل اختياري فتدبر، ثم الخطأ وإن كان جناية كما بينا إلا أن فيه شبهة العدم أي شبهة عدم الجناية، ولذا لا يؤاخذ به في الإثم سمعاً، كما قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: (إن الله تجاوز عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان وما أكرهوا عليه» (فلا يؤاخذ بحد ولا قصاص لأنهما يسقطان بالشبهات دون ضمان (المتلفات) خطأ من الأموال فإنه يؤاخذ به جبراً للمتلف لا لكونه جناية، ألا ترى أنه يجب على الصغير، ولما كان نوع جناية والقتل من أعظم الكبائر لم يهدر الخطأ فيه بل وجبت الكفارة وأما الدية فجزاء المحل
Issue: Accountability for error is permissible rationally, i.e., reason does not reject the possibility of accountability for committing an evil act by mistake, contrary to the Mu'tazila. Our proof: Allah Most High praised those who ask not to be held accountable for error when He said: 'And they say: We hear and we obey. (Grant us) Your forgiveness, our Lord, and to You is the return. Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity. For it is what it has earned, and against it is what it has acquired. Our Lord, do not hold us accountable if we forget or err.' (Al-Baqarah 2:285-286). If accountability were not rationally possible, they would not be praised for this request, because then it would be a request for what is impossible, and a request for what is impossible is invalid. The Mu'tazila said: Accountability is only for an offense, and that is by intent. There is no intent in error, so there is no offense, hence no accountability. We say: We do not accept that there is no offense in it; rather, there is an offense in it due to lack of due caution and precaution. Since error is caused by lack of caution, which is the offense, it also becomes an offense. Thus, accountability for it is also permissible. We do not say that accountability is only for lack of caution, but for the act of error itself, so that the objection that the dispute then becomes verbal is refuted. Rather, accountability is for it but due to its being caused by a voluntary act, so reflect. Then, although error is an offense as we explained, it has an element of doubt (shubhah) regarding the absence of offense. Therefore, one is not held accountable for it in terms of sin in the revealed law, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah has forgiven my ummah for error, forgetfulness, and what they are coerced into.' So one is not held accountable with a prescribed punishment or retaliation, because these are dropped due to doubts. However, compensation for property destroyed by mistake is held accountable, to make good the loss, not because it is an offense. Do you not see that it is obligatory on a minor? And since killing is a type of major offense, error in it is not disregarded; rather, expiation is obligatory, and as for the blood money, it is compensation for the life.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents a full inter-madhhab dispute on the legal accountability for actions performed by mistake. The Hanafi position is that accountability for error is rationally possible, and they prove it from the Quranic verse where believers pray for forgiveness for error; this implies that accountability is not impossible. The Mu'tazila counter that accountability requires intent, which is absent in error. The Hanafi response goes deeper: error itself involves a prior failure to take precaution (tathabbut and ihtiyat), which is a voluntary omission and therefore a jinaayah (offense). Thus, the erroneous act becomes an extension of that negligence. However, due to the shubhah (doubt) of intent, the harsh punishments of hadd and qisas are waived, but civil liability (damān) remains, as does expiation for killing. The hadith of forgiveness confirms the dropping of sin, not of worldly rights. This nuanced position distinguishes between criminal punishment and compensatory liability.

Key Terms
الخطأ (al-khaṭa'): An act done unintentionally or mistakenly, as opposed to intentionally.
الجناية (al-jināyah): An offense or harmful act that can be subject to punishment or liability.
التثبت (al-tathabbut): Caution and thoroughness in avoiding error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, why is a person who accidentally destroys someone's property still liable for compensation despite the hadith of forgiveness?
A) Because the hadith is not authentic.
B) Because compensation is not a punishment but a reparation of loss.
C) Because accident is not true error.
D) Because the victim's right takes precedence over forgiveness.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that accidental harm involves negligence, creating liability for compensation, though sin and penal punishment are forgiven.
